```lean
-- ‖EuclideanSpace.single i r‖ = ‖r‖
```

The vector `(EuclideanSpace.equiv (Fin n) ℝ).symm (fun i => if i = ⟨m, h⟩ then ε / 2 else 0)` is exactly `EuclideanSpace.single ⟨m, h⟩ (ε / 2)`, so:

```lean

      (fun i => if i = ⟨m, h⟩ then ε / 2 else 0) =
      EuclideanSpace.single ⟨m, h⟩ (ε / 2) := by
    simp [EuclideanSpace.single, EuclideanSpace.equiv]

      Real.norm_of_nonneg (by linarith)]
```

  let incl : F → E := fun x => coordE.symm (toEuclideanE (coordF_padded x))

vecCons h t prepends an entry h to a vector t.

The inverse functions are vecHead and vecTail. The notation ![a, b, ...] expands to vecCons a (vecCons b ...).

Response:
`Matrix.vecCons` is for building vectors element by element, which is not quite the right tool here. The right Mathlib machinery for zero-padding is already built into the linear map infrastructure. Here are the better alternatives.

---

## The Core Operation

What `pad` does is extend a vector `Fin m → ℝ` to `Fin n → ℝ` by zero-padding. Mathlib has this as `Fin.cons` style operations or more directly as a linear map:

```lean
#check LinearMap.funLeft
#check Finsupp.liftNC  
#check EuclideanSpace.single
```

But the most direct Mathlib replacement is:

---

## Option 1 — Use `LinearMap.funLeft` for the Projection Direction

As established earlier, `LinearMap.funLeft` goes the wrong way. However the **adjoint** direction can be expressed using `Finsupp` or directly as:

```lean
-- The inclusion as a continuous linear map directly
let incl : F →L[ℝ] E :=
  (basisE.repr.symm.toContinuousLinearEquiv.toContinuousLinearMap).comp
  ((EuclideanSpace.equiv (Fin n) ℝ).symm.toContinuousLinearMap.comp
  { toFun := fun v i => if hi : i.val < m then 
      (EuclideanSpace.equiv (Fin m) ℝ (basisF.repr v)) ⟨i.val, hi⟩ else 0
    map_add' := by intro x y; ext i; split_ifs <;> simp [map_add]
    map_smul' := by intro r x; ext i; split_ifs <;> simp [map_smul] })
```

---

## Option 2 — Use `OrthonormalBasis.repr` More Directly

The cleanest restructuring collapses `coordE`, `coordF`, `toEuclideanE` into direct use of the basis:

```lean
-- Before (many let statements)
let basisE := stdOrthonormalBasis ℝ E
let basisF := stdOrthonormalBasis ℝ F
let coordE := basisE.repr
let coordF := basisF.repr
let pad : (Fin m → ℝ) → (Fin n → ℝ) := 
  fun v i => if hi : i.val < m then v ⟨i.val, hi⟩ else 0
let coordF_padded : F → (Fin n → ℝ) := fun x => pad (coordF x)
let toEuclideanE : (Fin n → ℝ) → EuclideanSpace ℝ (Fin n) :=
  (EuclideanSpace.equiv (Fin n) ℝ).symm
let incl : F → E := fun x => coordE.symm (toEuclideanE (coordF_padded x))

-- After (collapsed)
let basisE := stdOrthonormalBasis ℝ E
let basisF := stdOrthonormalBasis ℝ F
let incl : F → E := fun x => basisE.repr.symm
  (EuclideanSpace.single ⟨·, ·⟩ -- not quite right
  )
```

---

## Option 3 — Use `EuclideanSpace.single` and `Finset.sum`

The padded vector is a sum of single basis contributions:

```lean
let incl : F → E := fun x =>
  ∑ i : Fin m, (basisF.repr x i).re • basisE i
```

Wait — since we are over `ℝ` not `ℂ`, `.re` is not needed:

```lean
let incl : F → E := fun x =>
  ∑ i : Fin m, (EuclideanSpace.equiv (Fin m) ℝ (basisF.repr x) i) • 
    (basisE.toBasis i)
```

This expresses `incl` directly as a linear combination of the first `m` basis vectors of `E`, which is mathematically the clearest statement of what the inclusion does.

---

## Option 4 — Most Compact Using `OrthonormalBasis`

```lean
let incl : F →L[ℝ] E :=
  ∑ i : Fin m, (basisF.toBasis.coord i).toContinuousLinearMap.smulRight 
    (basisE.toBasis i)
```

This builds the inclusion as a sum of rank-one operators, each taking the `i`-th coordinate of the input and placing it along the `i`-th basis vector of `E`.

---

## Recommendation

**Option 3** with the sum is the most mathematically transparent and uses the most Mathlib machinery:

```lean
let basisE := stdOrthonormalBasis ℝ E
let basisF := stdOrthonormalBasis ℝ F
let incl : F → E := fun x =>
  ∑ i : Fin m, (EuclideanSpace.equiv (Fin m) ℝ (basisF.repr x) i) •
    (basisE.toBasis i)
```

This eliminates `coordE`, `coordF`, `pad`, `coordF_padded`, and `toEuclideanE` entirely — five `let` statements replaced by one. Continuity and injectivity proofs would also likely become cleaner since `∑` and `•` are well-supported by `fun_prop` and `simp`.

Would you like to try building the injectivity and continuity proofs around this formulation?

[03/31/2026 20:12:33 +00:00] User:
Application type mismatch: The argument
  i
has type
  Fin m
but is expected to have type
  Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)

it fails to recognise i as being of Fin n, though it naturally should be, due to m < n

Response:
The issue is that `i : Fin m` but `basisE.toBasis` expects `Fin n`. We need to explicitly cast `i` using `Fin.castLE`:

---

## Fix

```lean
let incl : F → E := fun x =>
  ∑ i : Fin m, (EuclideanSpace.equiv (Fin m) ℝ (basisF.repr x) i) •
    (basisE.toBasis (Fin.castLE (Nat.le_of_lt this) i))
```

`Fin.castLE (Nat.le_of_lt this) i` casts `i : Fin m` to `Fin n` using the proof `this : m < n`, via `Nat.le_of_lt this : m ≤ n`.

---

## Why This Is Needed

`m` and `n` are definitionally:
```
m := Module.finrank ℝ F
n := Module.finrank ℝ E
```

Even though `m < n` is known, Lean does not automatically coerce `Fin m` to `Fin n`. The cast must be explicit.

---

## Cleaner Version — Name the Cast

To avoid repeating the cast, name it:

```lean
let castToN : Fin m → Fin n := Fin.castLE (Nat.le_of_lt this)
let incl : F → E := fun x =>
  ∑ i : Fin m, (EuclideanSpace.equiv (Fin m) ℝ (basisF.repr x) i) •
    (basisE.toBasis (castToN i))
```

This makes the structure cleaner and the cast reusable in the injectivity and continuity proofs.

[03/31/2026 20:16:36 +00:00] User:
have hincl_inj : Function.Injective incl := by sorry
is there any automation that might do this simply?

Response:
Yes. Since `incl` is built from a sum of basis vectors, it is actually a linear map, and Lean may be able to handle injectivity automatically. Try these in order:

---

## Option 1 — `fun_prop`

```lean
have hincl_inj : Function.Injective incl := by
  unfold_let incl
  fun_prop
```

---

## Option 2 — Show It Is a Linear Map First Then Use Linearity

```lean
have hincl_linear : LinearMap.ker (by exact -- the linear map version of incl
  ) = ⊥ := by
  simp
```

---

## Option 3 — Use `Finset.sum` Injectivity via Basis

Since the images `basisE.toBasis (castToN i)` are linearly independent (they are distinct basis vectors), the map is injective:

```lean
have hincl_inj : Function.Injective incl := by
  intro x y hxy
  unfold_let incl at hxy
  have := Finset.sum_left_injective -- likely does not exist
  sorry
```

---

## Option 4 — Extract Coordinates

The most reliable manual approach given the sum formulation:

```lean
have hincl_inj : Function.Injective incl := by
  intro x y hxy
  unfold_let incl at hxy
  apply basisF.repr.injective
  ext i
  have hli : LinearIndependent ℝ (fun j : Fin m => basisE.toBasis (castToN j)) :=
    basisE.toBasis.linearIndependent.comp castToN (Fin.castLE_injective _)
  have := hli.eq_of_sum_eq_sum hxy
  simpa using congr_fun this i
```

---

## Honest Assessment

The sum formulation makes injectivity **harder** to prove than the original `pad` formulation, where the proof was straightforward coordinate extraction. This is a case where the more abstract formulation is less convenient for proofs.

---

## Recommendation

Go back to checking whether the original `pad`-based `incl` with the explicit `coordE`/`coordF` machinery gives a cleaner injectivity proof, and only switch to the sum formulation if continuity becomes significantly easier. The two formulations have different tradeoffs:

| Formulation | Continuity | Injectivity |
|---|---|---|
| `pad` + `coordE`/`coordF` | Needs manual `by_cases` | Straightforward coordinate extraction |
| `∑ i, coord • basis` | Likely `fun_prop` | Needs linear independence argument |

```lean
    {E F : Type*}
    [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E] [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] [BrouwerFixedPoint E]
    [NormedAddCommGroup F] [InnerProductSpace ℝ F] [FiniteDimensional ℝ F] [BrouwerFixedPoint F]
    (h : Nonempty (E ≃ₜ F)) :
    Module.finrank ℝ E = Module.finrank ℝ F := by
  let φ := h.some
  -- Forward direction: E → F
  let f : E → F := φ
  have hf_cont : Continuous f := φ.continuous
  have hf_inj : Function.Injective f := φ.injective
  -- Backward direction: F → E
  let g : F → E := φ.symm
  have hg_cont : Continuous g := φ.symm.continuous
  have hg_inj : Function.Injective g := φ.symm.injective
  -- Apply invariance of dimension both ways
  have hle : Module.finrank ℝ E ≤ Module.finrank ℝ F :=
    invariance_of_dimension_of_injective f hf_cont hf_inj
  have hge : Module.finrank ℝ F ≤ Module.finrank ℝ E :=
    invariance_of_dimension_of_injective g hg_cont hg_inj
  exact Nat.le_antisymm hle hge
```

---

## Why This Works

- `h.some` extracts the homeomorphism from the `Nonempty` wrapper
- `.continuous` and `.injective` are fields of `Homeomorph`
- `.symm` gives the inverse homeomorphism, which is also continuous and injective
- `invariance_of_dimension_of_injective` applied in both directions gives `≤` both ways
- `Nat.le_antisymm` combines them into `=`

omit [BrouwerFixedPoint E] in
theorem differentiable_approx_of_continuous {δ : ℝ} (hδ : 0 < δ) {U : Set E} (hUcompact : IsCompact U) (G : E → E)
    (hG_cont : Continuous G) [Nontrivial E] : ∃ (P : E → E), Differentiable ℝ P ∧ ∀ y ∈ U, ‖P y - G y‖ < δ
    := by
  let basis := stdOrthonormalBasis ℝ E
  let n := Module.finrank ℝ E
  -- We construct the subalgebra of polynomials from `ℝ^n` to `ℝ` and show they are differentiable
  -- Projecting onto one of the axes is continuous and differentiable
  let coord_sigma (i : Fin n) : C(E, ℝ) :=
    { toFun := fun x => basis.toBasis.equivFunL x i
      continuous_toFun := by fun_prop}
  have hcoord_diff (i : Fin n) : Differentiable ℝ (coord_sigma i) :=
    ((ContinuousLinearMap.proj i).comp
    (basis.toBasis.equivFunL : E →L[ℝ] (Fin n → ℝ))).differentiable
  -- This gives us the subalgebra of polynomials.
  let generator_sigma : Set C(E, ℝ) := Set.range coord_sigma
  have hgen_diff : ∀ f ∈ generator_sigma, Differentiable ℝ f := by
    rintro _ ⟨i, rfl⟩
    exact hcoord_diff i
  let A_sigma : Subalgebra ℝ C(E, ℝ) := Algebra.adjoin ℝ generator_sigma
  have hA_diff : ∀ f ∈ A_sigma, Differentiable ℝ f := by
    let D : Subalgebra ℝ C(E, ℝ) :=
      { carrier := {f | Differentiable ℝ f}
        zero_mem' := differentiable_const 0
        one_mem' := differentiable_const 1
        add_mem' := fun hf hg => hf.add hg
        mul_mem' := fun hf hg => hf.mul hg
        algebraMap_mem' := fun r => differentiable_const r }
    have hgen_sub : generator_sigma ⊆ D := hgen_diff
    have hA_sub : A_sigma ≤ D := Algebra.adjoin_le hgen_sub
    exact fun f hf => hA_sub hf
  -- This subalgebra of polynomials separates points.
  have sep_sigma : A_sigma.SeparatesPoints := by
    intro x y hxy
    have hequiv: basis.toBasis.equivFunL x ≠ basis.toBasis.equivFunL y := by simpa
    obtain ⟨i, hi⟩ : ∃ i : (Fin n), basis.toBasis.equivFunL x i ≠ basis.toBasis.equivFunL y i := by
      contrapose! hequiv
      ext i
      exact (hequiv i)
    have hf_mem : coord_sigma i ∈ A_sigma := Algebra.subset_adjoin (Set.mem_range_self i)
    exact ⟨coord_sigma i, Set.mem_image_of_mem (fun f ↦ f.1) hf_mem, hi⟩
  let G_i (i : Fin n) : C(E, ℝ) :=
    { toFun := fun y => basis.toBasis.equivFunL (G y) i, continuous_toFun := by fun_prop }
  let coordEquiv := basis.toBasis.equivFunL
  have hpos_symm : 0 < ‖(coordEquiv.symm : ((Fin n) → ℝ) →L[ℝ] E)‖ := by
    refine lt_of_le_of_ne (norm_nonneg _) fun h_eq => ?_
    let w : Fin n → ℝ := fun _ => 1
    have hw : w ≠ 0 := by
      have : 0 < n := Module.finrank_pos
      haveI : Nonempty (Fin n) := Fin.pos_iff_nonempty.mp this
      obtain ⟨i⟩ := (inferInstance : Nonempty (Fin n))
      intro h
      have : w i = 0 := congr_fun h i
      linarith
    have hw0 : (coordEquiv.symm : (Fin n → ℝ) →L[ℝ] E) w = 0 := by
      rw [norm_eq_zero.1 h_eq.symm]
      rfl
    have hfalse : coordEquiv (coordEquiv.symm w) = coordEquiv 0 := congrArg coordEquiv hw0
    rw [coordEquiv.apply_symm_apply w, map_zero] at hfalse
    exact hw hfalse
  -- Define `C` as the operator norm for l.symm
  let C := ‖(coordEquiv.symm : (Fin n → ℝ) →L[ℝ] E)‖
  let ε' := δ / (2 * C)
  have hε' : 0 < ε' := div_pos (RCLike.ofReal_pos.mp hδ) (mul_pos zero_lt_two hpos_symm)
  -- Using the Stone-Weierstrass theorem, pick each `P_i` to be `ε'-close` to each `G_i`.
  have approx (i : Fin n) :=
    ContinuousMap.exists_mem_subalgebra_near_continuous_of_isCompact_of_separatesPoints
    sep_sigma (G_i i) hUcompact hε'
  choose p_i hp_i using approx
  -- Construct `P` as a function from `ℝ^n` to `ℝ^n` using the component functions `P_i`.
  let P : C(E, E) :=
    { toFun := fun y => basis.toBasis.equivFunL.symm (fun i => (p_i i : C(E, ℝ)) y),
      continuous_toFun := by fun_prop}
  -- The difference between `P` and `G` on `Σ` is bounded by `δ`
  have hP_bound : ∀ y ∈ U , ‖P y - G y‖ < δ := by
    intro y hy
    let v : Fin n → ℝ := fun i => (p_i i : C(E, ℝ)) y - (basis.toBasis.equivFunL (G y)) i
    have hv i : |v i| < ε' := by
      have := (hp_i i).2 y hy
      simp_all only [ ContinuousMap.coe_mk, Real.norm_eq_abs, G_i, v]
    have hnorm_v : ‖v‖ < ε' := by rw [pi_norm_lt_iff hε']; exact fun i => hv i
    have hP_eq : P y - G y = coordEquiv.symm v := by
      dsimp [P, v]
      have h_repr_eq : basis.toBasis.repr (G y) = coordEquiv (G y) := rfl
      have hG : G y = coordEquiv.symm (coordEquiv (G y)) := (coordEquiv.symm_apply_apply (G y)).symm
      have h_simp : coordEquiv (coordEquiv.symm (coordEquiv (G y))) = coordEquiv (G y) :=
        by rw [coordEquiv.symm_apply_apply (G y)]
      rw [h_repr_eq, hG, ← coordEquiv.symm.map_sub, h_simp]
      rfl
    rw [hP_eq]
    calc
      ‖coordEquiv.symm v‖
      ≤ C * ‖v‖ := ContinuousLinearMap.le_opNorm
          (coordEquiv.symm : (Fin n → ℝ) →L[ℝ] E) v
    _ < C * ε' := mul_lt_mul_of_pos_left hnorm_v hpos_symm
    _ = δ / 2 := by
        unfold ε'
        field_simp [ne_of_gt hpos_symm]
        exact div_self (ne_of_gt hpos_symm)
    _ < δ := half_lt_self hδ
  have hp_i_diff (i : Fin n) : Differentiable ℝ (p_i i) := hA_diff (p_i i) (hp_i i).1
  have hP_diff : Differentiable ℝ P :=
    (basis.toBasis.equivFunL.symm : (Fin n → ℝ) →L[ℝ] E).differentiable.comp
    (differentiable_pi.mpr hp_i_diff)
  use P

this part was separated out and in the main proof body there is now


  obtain ⟨P, hP_diff, hP_bound⟩ := differentiable_approx_of_continuous hδ1 hsigmacompact (fun (y: E) => (G y : E)) (hGcont)

have hP_cont : ContinuousOn (fun v => ‖P v‖) sigma1 := by fun_prop

now fun_prop is unable to close the goal

Response:
The issue is that `P` is obtained from `obtain` as a bare function `E → E`, so `fun_prop` cannot see that it is continuous. It only knows `hP_diff : Differentiable ℝ P`.

---

## Fix

Use `hP_diff.continuous` to get continuity, then apply `ContinuousOn.norm`:

```lean
have hP_cont : ContinuousOn (fun v => ‖P v‖) sigma1 :=
  hP_diff.continuous.continuousOn.norm
```

---

## Why `fun_prop` Fails

`fun_prop` works by looking up continuity facts in its database. When `P` is introduced via `obtain`, it is an opaque term with no registered continuity lemmas. `fun_prop` has no way to know `P` is continuous unless it is told explicitly via `hP_diff.continuous`.

---

## General Pattern

Whenever you have a function obtained from `obtain` or `choose`, you need to bridge the gap manually before `fun_prop` can use it:

```lean
-- fun_prop cannot see this
obtain ⟨P, hP_diff, hP_bound⟩ := ...

-- Bridge: extract continuity explicitly
have hP_cont : Continuous P := hP_diff.continuous

-- Now fun_prop can use hP_cont for downstream goals
have hP_norm_cont : ContinuousOn (fun v => ‖P v‖) sigma1 :=
  hP_cont.continuousOn.norm
```


## If `P` Needs to Be a `ContinuousMap`

Alternatively, change `differentiable_approx_of_continuous` to return a `C(E, E)` instead of a bare function, so the continuity is bundled:

```lean
omit [BrouwerFixedPoint E] in
theorem differentiable_approx_of_continuous {δ : ℝ} (hδ : 0 < δ) {U : Set E} 
    (hUcompact : IsCompact U) (G : E → E)
    (hG_cont : Continuous G) [Nontrivial E] : 
    ∃ (P : C(E, E)), Differentiable ℝ (P : E → E) ∧ ∀ y ∈ U, ‖P y - G y‖ < δ := by
```

Then `P` carries its continuity automatically and `fun_prop` can use it downstream:

```lean
let P' : C(E, E) := {toFun := fun y => P y - v, continuous_toFun := by fun_prop}
```

---

## Recommendation

Changing the return type to `C(E, E)` is the cleaner fix since it avoids manually threading `hP_diff.continuous` through every downstream use of `P`. It also makes the type of `differentiable_approx_of_continuous` more informative.

[04/15/2026 17:58:12 +00:00] User:
unfold_let is not a tactic that exists

Response:
You are right. `unfold_let` is not a real tactic. The correct tactic for unfolding `let` bindings is `simp only` with the let names, or `show` to restate the goal with the definitions expanded.

---

## Option 1 — `simp only` with let names

```lean
have hincl_cont : Continuous incl := by
  simp only [incl, toEuclideanE, coordF_padded, pad, coordF]
  fun_prop
```

---

## Option 2 — `delta` to unfold specific definitions

```lean
have hincl_cont : Continuous incl := by
  delta incl toEuclideanE coordF_padded pad coordF
  fun_prop
```

---

## Option 3 — `show` to restate with expanded definition

```lean
have hincl_cont : Continuous incl := by
  show Continuous (fun x => coordE.symm (toEuclideanE (coordF_padded x)))
  apply Continuous.comp' (LinearIsometryEquiv.continuous _)
  apply Continuous.comp' (ContinuousLinearEquiv.continuous _)
  exact continuous_pi fun i => by
    by_cases hi : i.val < m
    · simp only [dif_pos hi]; fun_prop
    · simp only [dif_neg hi]; exact continuous_const
```

---

## Recommendation

Try **Option 1** first since `simp only` with let names is the standard way to unfold `let` bindings in Lean 4 tactic proofs. If `fun_prop` still cannot handle the `dif` branches after unfolding, fall back to **Option 3**.

[05/14/2026 16:47:25 +00:00] User:
i am trying to prove a lemma that should lead to the brouwer's fixed point theorem. I want to state it in the most natural way in lean

The lemma is , It is not possible for a continuously differentiable function to map B^n onto S^(n-1) and to leave each point of S^(n-1) fixed

Response:
Here is the most natural way to state this in Lean using Mathlib's existing vocabulary:

```lean
/-- It is not possible for a continuously differentiable function to map `B^n` onto `S^(n-1)`
    and to leave each point of `S^(n-1)` fixed. -/
lemma no_retraction_of_ball_to_sphere
    [Nontrivial E]
    (f : E → E)
    (hf_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 f)
    (hf_maps : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1)
    (hf_fixed : ∀ x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1, f x = x) :
    False := by
  sorry
```

---

## Design Decisions

### `ContDiff ℝ 1 f` vs `Differentiable ℝ f`

`ContDiff ℝ 1 f` means continuously differentiable ($$C^1$$), which is the standard hypothesis for the proof via Stokes' theorem or the degree argument. `Differentiable ℝ f` is weaker and may not suffice depending on the proof strategy.

### `sphere (0 : E) 1` vs `frontier (closedBall 0 1)`

Both are equivalent in a normed space but `sphere` is more direct:
```lean
#check sphere (0 : E) 1   -- {x | ‖x‖ = 1}
#check frontier (closedBall (0 : E) 1)  -- equivalent but less direct
```

### `hf_maps` as `MapsTo`

An alternative using `Set.MapsTo`:
```lean
(hf_maps : Set.MapsTo f (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (sphere (0 : E) 1))
```

### `hf_fixed` as a Retraction

The condition that `f` fixes `S^(n-1)` is exactly saying `f` is a **retraction** onto the sphere. Mathlib has:
```lean
#check Set.LeftInvOn
-- Set.LeftInvOn id f (sphere 0 1)
```

So an alternative statement uses this directly:
```lean
(hf_fixed : Set.EqOn f id (sphere (0 : E) 1))
```

---

## Most Concise Version

Using `MapsTo` and `EqOn`:

```lean
lemma no_retraction_of_ball_to_sphere
    [Nontrivial E]
    (f : E → E)
    (hf_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 f)
    (hf_maps : Set.MapsTo f (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (sphere (0 : E) 1))
    (hf_fixed : Set.EqOn f id (sphere (0 : E) 1)) :
    False := by
  sorry
```

---

## Which Version to Use

| Hypothesis | More Explicit | More Concise |
|---|---|---|
| Maps ball to sphere | `∀ x ∈ closedBall 0 1, f x ∈ sphere 0 1` | `Set.MapsTo f (closedBall 0 1) (sphere 0 1)` |
| Fixes sphere | `∀ x ∈ sphere 0 1, f x = x` | `Set.EqOn f id (sphere 0 1)` |

The **most concise version** with `MapsTo` and `EqOn` is the most idiomatic for Mathlib. The **more explicit version** with `∀` is easier to work with inside the proof since the hypotheses can be applied directly without unfolding.

## The Fix

`ContDiff` in Lean 4 Mathlib uses a `ℕ∞` argument, not a plain `ℕ`[doc3]. The correct spelling for continuously differentiable is:

```lean
-- For C^1
(hf_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 f)

-- For C^n with n : ℕ∞
(hf_diff : ContDiff ℝ ⊤ f)  -- smooth (C^∞)
```

The number `1` needs to be coerced to `ℕ∞`. Try:

```lean
lemma no_retraction_of_ball_to_sphere
    [Nontrivial E]
    (f : E → E)
    (hf_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 f)
    (hf_maps : Set.MapsTo f (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (sphere (0 : E) 1))
    (hf_fixed : Set.EqOn f id (sphere (0 : E) 1)) :
    False := by
  sorry
```

If `ContDiff` is still not found, add the explicit import:

```lean
import Mathlib.Analysis.Calculus.ContDiff.Basic
```

Response:
The interpolation between `x` and `f(x)` controlled by `t` is:

$$f_t(x) = x + t \cdot g(x) = x + t \cdot (f(x) - x)$$

---

## Definition

```lean
let g : E → E := fun x => f x - x
let f_t : ℝ → E → E := fun t x => x + t • g x
```

---

## Unfolded Version

Substituting `g` directly:

```lean
let f_t : ℝ → E → E := fun t x => x + t • (f x - x)
```

---

## Checking the Boundary Cases

You can verify the boundary cases hold definitionally:

```lean
-- At t = 0, f_t is the identity
have hft0 : ∀ x, f_t 0 x = x := by
  intro x; simp [f_t, g]

-- At t = 1, f_t is f
have hft1 : ∀ x, f_t 1 x = f x := by
  intro x; simp [f_t, g]
```

---

## Regularity

Since `f` is `ContDiff ℝ 1`, `f_t` is jointly `ContDiff` in both `t` and `x`:

```lean
have hft_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 (fun (p : ℝ × E) => f_t p.1 p.2) := by
  unfold_let f_t g
  apply ContDiff.add
  · exact contDiff_snd
  · apply ContDiff.smul
    · exact contDiff_fst
    · exact hf_diff.comp contDiff_snd |>.sub contDiff_snd
```

---

## The Key Property for the Proof

`f_t` maps `closedBall 0 1` to itself for all `t ∈ [0, 1]` — this is what will eventually be needed:

```lean
have hft_maps : ∀ t ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) 1, 
    Set.MapsTo (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  sorry
```

And `f_t` fixes the sphere for all `t`:

```lean
have hft_fixed : ∀ t, Set.EqOn (f_t t) id (sphere (0 : E) 1) := by
  intro t x hx
  simp only [f_t, g, id]
  rw [hf_fixed hx]
  simp
```

## Why This Works

- `hf_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 f` — given hypothesis
- `contDiff_id : ContDiff ℝ 1 id` — Mathlib lemma for the identity function
- `.sub` — `ContDiff.sub : ContDiff ℝ n f → ContDiff ℝ n g → ContDiff ℝ n (f - g)`

```lean
have hg_cont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g :=
  hf_diff.sub contDiff_id
```

This works if `g` unfolds definitionally to `f - id`, which it does since:

```lean
let g : E → E := fun x => f x - x
-- f x - x = f x - id x = (f - id) x
```


shows that `ContDiff ℝ 1 f` is unfolding to its definition `∃ p, HasFTaylorSeriesUpTo 1 f p`. This happens when Lean elaborates `1` as a natural number and then unfolds `ContDiff` to check the type. Adding the explicit `(1 : ℕ∞)` annotation prevents this unfolding.

it says Unknown constant `ContDiff.sub`

Response:
The search confirms that the correct lemma name is `ContDiff.sub` [doc1], which exists in `Mathlib.Analysis.Calculus.ContDiff.Operations` [doc1]. The issue is not the lemma name but how it is being called.

---

## The Problem

The error says `hf_diff` has type `∃ p, HasFTaylorSeriesUpTo (↑1) f p`, which means Lean is unfolding `ContDiff ℝ 1 f` to its definition rather than treating it as `ContDiff` [doc1]. This is a **coercion issue** with the `1` literal.

---

## The Fix

Add an explicit type annotation to `1` in the hypothesis:

```lean
lemma no_retraction_of_ball_to_sphere
    [Nontrivial E]
    (f : E → E)
    (hf_diff : ContDiff ℝ (1 : ℕ∞) f)  -- explicit type annotation here
    (hf_maps : Set.MapsTo f (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (sphere (0 : E) 1))
    (hf_fixed : Set.EqOn f id (sphere (0 : E) 1)) :
    False := by
  ...
```

Then `ContDiff.sub` can be applied via dot notation since `hf_diff` is now properly typed [doc1]:

```lean
have hg_cont_diff : ContDiff ℝ (1 : ℕ∞) g :=
  hf_diff.sub contDiff_id
```

---

## Why This Happens

`ContDiff ℝ n f` takes `n : WithTop ℕ∞` [doc1]. When you write `1`, Lean tries to elaborate it and may choose `ℕ` instead of `ℕ∞`, causing `ContDiff` to unfold to its definition `∃ p, HasFTaylorSeriesUpTo` rather than remaining as an opaque predicate. The explicit `(1 : ℕ∞)` annotation forces the correct type [doc1].

Response:

```lean
  · exact hg_cont_diff.contDiffOn
```

## Breaking Down the Four Arguments

| Argument | What it proves | Lemma used |
|---|---|---|
| `hg_cont_diff.contDiffOn` | `ContDiffOn ℝ 1 g (closedBall 0 1)` | `ContDiff.contDiffOn` |
| `norm_num` | `(1 : ℕ∞) ≠ 0` | numeric |
| `convex_closedBall 0 1` | `Convex ℝ (closedBall 0 1)` | Mathlib lemma |

## Extracting `C`

```lean

-- hK : LipschitzOnWith K g (closedBall 0 1)
-- which means ∀ x ∈ closedBall 0 1, ∀ y ∈ closedBall 0 1,

```

The `LipschitzOnWith K f s` statement in Mathlib means:

$$\forall x \in s, \forall y \in s, \|f(x) - f(y)\| \leq K \cdot \|x - y\|$$

which is exactly the bound you need with `C = K`.

[05/14/2026 17:28:45 +00:00] User:
have statement saying that f_t is injective when 0 le t < 1/C

Response:
The key idea is that if `t < 1/C` then `t * C < 1`, which means the map `x ↦ t • g x` is a contraction, so `f_t t = id + t • g` is injective.

---

## The Have Statement

```lean
have hft_inj : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < 1 / K → Function.Injective (f_t t) := by
  intro t ht0 htK
  intro x y hxy
  simp only [f_t] at hxy
  -- hxy : x + t • g x = y + t • g y
  have hxy' : x - y = t • (g y - g x) := by
    have := congr_arg (· - (y + t • g y)) hxy
    simp only [add_sub_cancel_left] at this
    linarith [this]
    abel_nf at this ⊢
    linarith
  -- Take norms
  by_contra hne
  have hne' : ‖x - y‖ > 0 := norm_pos_iff.mpr (sub_ne_zero.mpr hne)
  have hbound : ‖x - y‖ ≤ t * K * ‖x - y‖ := by
    calc ‖x - y‖ = ‖t • (g y - g x)‖ := by rw [hxy']
      _ = t * ‖g y - g x‖ := by rw [norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
      _ ≤ t * (K * ‖y - x‖) := by
          apply mul_le_mul_of_nonneg_left _ ht0
          have := hK.norm_sub_le (mem_closedBall_self (by norm_num))
            (mem_closedBall_self (by norm_num))
          exact this
      _ = t * K * ‖x - y‖ := by rw [norm_sub_rev]; ring
  have : t * K < 1 := by
    rw [div_lt_iff (by positivity)] at htK
    linarith
  linarith
```

---

## Cleaner Version

The argument is cleaner if we separate the norm bound:

```lean
have hft_inj : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < 1 / K → Function.Injective (f_t t) := by
  intro t ht0 htK x y hxy
  -- Rearrange hxy to x - y = t • (g y - g x)
  have hkey : x - y = t • (g y - g x) := by
    simp only [f_t] at hxy
    linear_combination hxy
  -- If x ≠ y, derive a contradiction via the Lipschitz bound
  by_contra hne
  have hpos : 0 < ‖x - y‖ := norm_pos_iff.mpr (sub_ne_zero.mpr hne)
  have hle : ‖x - y‖ ≤ t * K * ‖x - y‖ := by
    nth_rw 1 [hkey]
    rw [norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0, norm_sub_rev]
    have hLip := hK.norm_sub_le
      (x := x) (y := y)
      (hK.1 (mem_closedBall_self (by norm_num)))
      (hK.1 (mem_closedBall_self (by norm_num)))
    nlinarith
  have htK' : t * K < 1 := by
    rwa [div_lt_iff (NNReal.coe_pos.mpr (by positivity))] at htK
  linarith
```

---

## Note on `K`

`K : NNReal` from `LipschitzOnWith`, so you may need `(K : ℝ)` coercions in the arithmetic. The bound `LipschitzOnWith K g s` means:

$$\|g(x) - g(y)\| \leq K \cdot \|x - y\|$$

so `t * K < 1` ensures `f_t t` is injective by the standard argument that `id + contraction` is injective.

[05/14/2026 17:39:27 +00:00] User:

Response:

Wait — this should follow directly from rearranging `hxy`. Let me state it cleanly:

---

## The Have Statement

```lean
have hnorm_eq : ‖y - x‖ = ‖t • g y - t • g x‖ := by
  have hrearrange : y - x = t • g y - t • g x := by
    simp only [f_t] at hxy
    linear_combination hxy
  rw [hrearrange]
```

---

## Why This Works

From `hxy : f_t t x = f_t t y`, expanding the definition:

$$x + t \cdot g(x) = y + t \cdot g(y)$$

Rearranging:

$$y - x = t \cdot g(y) - t \cdot g(x)$$

Taking norms of both sides gives the result. The key step is `linear_combination hxy` which handles the algebraic rearrangement automatically.

---

## If `linear_combination` Fails

```lean
have hrearrange : y - x = t • g y - t • g x := by
  simp only [f_t] at hxy
  have := congr_arg (fun z => z - x - t • g x) hxy
  simp only [add_sub_cancel_left] at this
  linarith
```

[05/14/2026 17:45:30 +00:00] User:
have hnorm_le : ‖t • g y - t • g x‖ ≤ t * C * ‖y - x‖ := by sorry
want to turn into a form that can be done by grind

Response:
The bound follows from the Lipschitz condition on `g` and linearity of the scalar multiplication. Break it down to get it into a form `grind` can handle:

---

## Step by Step

```lean
have hnorm_le : ‖t • g y - t • g x‖ ≤ t * C * ‖y - x‖ := by
  rw [← smul_sub, norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
  have hLip : ‖g y - g x‖ ≤ C * ‖y - x‖ := by
    have := hK.norm_sub_le hy hx
    simp only [NNReal.coe_mk] at this
    linarith
  nlinarith
```

---

## Breaking Down Each Step

### `rw [← smul_sub, norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]`

Rewrites the left side:

$$\|t \cdot g(y) - t \cdot g(x)\| = \|t \cdot (g(y) - g(x))\| = t \cdot \|g(y) - g(x)\|$$

using `t ≥ 0` for `Real.norm_of_nonneg`.

### `hLip`

Extracts the Lipschitz bound from `hK : LipschitzOnWith K g (closedBall 0 1)`:

$$\|g(y) - g(x)\| \leq C \cdot \|y - x\|$$

### `nlinarith`

Combines `t ≥ 0`, `hLip`, and the rewritten left side to close:

$$t \cdot \|g(y) - g(x)\| \leq t \cdot C \cdot \|y - x\|$$

---

## Note on `C` vs `K`

If `K : NNReal` you will need the coercion `C := (K : ℝ)` and `NNReal.coe_mk` or `NNReal.coe_le_coe` to move between the two. Share the exact type of `C` in your proof if `nlinarith` fails and we can adjust.

[05/14/2026 17:48:46 +00:00] User:

Response:
Good point. `LipschitzOnWith` requires membership proofs for the points, and using `InjOn` means the points `x y` are already known to be in the set. Here is the corrected statement:

```lean

  intro t ht0 htC x hx y hy hxy
```

Now `hx : x ∈ closedBall 0 1` and `hy : y ∈ closedBall 0 1` are available directly from `InjOn`, so the Lipschitz bound becomes:

```lean
  have hnorm_le : ‖t • g y - t • g x‖ ≤ t * C * ‖y - x‖ := by
    rw [← smul_sub, norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
    have hLip : ‖g y - g x‖ ≤ C * ‖y - x‖ := by

      simp only [NNReal.coe_mk] at this
```

## Why `InjOn` is More Natural Here

`Function.Injective` requires the function to be injective on all of `E`, but `f_t t` is only injective on `closedBall 0 1` where the Lipschitz bound holds. `Set.InjOn` is the correct statement since:

- The Lipschitz bound `hK` only holds on `closedBall 0 1`
- The membership proofs `hx` and `hy` are needed to apply `hK.norm_sub_le`
- The conclusion is only needed on `closedBall 0 1` for the rest of the proof

```lean
have : t * C < 1 := by
  rcases eq_or_lt_of_le (NNReal.coe_nonneg K) with hC | hC
  · simp [← hC]
    positivity
```

[05/14/2026 18:00:16 +00:00] User:
the lipschitz constant provided by the theorem should be possible to be 0, in that case, x = y follows directly

Response:
Good point. If `C = 0` then `g` is constant (specifically `g = 0` on the ball), which means `f_t t x = x + t • g x = x + 0 = x` for all `x`, so `f_t t` is the identity and injectivity is trivial.

---

## Fix with Case Split on `C`

```lean
have hft_inj : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < 1 / C → Set.InjOn (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx y hy hxy
  rcases eq_or_lt_of_le (NNReal.coe_nonneg K) with hC | hC
  · -- Case C = 0: g is constant zero on the ball
    have hgx : g x = 0 := by
      have := hK.norm_sub_le hx hx
      simp [← hC] at this
      exact norm_eq_zero.mp (le_antisymm this (norm_nonneg _))
    have hgy : g y = 0 := by
      have := hK.norm_sub_le hy hy
      simp [← hC] at this
      exact norm_eq_zero.mp (le_antisymm this (norm_nonneg _))
    simp only [f_t, hgx, hgy, smul_zero, add_zero] at hxy
    exact hxy
  · -- Case C > 0: use the norm bound
    by_contra hne
    have hpos : 0 < ‖x - y‖ := norm_pos_iff.mpr (sub_ne_zero.mpr hne)
    have hnorm_le : ‖x - y‖ ≤ t * C * ‖x - y‖ := by
      have hrearrange : x - y = t • g y - t • g x := by
        simp only [f_t] at hxy
        linear_combination hxy
      rw [hrearrange, ← smul_sub, norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
      have hLip : ‖g y - g x‖ ≤ C * ‖y - x‖ := by
        have := hK.norm_sub_le hy hx
        simp only [NNReal.coe_mk] at this
        linarith
      nlinarith [norm_sub_rev x y]
    have htC' : t * C < 1 := by
      rwa [lt_div_iff hC] at htC
    linarith
```

---

## Why the `C = 0` Case Is Separate

When `C = 0`, `1 / C` is `1 / 0 = 0` in Lean's real number arithmetic, so `t < 1 / C` becomes `t < 0`, which contradicts `ht0 : 0 ≤ t`. This means the `C = 0` case is actually **vacuously true** and can be closed immediately:

```lean
rcases eq_or_lt_of_le (NNReal.coe_nonneg K) with hC | hC
· -- C = 0 so 1/C = 0 and t < 0 contradicts ht0
  simp [← hC, div_zero] at htC
  linarith
· -- C > 0: main argument
  ...
```

This is cleaner since we do not need to reason about `g` at all in the zero case.

[05/14/2026 18:10:14 +00:00] User:
hnorm_le' : ‖x - y‖ ≤ t * ↑C * ‖y - x‖
this : t * ↑C < 1
⊢ x = y
this could be done by contradiction, x-y being positive etc., is there a nicer way?

Response:
Yes. Since `‖x - y‖ = ‖y - x‖`, the hypothesis `hnorm_le'` says `‖x - y‖ ≤ t * C * ‖x - y‖` with `t * C < 1`, which directly gives `‖x - y‖ ≤ 0`, hence `x = y`:

```lean
have : ‖x - y‖ = 0 := by
  rw [norm_sub_rev] at hnorm_le'
  nlinarith
exact sub_eq_zero.mp (norm_eq_zero.mp this)
```

Or even more directly in one line:

```lean
exact sub_eq_zero.mp (norm_eq_zero.mp (by rw [norm_sub_rev] at hnorm_le'; nlinarith))
```

---

## Why This Is Nicer

Rather than introducing a contradiction and working with `‖x - y‖ > 0`, we directly show `‖x - y‖ = 0` using `nlinarith` which sees:

- `hnorm_le' : ‖x - y‖ ≤ t * C * ‖x - y‖`
- `this : t * C < 1`
- `norm_nonneg (x - y) : 0 ≤ ‖x - y‖`

From these three facts, `nlinarith` concludes `‖x - y‖ ≤ 0`, and combined with nonnegativity gives `‖x - y‖ = 0`, hence `x = y`.

[05/14/2026 18:12:29 +00:00] User:
nlinarith did not close the goal, doesnt this implicitly rely on norm x-y not being 0

Response:
You are right. `nlinarith` needs the nonnegativity of `‖x - y‖` explicitly provided. The issue is that from:

- `‖x - y‖ ≤ t * C * ‖x - y‖`
- `t * C < 1`

we need to conclude `‖x - y‖ = 0`, but this requires knowing `0 ≤ ‖x - y‖` to rule out the case where `‖x - y‖` could be negative (which it cannot, but `nlinarith` needs to be told):

---

## Fix

```lean
have hpos : 0 ≤ ‖x - y‖ := norm_nonneg _
have hzero : ‖x - y‖ = 0 := by
  rw [norm_sub_rev] at hnorm_le'
  nlinarith
exact sub_eq_zero.mp (norm_eq_zero.mp hzero)
```

---

## Why This Works Now

With `hpos` explicitly in context, `nlinarith` has all three facts it needs:

$$0 \leq \|x - y\|$$
$$\|x - y\| \leq t \cdot C \cdot \|x - y\|$$
$$t \cdot C < 1$$

From these it can derive:

$$\|x - y\| \leq t \cdot C \cdot \|x - y\| < 1 \cdot \|x - y\| = \|x - y\|$$

which forces `‖x - y‖ = 0`, and then `sub_eq_zero.mp (norm_eq_zero.mp hzero)` gives `x = y`.

[05/14/2026 18:14:42 +00:00] User:

```lean
rcases (norm_nonneg (x - y)).eq_or_gt with hzero | hpos

  rw [norm_sub_rev] at hnorm_le'
```

## Why This Is Clean

The `rcases` split on `0 ≤ ‖x - y‖` gives exactly two cases:

- **`hzero : 0 = ‖x - y‖`** — directly gives `x = y` via `norm_eq_zero` and `sub_eq_zero`
- **`hpos : 0 < ‖x - y‖`** — now `nlinarith` can derive a contradiction from:
  - `hpos : 0 < ‖x - y‖`
  - `hnorm_le' : ‖x - y‖ ≤ t * C * ‖y - x‖` (after `norm_sub_rev`)
  - `this : t * C < 1`

since these three together give `‖x - y‖ < ‖x - y‖`, which is `False`.

[05/14/2026 18:31:36 +00:00] User:
nlinarith did not close the goal, explicitly show ‖x - y‖ < ‖x - y‖, maybe with calc

Response:
```lean
· exfalso
  rw [norm_sub_rev] at hnorm_le'
  have : ‖x - y‖ < ‖x - y‖ := calc
    ‖x - y‖ ≤ t * C * ‖x - y‖ := by rwa [norm_sub_rev]
    _ < 1 * ‖x - y‖ := by nlinarith
    _ = ‖x - y‖ := one_mul _
  exact lt_irrefl _ this
```

---

## Why This Works

The `calc` chain makes each step explicit:

1. `‖x - y‖ ≤ t * C * ‖x - y‖` — from `hnorm_le'` after `norm_sub_rev`
2. `t * C * ‖x - y‖ < 1 * ‖x - y‖` — from `this : t * C < 1` and `hpos : 0 < ‖x - y‖`, closed by `nlinarith`
3. `1 * ‖x - y‖ = ‖x - y‖` — by `one_mul`

This gives `‖x - y‖ < ‖x - y‖` which `lt_irrefl` turns into `False`.

[05/14/2026 18:42:30 +00:00] User:
how does one work with jacobians in mathlib

Response:
Mathlib's Jacobian machinery is built around the Fréchet derivative. Here is an overview of the key components.

---

## 1. The Fréchet Derivative

The fundamental object is `fderiv ℝ f x`, the Fréchet derivative of `f` at `x`:

```lean
#check fderiv
-- fderiv : (𝕜 : Type) → (E → F) → E → (E →L[𝕜] F)
```

For `f : E → E` where `E` is finite dimensional, this is a continuous linear map `E →L[ℝ] E`, which corresponds to the Jacobian matrix.

---

## 2. The Determinant of the Jacobian

The determinant is accessed via the `LinearMap.det` of the underlying linear map:

```lean
#check LinearMap.det
-- LinearMap.det : (E →ₗ[R] E) → R
```

For the Jacobian of `f` at `x`:

```lean
let J := fderiv ℝ f x
let detJ := LinearMap.det (J : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)
```

---

## 3. Change of Variables Formula

The main theorem relating Jacobians to integration:

```lean
#check MeasureTheory.integral_image_eq_integral_abs_det_fderiv_smul
```

This says for an injective `C¹` map `f`:

$$\int_{f(s)} g \, d\mu = \int_s |det(Df_x)| \cdot g(f(x)) \, d\mu$$

---

## 4. The Jacobian as a Function

Mathlib defines the Jacobian determinant as a standalone function:

```lean
#check MeasureTheory.jacobian
-- MeasureTheory.jacobian : (E → F) → E → ℝ≥0∞
```

Used in:

```lean
#check MeasureTheory.lintegral_image_eq_lintegral_abs_det_fderiv_mul
```

---

## 5. Key Lemmas for Working with Jacobians

### Differentiability implies Jacobian exists

```lean
#check HasFDerivAt
#check DifferentiableAt.hasFDerivAt
```

### The Jacobian of a composition (chain rule)

```lean
#check fderiv.comp
-- fderiv ℝ (g ∘ f) x = fderiv ℝ g (f x) ∘L fderiv ℝ f x
```

### Determinant of composition

```lean
#check LinearMap.det_comp
-- LinearMap.det (f ∘ g) = LinearMap.det f * LinearMap.det g
```

### Jacobian of a linear map

```lean
#check ContinuousLinearMap.fderiv
-- fderiv ℝ f x = f  (for linear f)
```

---

## 6. Measure Zero via Jacobian

The lemma used in your invariance of domain proof:

```lean
#check MeasureTheory.addHaar_image_eq_zero_of_differentiableOn_of_addHaar_eq_zero
```

This says if `f` is differentiable and the domain has measure zero, so does the image.

---

## 7. Practical Example

Computing with the Jacobian of a specific map:

```lean
example (f : E → E) (hf : HasFDerivAt f L x) :
    LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) = LinearMap.det (L : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) := by
  rw [hf.fderiv]
```

---

## 8. The Integral of the Jacobian Over the Ball

For the no-retraction proof, the key fact is:

```lean
#check MeasureTheory.integral_divergence_of_hasFDerivWithinAt_off_countable
```

This is the divergence theorem, which combined with Jacobian computations gives the contradiction in the standard proof of no-retraction via integration.

[05/14/2026 18:46:05 +00:00] User:
Want to show that the jacobian matrix of f_t is nonsingular provided t small to apply the inverse function theorem

Response:
The Jacobian of `f_t t` at `x` is:

$$D(f_t)_x = I + t \cdot Dg_x$$

For this to be nonsingular, we need `det(I + t · Dg_x) ≠ 0`, which follows from the operator norm bound when `t` is small.

---

## Step 1 — Compute the Fréchet Derivative of `f_t`

```lean
have hft_fderiv : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    HasFDerivAt (f_t t) (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x := by
  intro x hx
  unfold_let f_t
  have hg_diff : DifferentiableAt ℝ g x :=
    hg_cont_diff.differentiable (by norm_num) |>.differentiableAt
  have := hg_diff.hasFDerivAt
  have hid : HasFDerivAt id (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E) x := hasFDerivAt_id ℝ x
  simpa using hid.add (this.const_smul t)
```

---

## Step 2 — Bound the Operator Norm of `t • fderiv ℝ g x`

```lean
have hderiv_bound : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    ‖t • fderiv ℝ g x‖ < 1 := by
  intro x hx
  rw [norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
  have hbound : ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ ≤ C := by
    sorry -- follows from hg_cont_diff and the Lipschitz bound
  calc t * ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖
      ≤ t * C := by nlinarith
    _ < 1 := by rwa [lt_div_iff hCpos] at htC
```

---

## Step 3 — The Jacobian is Nonsingular

When `‖t • fderiv ℝ g x‖ < 1`, the operator `I + t • Dg_x` is invertible by the Neumann series:

```lean
have hft_nonsingular : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    IsUnit (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) := by
  intro x hx
  apply ContinuousLinearMap.isUnit_of_norm_lt_one
  · exact hderiv_bound x hx
```

---

## Step 4 — The Determinant is Nonzero

```lean
have hdet_nonzero : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) ≠ 0 := by
  intro x hx
  have hunit := hft_nonsingular x hx
  rw [(hft_fderiv x hx).fderiv]
  exact LinearMap.det_ne_zero_of_isUnit hunit
```

---

## Step 5 — Apply the Inverse Function Theorem

```lean
#check ContDiff.to_localInverse
#check HasStrictFDerivAt.localInverse
```

With the nonsingular Jacobian, the inverse function theorem gives a local inverse:

```lean
have hft_local_inv : ∀ x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
    ∃ (g : E → E), ContDiffAt ℝ 1 g (f_t t x) ∧
    ∀ y ∈ nhds (f_t t x), g (f_t t y) = y := by
  intro x hx
  have hstrict : HasStrictFDerivAt (f_t t)
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x := by
    exact (hft_fderiv x (interior_subset hx)).hasStrictFDerivAt
      (hg_cont_diff.contDiffAt)
  exact ⟨hstrict.localInverse _ _ (hft_nonsingular x (interior_subset hx)),
    hstrict.localInverse_apply_image, hstrict.eventually_left_inverse⟩
```

---

## Key Lemma Needed

The bound `‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ ≤ C` in Step 2 is the main `sorry`. This follows from the fact that for a `C¹` function, the operator norm of the derivative is bounded by the Lipschitz constant:

```lean
#check ContDiffOn.norm_fderiv_le_of_lipschitzOnWith
-- or
#check LipschitzOnWith.norm_fderiv_le
```

The relationship is:

$$\|Dg_x\| \leq K$$

whenever `g` is `K`-Lipschitz, which connects Step 2 back to `hK : LipschitzOnWith K g (closedBall 0 1)`.

---

## Summary

| Step | Key Lemma |
|---|---|
| Compute `D(f_t)` | `HasFDerivAt.add`, `HasFDerivAt.const_smul` |
| Bound `‖t • Dg‖` | Lipschitz constant bounds derivative norm |
| Nonsingularity | `ContinuousLinearMap.isUnit_of_norm_lt_one` |
| Det nonzero | `LinearMap.det_ne_zero_of_isUnit` |
| Local inverse | `HasStrictFDerivAt.localInverse` |

Response:
The right approach is to introduce `t` with `obtain` or `use` only when needed, and work with a universally quantified statement until then. The cleanest structure is:

---

## Structure

```lean
-- State everything for a general t satisfying the bounds
suffices h : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < 1 / C →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    IsUnit (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) by
  -- Then pick a specific t0
  obtain ⟨t0, ht0_pos, ht0_bound⟩ : ∃ t0 : ℝ, 0 < t0 ∧ t0 < 1 / C := by
    exact ⟨1 / (2 * C), by positivity, by
      rw [div_lt_div_iff (by positivity) (by positivity)]
      linarith⟩
  exact h t0 ht0_pos.le ht0_bound
intro t ht0 htC x hx
```

---

## Alternative — Introduce `t` with `intro` Directly

If the goal is already universally quantified over `t`:

```lean

    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    IsUnit (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx
  ...
```

Then later pick a specific `t`:

```lean
obtain ⟨t, ht0, htC⟩ : ∃ t : ℝ, 0 < t ∧ t < 1 / C :=
  ⟨1 / (2 * C), by positivity, by
    apply div_lt_div_of_pos_left one_pos (by positivity)
    linarith⟩
```

---

## Recommendation

State all the intermediate lemmas (`hft_fderiv`, `hft_nonsingular`, `hdet_nonzero`) universally quantified over `t` with the bounds `0 ≤ t` and `t < 1 / C` as hypotheses. Only introduce a specific `t0` at the point where the inverse function theorem is applied, using `obtain` to extract it from the existence of a value in `(0, 1/C)`.

[05/14/2026 18:59:49 +00:00] User:
let's use

Response:
The function `f_t t` is `fun x => x + t • g x`, which is `id + t • g`. So we need `HasFDerivAt` for both parts and then add them:

---

## Using `HasFDerivAt.add`

```lean
have hft_fderiv : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ x : E,
    HasFDerivAt (f_t t) (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x := by
  intro t x
  have hid : HasFDerivAt id (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E) x :=
    hasFDerivAt_id ℝ x
  have hg_diff : HasFDerivAt g (fderiv ℝ g x) x :=
    (hg_cont_diff.differentiable (by norm_num)).differentiableAt.hasFDerivAt
  have hsmul : HasFDerivAt (fun x => t • g x) (t • fderiv ℝ g x) x :=
    hg_diff.const_smul t
  have := hid.add hsmul
  simp only [f_t, id] at this ⊢
  exact this
```

---

## Why `id` Needs Care

`HasFDerivAt.add` expects `f + g` as a function, which is `fun x => f x + g x`. The function `f_t t = fun x => x + t • g x` is exactly `id + (fun x => t • g x)`, so the derivatives add to `ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x`.

---

## Simpler Version

If `simp` can handle the unfolding:

```lean
have hft_fderiv : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ x : E,
    HasFDerivAt (f_t t) (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x := by
  intro t x
  exact (hasFDerivAt_id ℝ x).add
```

[05/15/2026 12:57:41 +00:00] User:
the statement for hderiv_bound should have an exists t0, such that if t is less than the t0 the bound holds 

Response:
```lean
have hderiv_bound : ∃ t0 : ℝ, 0 < t0 ∧ ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    ‖t • fderiv ℝ g x‖ < 1 := by
  sorry
```

---

## What `t0` Should Be

The natural choice is `t0 = 1 / C` where `C` bounds `‖fderiv ℝ g x‖` on the ball. Then for `t < t0`:

$$\|t \cdot Dg_x\| = t \cdot \|Dg_x\| \leq t \cdot C < t_0 \cdot C = 1$$

---

## Proof

```lean
have hderiv_bound : ∃ t0 : ℝ, 0 < t0 ∧ ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    ‖t • fderiv ℝ g x‖ < 1 := by
  -- Bound the operator norm of fderiv g on the ball
  have hfderiv_bound : ∃ M : ℝ, 0 ≤ M ∧ ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ ≤ M := by
    have hcont : ContinuousOn (fun x => ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
      (hg_cont_diff.continuous_fderiv (by norm_num)).continuousOn.norm
    obtain ⟨x, _, hmax⟩ := (isCompact_closedBall (0 : E) 1).exists_isMaxOn
      (by simp) hcont
    exact ⟨‖fderiv ℝ g x‖, norm_nonneg _, fun y hy => hmax hy⟩
  obtain ⟨M, hM0, hM⟩ := hfderiv_bound
  -- Pick t0 = 1 / (M + 1) to avoid division by zero
  refine ⟨1 / (M + 1), by positivity, fun t ht0 htM x hx => ?_⟩
  rw [norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
  have hMx : ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ ≤ M := hM x hx
  have hMpos : 0 < M + 1 := by linarith
  calc t * ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖
      ≤ t * M := by nlinarith
    _ < (1 / (M + 1)) * M := by nlinarith
    _ < 1 := by rw [div_mul_eq_mul_div, div_lt_one hMpos]; linarith
```

---

## Why `M + 1` Instead of `M`

Using `t0 = 1 / (M + 1)` instead of `1 / M` avoids the case `M = 0` causing division by zero, and the proof goes through cleanly since `M + 1 > 0` always.

[05/15/2026 13:06:26 +00:00] User:
nlinarith fails for 
_ < (1 / (M + 1)) * M := by nlinarith
this line because t could be 0

Response:
You are right. If `t = 0` then `t * M = 0` and `(1 / (M + 1)) * M ≥ 0`, so the strict inequality `t * M < (1 / (M + 1)) * M` fails when `M = 0` as well. The issue is that we need `t * M < 1` directly, not via this intermediate step.

---

## Fix — Go Directly to the Goal

```lean
calc t * ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖
    ≤ t * M := by nlinarith
  _ < 1 := by
      have : t * (M + 1) < 1 := by
        calc t * (M + 1) < (1 / (M + 1)) * (M + 1) := by
              apply mul_lt_mul_of_pos_right htM hMpos
          _ = 1 := by field_simp
      nlinarith
```

---

## Why This Works

Instead of going through `(1 / (M + 1)) * M`, we use `t * (M + 1) < 1` which follows from `t < 1 / (M + 1)` by multiplying both sides by `M + 1 > 0`. Then:

$$t \cdot M \leq t \cdot (M + 1) - t < 1 - t \leq 1$$

which `nlinarith` can handle with `ht0 : 0 ≤ t` in context.

## If `ContinuousLinearMap.isUnit_of_norm_lt_one` Does Not Exist

The correct Mathlib lemma may be:

```lean
#check ContinuousLinearMap.units_of_norm_lt_one
-- or
#check ContinuousLinearMap.isUnit_of_dist_lt_one
```

The underlying fact is that `I + A` is invertible when `‖A‖ < 1` by the Neumann series. The relevant lemma is:

```lean
#check Units.add_of_norm_lt_one
```

Which gives:

```lean
have hft_nonsingular : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    IsUnit (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx
  have hbound := hderiv_bound t ht0 htC x hx
  rw [isUnit_iff_ne_zero]
  -- I + A is invertible when ‖A‖ < 1
  exact (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E).isUnit_add_of_norm_lt hbound
```

[05/15/2026 13:39:09 +00:00] User:
searching on mathlib, no such lemma exists, 

why is the lemma true? intuitively, if one takes the identity matrix and only adds small values to each of the rows, there is no way that the rows would become linearly dependent, but what machinery should be used with the operator norms?

Response:
The lemma is true because of the **Neumann series**. If `‖A‖ < 1`, then the series `∑ Aⁿ` converges and its sum is the inverse of `I - A`. Applied to `I + A = I - (-A)` with `‖-A‖ = ‖A‖ < 1`, this gives an explicit inverse.

---

## The Mathlib Machinery

The relevant Mathlib theorem is:

```lean
#check ContinuousLinearMap.units_of_norm_lt_one
-- or
#check NormedRing.inverse_add
#check Units.add
```

Actually the correct one is:

```lean
#check ContinuousLinearMap.isUnit_of_norm_lt_one
```

Which does not exist. But this does:

```lean
#check ContinuousLinearMap.isOpen_setOf_isUnit
```

The actual Mathlib approach uses:

```lean
#check invertibleOfNormLtOne
```

Or via the `Units` API:

```lean
example (A : E →L[ℝ] E) (h : ‖A‖ < 1) :
    IsUnit (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + A) := by
  exact?
```

---

## The Neumann Series in Mathlib

The key theorem is:

```lean
#check NormedRing.summable_geometric_of_norm_lt_one
-- ‖r‖ < 1 → Summable (fun n => r ^ n)

#check tsum_geometric_of_norm_lt_one  
-- ‖r‖ < 1 → ∑ r^n = (1 - r)⁻¹
```

For continuous linear maps specifically:

```lean
#check ContinuousLinearMap.hasSum_geometric_of_norm_lt_one
```

---

## Manual Proof of Invertibility

The cleanest approach in Mathlib is through the `Units` of the normed ring `E →L[ℝ] E`:

```lean
have hft_nonsingular : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    IsUnit (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx
  have hbound := hderiv_bound t ht0 htC x hx
  -- Rewrite as 1 + A where ‖A‖ < 1
  rw [show ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x =
    1 + t • fderiv ℝ g x from by simp]
  -- Use that 1 + A is a unit when ‖A‖ < 1 in a Banach algebra
  apply isUnit_of_norm_lt_one
  simpa using hbound
```

Where `isUnit_of_norm_lt_one` is:

```lean
#check isUnit_of_norm_lt_one
-- in a Banach algebra, ‖1 - u‖ < 1 → IsUnit u
-- or equivalently ‖a‖ < 1 → IsUnit (1 + a)
```

---

## If That Fails — Use `Metric.isOpen_setOf_isUnit`

The set of units is open in a Banach algebra, and `id` is a unit, so nearby elements are also units:

```lean
have hft_nonsingular : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    IsUnit (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx
  have hbound := hderiv_bound t ht0 htC x hx
  have hid : IsUnit (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E) := isUnit_one
  -- The set of units is open
  have hopen : IsOpen {f : E →L[ℝ] E | IsUnit f} :=
    ContinuousLinearMap.isOpen_setOf_isUnit
  -- id + t • fderiv g x is close to id
  have hdist : dist (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x)
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E) < 1 := by
    simp [dist_eq_norm, hbound]
  -- Since the set of units is open and id is a unit,
  -- nearby elements are also units
  exact hopen.mem_nhds hid |>.eventually.mono (fun _ h => h) |>.self_of_nhds
```

---

## Most Direct Route

```lean
    IsUnit (1 + A) := by
```

## Summary of the Mathematical Argument

| Step | Mathematical Content | Mathlib Tool |
|---|---|---|
| `‖A‖ < 1` | Operator norm bound | `hderiv_bound` |
| `∑ (-A)ⁿ` converges | Neumann series | `summable_geometric_of_norm_lt_one` |
| `(I + A)⁻¹ = ∑ (-A)ⁿ` | Geometric series identity | `tsum_geometric_of_norm_lt_one` |
| `I + A` is invertible | Hence a unit | `IsUnit` |

[05/15/2026 13:52:39 +00:00] User:
instead of trying to use the neumann series, use the fact that provided t is small enough, the matrix is strictly dominated by its diagonal, in particular, the mathlib theorem
where the previous steps may have to be redone to accomodate

theorem det_ne_zero_of_sum_row_lt_diag {K : Type u_1} {n : Type u_2} [NormedField K] [Fintype n] [DecidableEq n] {A : Matrix n n K} (h : ∀ (k : n), ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖A k j‖ < ‖A k k‖) :
A.det ≠ 0

Response:
Good approach. This is the **Gershgorin circle theorem** — a matrix is nonsingular if it is strictly diagonally dominant. The plan is to show the matrix of `I + t • Dg_x` in the standard basis is strictly diagonally dominant for small `t`.

---

## The Setup

We need to work with the matrix representation of `ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x` in the orthonormal basis. The diagonal entries are `1 + t • (Dg_x)_ii` and the off-diagonal entries are `t • (Dg_x)_ij`.

---

## Step 1 — Represent the Linear Map as a Matrix

```lean
let basis := stdOrthonormalBasis ℝ E
let toMatrix := LinearMap.toMatrix basis.toBasis basis.toBasis
let J : Matrix (Fin n) (Fin n) ℝ := 
  toMatrix (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x)
```

---

## Step 2 — The Matrix Entries

```lean
have hJ_diag : ∀ k : Fin n, J k k = 1 + t * (toMatrix (fderiv ℝ g x)) k k := by
  intro k
  simp [J, toMatrix, LinearMap.toMatrix_add, LinearMap.toMatrix_smul,
    LinearMap.toMatrix_id]

have hJ_offdiag : ∀ k j : Fin n, k ≠ j → 
    J k j = t * (toMatrix (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j := by
  intro k j hkj
  simp [J, toMatrix, LinearMap.toMatrix_add, LinearMap.toMatrix_smul,
    LinearMap.toMatrix_id, hkj]
```

---

## Step 3 — Bound the Off-Diagonal Entries

```lean
have hoffdiag_bound : ∃ t0 : ℝ, 0 < t0 ∧ ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, ∀ k : Fin n,
    ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J k j‖ < ‖J k k‖ := by
  sorry
```

---

## Step 4 — Apply `det_ne_zero_of_sum_row_lt_diag`

```lean
have hdet_nonzero : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    (toMatrix (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x)).det ≠ 0 := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx
  apply Matrix.det_ne_zero_of_sum_row_lt_diag
  exact hoffdiag_bound t ht0 htC x hx
```

---

## Step 5 — Connect Matrix Det to Linear Map

```lean
have hlinmap_nonsingular : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    LinearMap.det (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) ≠ 0 := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx
  rw [LinearMap.det_eq_matrix_det basis.toBasis]
  exact hdet_nonzero t ht0 htC x hx
```

---

## The Key Challenge — Step 3

The diagonal dominance condition requires:

$$\sum_{j \neq k} |t \cdot (Dg)_{kj}| < |1 + t \cdot (Dg)_{kk}|$$

For small `t`, the left side is `O(t)` and the right side is `1 + O(t)`, so the condition holds. The precise bound needs:

```lean
-- Left side: ∑ j ≠ k, |t * (Dg)_kj| = t * ∑ j ≠ k, |(Dg)_kj| ≤ t * n * ‖Dg‖
-- Right side: |1 + t * (Dg)_kk| ≥ 1 - t * ‖Dg‖
-- Condition: t * n * ‖Dg‖ < 1 - t * ‖Dg‖
-- i.e. t * (n + 1) * ‖Dg‖ < 1
-- i.e. t < 1 / ((n + 1) * ‖Dg‖)
```

So `t0 = 1 / ((n + 1) * M)` where `M` bounds `‖fderiv ℝ g x‖` on the ball.

---

## Revised `t0`

```lean
obtain ⟨M, hM0, hM⟩ := hfderiv_bound
let t0 : ℝ := 1 / ((n + 1) * (M + 1))
have ht0_pos : 0 < t0 := by positivity
```

- `Basis.toMatrix_self` gives `basis.toBasis.toMatrix (⇑basis.toBasis) = 1`
- `Matrix.one_apply` gives `(1 : Matrix n n ℝ) k k = if k = k then 1 else 0`
- `if k = k` reduces to `true` so the entry is `1`

## What to Check

The issue is likely that `⇑b` is not definitionally equal to `b.toBasis.equivFun.toFun` or `b.toBasis.repr`. Check what `⇑b` unfolds to:

```lean
#check (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin n) ℝ E)
#check (⇑b : Fin n → E)  -- b as a function gives basis vectors
```

The coercion `⇑b : Fin n → E` gives the **basis vectors**, while `toMatrix` expects the **coordinate functions**. So the goal may be:

```lean
b.toBasis.toMatrix (fun i => b i) k k = 1
```

where `b i` is the `i`-th basis vector, not the `i`-th coordinate function. Try:

```lean

  exact Module.Basis.toMatrix_self b.toBasis
simp [hself, Matrix.one_apply]
```

## If That Fails

Check the exact type of `b.toBasis.toMatrix`:

```lean
#check @Basis.toMatrix
-- Basis.toMatrix : Basis ι R M → (ι → M) → Matrix ι ι R
```

The second argument should be `ι → M`, i.e. a family of vectors. So `b.toBasis.toMatrix (⇑b)` takes the basis vectors of `b` and expresses them in terms of `b.toBasis`, which should give the identity. The mismatch may be between `⇑b` and `⇑b.toBasis` — try:

```lean
have hcoe : (⇑b : Fin n → E) = (⇑b.toBasis : Fin n → E) := by
  ext i; simp [OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis]
rw [hcoe]
exact Module.Basis.toMatrix_self b.toBasis |>.symm ▸ Matrix.one_apply_eq k
```

## Why This Works

- `Matrix.one_apply` gives `(1 : Matrix n n ℝ) k j = if k = j then 1 else 0`

[05/15/2026 15:20:00 +00:00] User:
hJ_diag : ∀ (t : ℝ) (x : E) (k : Fin n), J t x k k = 1 + t * (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis) (↑(fderiv ℝ g x)) k k
hJ_offdiag : ∀ (t : ℝ) (x : E) (k j : Fin n), k ≠ j → J t x k j = t * (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis) (↑(fderiv ℝ g x)) k j
now want to pick a suitable t0 to bound the sum of the non-diagonal entires in each row and then use

det_ne_zero_of_sum_row_lt_diag

Response:
The diagonal dominance condition requires for each row `k`:

$$\sum_{j \neq k} |J_t(x)_{kj}| < |J_t(x)_{kk}|$$

Using `hJ_diag` and `hJ_offdiag`, this becomes:

$$t \sum_{j \neq k} |(Dg_x)_{kj}| < |1 + t \cdot (Dg_x)_{kk}|$$

---

## Step 1 — Bound the Matrix Entries of `fderiv ℝ g`

```lean
-- Let A be the matrix of fderiv g x
let A : ℝ → E → Matrix (Fin n) (Fin n) ℝ := fun t x =>
  LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)
-- Bound all entries of A uniformly on the ball
have hA_bound : ∃ M : ℝ, 0 ≤ M ∧ ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    ∀ k j : Fin n, ‖A 0 x k j‖ ≤ M := by
  have hcont : ContinuousOn (fun x => ‖(LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis
      (fderiv ℝ g x))‖) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    (hg_cont_diff.continuous_fderiv (by norm_num)).continuousOn.norm
  obtain ⟨x, _, hmax⟩ := (isCompact_closedBall (0 : E) 1).exists_isMaxOn
    (by simp) hcont
  refine ⟨‖LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)‖,
    norm_nonneg _, fun y hy k j => ?_⟩
  calc ‖A 0 y k j‖ 
      ≤ ‖LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g y)‖ := 
        Matrix.norm_entry_le_entrywise_sup_norm _ _ _
    _ ≤ ‖LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)‖ := hmax hy
```

---

## Step 2 — Pick `t0`

```lean
obtain ⟨M, hM0, hM⟩ := hA_bound
-- Pick t0 small enough that t * n * M < 1 - t * M
-- i.e. t * (n + 1) * M < 1
-- i.e. t < 1 / ((n + 1) * (M + 1))
let t0 : ℝ := 1 / ((n + 1) * (M + 1))
have ht0_pos : 0 < t0 := by positivity
```

---

## Step 3 — Show Diagonal Dominance

```lean
have hdiag_dom : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, ∀ k : Fin n,
    ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖ < ‖J t x k k‖ := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx k
  -- Rewrite using hJ_diag and hJ_offdiag
  have hdiag := hJ_diag t x k
  have hoffdiag := fun j hj => hJ_offdiag t x k j (Finset.ne_of_mem_erase hj)
  rw [hdiag]
  -- Bound the off-diagonal sum
  have hsum_bound : ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖ ≤ t * n * M := by
    calc ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖
        = ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖t * A 0 x k j‖ := by
            congr 1; ext j
            rw [hoffdiag j (Finset.mem_univ j |>.mp (by simp))]
            simp [norm_mul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
      _ ≤ ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, t * M := by
            apply Finset.sum_le_sum
            intro j _
            apply mul_le_mul_of_nonneg_left (hM x hx k j) ht0
      _ = t * n * M := by
            simp [Finset.card_erase_of_mem, Finset.card_fin]
            ring
  -- Bound the diagonal
  have hdiag_bound : t * n * M < ‖1 + t * A 0 x k k‖ := by
    have : ‖1 + t * A 0 x k k‖ ≥ 1 - t * M := by
      calc ‖1 + t * A 0 x k k‖ 
          ≥ |1| - ‖t * A 0 x k k‖ := by
              rw [← Real.norm_of_nonneg (by norm_num)]
              exact norm_sub_norm_le _ _
        _ = 1 - t * ‖A 0 x k k‖ := by
              simp [norm_mul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
        _ ≥ 1 - t * M := by
              linarith [hM x hx k k]
    have ht_bound : t * n * M < 1 - t * M := by
      have : t * ((n + 1) * (M + 1)) < 1 := by
        calc t * ((n + 1) * (M + 1)) 
            < t0 * ((n + 1) * (M + 1)) := by
                apply mul_lt_mul_of_pos_right htC
                positivity
          _ = 1 := by unfold_let t0; field_simp
      nlinarith [Fintype.card_fin n]
    linarith
  linarith
```

---

## Step 4 — Apply `det_ne_zero_of_sum_row_lt_diag`

```lean
have hdet_nonzero : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, (J t x).det ≠ 0 := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx
  apply Matrix.det_ne_zero_of_sum_row_lt_diag
  exact hdiag_dom t ht0 htC x hx
```

[05/15/2026 15:31:22 +00:00] User:

      J t x k j = t * ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis) (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j := by

Response:
The issue is in how `hoffdiag` is being applied. `hJ_offdiag` takes `k ≠ j` as a hypothesis but we are trying to get it from `Finset.mem_erase`. Let's fix the application:

---

## Fix

```lean
have hsum_bound : ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖ ≤ t * n * M := by
  calc ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖
      = ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖t * ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis)
          (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖ := by
          congr 1; ext j
          congr 1
          apply hJ_offdiag t x k j
          exact Finset.ne_of_mem_erase (by simp)
    _ ≤ ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, t * M := by
          apply Finset.sum_le_sum
          intro j _
          rw [norm_mul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
          exact mul_le_mul_of_nonneg_left (hM x hx k j) ht0
    _ = t * n * M := by
          simp [Finset.card_erase_of_mem, Finset.card_fin]
          ring
```

---

## The Key Fix

`Finset.ne_of_mem_erase` has signature:
```lean
Finset.ne_of_mem_erase : a ∈ s.erase b → a ≠ b
```

But we need `k ≠ j`, not `j ≠ k`. So we need:

```lean
exact (Finset.ne_of_mem_erase (by simp)).symm
```

Or use `Finset.mem_erase.mp` directly:

```lean
apply hJ_offdiag t x k j
intro hkj
simp [hkj] at *
```

[05/15/2026 15:35:37 +00:00] User:
instead of calc steps, let's use a series of haves and rw, with the intention of maybe turning these into a calc later

Response:
```lean
have hsum_bound : ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖ ≤ t * n * M := by
  -- Rewrite each entry using hJ_offdiag
  have hentries : ∀ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k,
      ‖J t x k j‖ = t * ‖((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis)
        (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖ := by
    intro j hj
    have hkj : k ≠ j := (Finset.mem_erase.mp hj).1
    rw [hJ_offdiag t x k j hkj, norm_mul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
  -- Rewrite the sum using hentries
  have hsum_eq : ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖ =
      ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, t * ‖((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis)
        (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖ := by
    congr 1; ext j
    by_cases hj : j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k
    · exact hentries j hj
    · rfl
  -- Bound each entry by t * M
  have hentry_bound : ∀ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k,
      t * ‖((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis) (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖ ≤ t * M := by
    intro j _
    apply mul_le_mul_of_nonneg_left _ ht0
    exact hM x hx k j
  -- Bound the sum by t * n * M
  have hsum_le : ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, t * ‖((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis)
      (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖ ≤ t * n * M := by
    have hcard : (Finset.univ.erase k).card = n - 1 := by
      simp [Finset.card_erase_of_mem]
    calc ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, t * ‖((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis)
            (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖
        ≤ ∑ _ ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, t * M :=
            Finset.sum_le_sum hentry_bound
      _ = (Finset.univ.erase k).card • (t * M) := by
            rw [Finset.sum_const]
      _ ≤ t * n * M := by
            simp [hcard]
            nlinarith [Nat.sub_le n 1]
  rw [hsum_eq]
  exact hsum_le
```

[05/15/2026 15:49:04 +00:00] User:
rfl didn't close the goal after by_cases, the goal is

The `rfl` was wrong — in the `hj : j ∉ Finset.univ.erase k` case we still need to prove the equality, and `j ∉ Finset.univ.erase k` combined with `j ∈ Finset.univ` actually means `j = k`, not `j ≠ k`. Let's fix the approach:

---

## Fix — Remove the `by_cases`

The `by_cases` is unnecessary since `congr 1; ext j` gives us a `j` without membership, and we should use `Finset.sum_congr` instead:

```lean
have hsum_eq : ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖ =
    ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, t * ‖((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis)
      (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖ := by
  apply Finset.sum_congr rfl
  intro j hj
  have hkj : k ≠ j := (Finset.mem_erase.mp hj).1
  rw [hJ_offdiag t x k j hkj, norm_mul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
```

---

## Why `Finset.sum_congr` Is Better Here

`Finset.sum_congr rfl` gives us `j` together with `hj : j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k` for free, so we can immediately extract `k ≠ j` from `hj` using `Finset.mem_erase.mp`. This avoids the `by_cases` entirely and makes the proof cleaner.

- `push_cast` normalises the natural number cast `↑(n - 1)` into `↑n - 1` or handles the coercion cleanly
- `Nat.cast_le.mpr hn` gives `(↑(n - 1) : ℝ) ≤ ↑n`
- `nlinarith` then closes `↑(n-1) * (t * M) ≤ t * ↑n * M` from:

## Fix Using `norm_sub_norm_le`

```lean
have hrev : ‖(1 : ℝ)‖ - ‖t * A 0 x k k‖ ≤ ‖1 + t * A 0 x k k‖ := by
  have := norm_sub_norm_le (1 + t * A 0 x k k) (t * A 0 x k k)
  simp only [add_sub_cancel_right] at this
  linarith
```

---

## Why This Works

`norm_sub_norm_le (a + b) b` gives:

$$\|a + b\| - \|b\| \leq \|(a + b) - b\| = \|a\|$$

Rearranging:

$$\|a\| - \|b\| \leq \|a + b\|$$

with `a = 1` and `b = t * A 0 x k k`, which is exactly what we need. The `simp only [add_sub_cancel_right]` simplifies `(1 + t * A 0 x k k) - (t * A 0 x k k)` to `1`.

failed to synthesize instance of type class
  Norm (Matrix (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ)

Response:
Matrices do not have a canonical `Norm` instance in Mathlib. We need to use a specific matrix norm. The simplest fix is to bound the entries directly using the operator norm of the linear map instead:

---

## Fix — Bound via Operator Norm of `fderiv ℝ g x`

```lean
have hA_bound : ∃ M : ℝ, 0 ≤ M ∧ ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    ∀ k j : Fin n, ‖A 0 x k j‖ ≤ M := by
  -- Bound the operator norm of fderiv g on the ball
  have hcont : ContinuousOn (fun x => ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    (hg_cont_diff.continuous_fderiv (by norm_num)).continuousOn.norm
  obtain ⟨x, hx, hmax⟩ := (isCompact_closedBall (0 : E) 1).exists_isMaxOn
    (by simp) hcont
  refine ⟨‖fderiv ℝ g x‖, norm_nonneg _, fun y hy k j => ?_⟩
  -- Each matrix entry is bounded by the operator norm
  have hentry : ‖A 0 y k j‖ ≤ ‖fderiv ℝ g y‖ := by
    simp only [A, LinearMap.toMatrix_apply]
    exact ContinuousLinearMap.le_opNorm (fderiv ℝ g y) (b.toBasis j)
      |>.trans (by simp [mul_comm])
  exact hentry.trans (hmax hy)
```

---

## Why This Works

Each matrix entry `A 0 y k j` is:

$$A_{kj} = \langle e_k, Dg_y(e_j) \rangle$$

which is bounded by `‖Dg_y‖ · ‖e_j‖ = ‖Dg_y‖` since the basis vectors have norm `1`. The operator norm `‖fderiv ℝ g y‖` is continuous on the compact ball, so it attains its maximum `M`.

## The `sorry` in `hstep2`

`hstep2` says the norm of the coordinate representation is at most the norm of the vector. This follows from the fact that `b.toBasis.repr` is a linear isometry:

```lean
  have hstep2 : ‖b.toBasis.repr (↑(fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))‖ ≤
      ‖(fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)‖ := by
    have := b.repr.norm_map ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))
    simp only [LinearIsometryEquiv.norm_map] at this
    linarith
```

Or more directly since `b.repr` is an isometry:

```lean
  have hstep2 : ‖b.toBasis.repr (↑(fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))‖ =
      ‖(fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)‖ :=
    b.repr.norm_map _
```

Which gives equality rather than just `≤`, making the final `linarith` easier.

[05/16/2026 08:41:35 +00:00] User:
what exactly does the error
typeclass instance problem is stuck, it is often due to metavariables
  (i : ?m.1712) → SeminormedAddCommGroup
mean

Response:
## What the Error Means

The error means Lean is trying to find a `SeminormedAddCommGroup` instance for some type `?m.1713 i`, but the type `?m.1713` is still an **unknown metavariable** — Lean has not yet figured out what type family it is working with.

---

## Why It Happens

`PiLp.norm_apply_le` has signature:

```lean
theorem PiLp.norm_apply_le (f : PiLp p α) (i : ι) : ‖f i‖ ≤ ‖f‖
```

where `α : ι → Type*` is a type family. Lean needs to know:
- What `ι` is — the index type
- What `α i` is — the type at each index
- That each `α i` has a `SeminormedAddCommGroup` instance

When any of these are unknown metavariables `?m`, Lean cannot search for the instance and gets stuck.

---

## In Your Specific Case

The expression `b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b j))` has type `EuclideanSpace ℝ (Fin n)`, which is `PiLp 2 (fun _ : Fin n => ℝ)`. Lean needs to unify:

```
ι     := Fin n
α i   := ℝ
p     := 2
```

But without explicit annotations, one or more of these remain as metavariables, causing the instance search to fail.

---

## The Fix

Tell Lean all three pieces explicitly:

```lean
@PiLp.norm_apply_le 2 (Fin n) (fun _ : Fin n => ℝ) 
  (fun _ => inferInstance)   -- NNNorm instance
  (fun _ => inferInstance)   -- SeminormedAddCommGroup instance
  (b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b j))) k
```

Or use `show` to restate the goal in a form where Lean can infer everything:

```lean
have hstep1 : ‖b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b j)) k‖ ≤
    ‖b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b j))‖ := by
  show ‖(b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b j)) : PiLp 2 (fun _ : Fin n => ℝ)) k‖ ≤
    ‖(b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b j)) : PiLp 2 (fun _ : Fin n => ℝ))‖
  exact PiLp.norm_apply_le _ k
```

The `show` forces the type to be `PiLp 2 (fun _ : Fin n => ℝ)`, which resolves all the metavariables and allows the instance search to succeed.

Check if `b j` and `b.toBasis j` are definitionally equal:

```lean
have hbeq : b j = b.toBasis j := by
  simp [OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis]
```

---

## Fix — Rewrite to Align the Terms

```lean
have hbeq : b j = b.toBasis j := by
  simp [OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis]
rw [hbeq] at hstep1
linarith [hstep1, hstep2, hstep3, hstep4, hM]
```

---

## If `linarith` Still Fails

Provide the chain explicitly:

```lean
have hbeq : b j = b.toBasis j := by
  simp [OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis]
rw [hbeq] at hstep1
have hchain : ‖(b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))).ofLp k‖ ≤ M := by
  calc ‖(b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))).ofLp k‖
      ≤ ‖b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))‖ := hstep1
    _ = ‖(fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)‖ := hstep2
    _ ≤ ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ * ‖b.toBasis j‖ := hstep3
    _ = ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ * 1 := by rw [hstep4]
    _ = ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ := mul_one _
    _ ≤ M := hM
exact hchain
```

[05/16/2026 09:13:30 +00:00] User:
For 0 le t le t0, the inverse function theorem gives us that f_t maps the interior of B^n into an open set, call it G_t contained in B^n

what is the way to use the inverse function theorem in lean to give this

Response:
The relevant Mathlib theorem is:

```lean
#check HasStrictFDerivAt.localInverse
#check HasStrictFDerivAt.isLocalHomeomorph
```

But the most directly useful one for showing the image is open is:

```lean
#check HasStrictFDerivAt.image_mem_nhds
```

---

## The Key Theorems

```lean
-- If f has a strict derivative at x and the derivative is invertible,
-- then f maps neighbourhoods of x to neighbourhoods of f x
#check HasStrictFDerivAt.image_mem_nhds

-- A C^1 function with invertible derivative is a local homeomorphism
#check ContDiffAt.isLocalHomeomorphOn
```

---

## What We Need

For each `x ∈ interior (closedBall 0 1)` and `t ∈ [0, t0]`:

1. `f_t t` has a strict Fréchet derivative at `x`
2. The derivative is invertible (from `hdet_nonzero`)
3. Therefore `f_t t` maps a neighbourhood of `x` to a neighbourhood of `f_t t x`
4. The union of these neighbourhoods is `G_t`

---

## Step 1 — Get `HasStrictFDerivAt` from `ContDiff`

```lean
have hft_strict_fderiv : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
    HasStrictFDerivAt (f_t t)
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx
  apply ContDiff.hasStrictFDerivAt _ (n := 1)
  · -- f_t t is C^1
    unfold_let f_t g
    apply ContDiff.add contDiff_id
    apply ContDiff.smul contDiff_const
    exact hf_diff.comp contDiff_id |>.sub contDiff_id
  · norm_num
```

---

## Step 2 — The Derivative is a Continuous Linear Equivalence

```lean
have hft_equiv : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
    IsUnit (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx
  exact hft_nonsingular t ht0 htC x (interior_subset hx)
```

---

## Step 3 — Define `G_t` as the Image of the Interior

```lean
have hGt_open : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    IsOpen (f_t t '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) := by
  intro t ht0 htC
  apply isOpen_iff_mem_nhds.mpr
  intro y ⟨x, hx, hxy⟩
  rw [← hxy]
  -- Get the strict derivative
  have hstrict := hft_strict_fderiv t ht0 htC x hx
  -- Get the unit
  obtain ⟨u, hu⟩ := hft_equiv t ht0 htC x hx
  -- The image of a neighbourhood is a neighbourhood
  have hcle : (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).IsInvertible := by
    exact ⟨u, hu⟩
  exact hstrict.image_mem_nhds (interior_mem_nhds.mpr hx) hcle
```

---

## Step 4 — `G_t` is Contained in `B^n`

```lean
have hGt_subset : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t ≤ 1 →
    f_t t '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) ⊆ closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by
  intro t ht0 ht1 y ⟨x, hx, hxy⟩
  rw [← hxy]
  exact hft_maps t ht0 ht1 (interior_subset hx)
```

---

## The Relevant Mathlib Theorem

The most direct theorem connecting invertible derivative to open image is:

```lean
#check IsLocalHomeomorph.isOpen_image
#check HasStrictFDerivAt.localHomeomorph
```

Which gives:

```lean
have hft_local_homeo : ∀ x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
    ∃ (s : Set E), s ∈ nhds x ∧ IsOpen (f_t t '' s) := by
  intro x hx
  have hstrict := hft_strict_fderiv t ht0 htC x hx
  obtain ⟨u, hu⟩ := hft_equiv t ht0 htC x hx
  exact ⟨_, hstrict.image_mem_nhds (interior_mem_nhds.mpr hx),
    hstrict.localHomeomorph_source_mem_nhds⟩
```

---

## Summary

| Step | Mathlib Tool |
|---|---|
| `C^1` → strict derivative | `ContDiff.hasStrictFDerivAt` |
| Invertible derivative | `hft_nonsingular` via `hdet_nonzero` |
| Image of neighbourhood is open | `HasStrictFDerivAt.image_mem_nhds` |
| Union gives open set `G_t` | `isOpen_iUnion` |
| `G_t ⊆ B^n` | `hft_maps` |

Given a function f with an invertible derivative, returns a function that is locally inverse to f.

would this be appropriate?

Response:
Yes, `HasStrictFDerivAt.localInverse` is the right tool. It gives a local inverse, and from the local inverse we can conclude the image is open. The key supporting theorems are:

```lean
#check HasStrictFDerivAt.localInverse_apply_image
-- f (localInverse f f' a hf (f a)) = f a  (locally)

#check HasStrictFDerivAt.eventually_left_inverse
-- eventually, localInverse f f' a hf (f x) = x

#check HasStrictFDerivAt.map_nhds_eq_of_equiv
-- f maps nhds a to nhds (f a)
```

The most relevant one for showing the image is open is:

```lean
#check HasStrictFDerivAt.map_nhds_eq_of_equiv
```

---

## The Setup

To use `HasStrictFDerivAt.localInverse`, the derivative must be given as a `ContinuousLinearEquiv` `E ≃L[𝕜] F`, not just a `ContinuousLinearMap`. So we need to extract the equivalence from `hft_nonsingular`:

---

## Step 1 — Extract the `ContinuousLinearEquiv`

```lean
have hft_equiv : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
    ∃ (e : E ≃L[ℝ] E),
    (e : E →L[ℝ] E) = ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx
  obtain ⟨u, hu⟩ := hft_nonsingular t ht0 htC x (interior_subset hx)
  exact ⟨u.toContinuousLinearEquiv, by simp [hu]⟩
```

---

## Step 2 — Get `HasStrictFDerivAt`

```lean
have hft_strict : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
    HasStrictFDerivAt (f_t t)
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x := by
  intro t ht0 htC x hx
  apply ContDiff.hasStrictFDerivAt (n := 1)
  · unfold_let f_t g
    exact (contDiff_id.add
      (contDiff_const.smul (hf_diff.sub contDiff_id)))
  · norm_num
```

---

## Step 3 — Apply `localInverse` to Get Open Image

```lean
have hGt_open : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    IsOpen (f_t t '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) := by
  intro t ht0 htC
  apply isOpen_iff_mem_nhds.mpr
  intro y ⟨x, hx, hxy⟩
  rw [← hxy]
  obtain ⟨e, he⟩ := hft_equiv t ht0 htC x hx
  have hstrict := hft_strict t ht0 htC x hx
  -- Rewrite derivative as the equiv
  rw [← he] at hstrict
  -- localInverse gives us a neighbourhood mapping
  have hlocal := HasStrictFDerivAt.localInverse (f_t t) e x hstrict
  -- The image of a neighbourhood of x under f_t t is a neighbourhood of f_t t x
  have hmem : f_t t '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) ∈ nhds (f_t t x) := by
    apply hstrict.map_nhds_eq_of_equiv
    exact interior_mem_nhds.mpr hx
  exact hmem
```

---

## Key Issue — `map_nhds_eq_of_equiv`

Check if this exists:

```lean
#check HasStrictFDerivAt.map_nhds_eq_of_equiv
```

If not, the alternative is:

```lean
#check HasStrictFDerivAt.isLocalHomeomorph
```

Which gives a local homeomorphism, and local homeomorphisms map open sets to open sets:

```lean
have hGt_open : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    IsOpen (f_t t '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) := by
  intro t ht0 htC
  have : IsLocalHomeomorph (f_t t) := by
    apply isLocalHomeomorph_iff_isLocalHomeomorphOn.mpr
    intro x hx
    obtain ⟨e, he⟩ := hft_equiv t ht0 htC x (mem_interior_iff_mem_nhds.mp hx |>.1)
    have hstrict := hft_strict t ht0 htC x hx
    rw [← he] at hstrict
    exact ⟨hstrict.localHomeomorph (f_t t) e x, 
      hstrict.localHomeomorph_mem_nhds, 
      hstrict.localHomeomorph_target_mem_nhds⟩
  exact this.isOpen_image isOpen_interior
```

`HasStrictFDerivAt.map_nhds_eq_of_surj` is the right one since we are in the multivariable case (`FDeriv` not `Deriv`). The derivative being an isomorphism implies it is surjective.
