## Step 1 — Show the Derivative is Surjective

```lean
have hft_surj : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
    (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).range = ⊤ := by
```

```lean
have hGt_open : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    IsOpen (f_t t '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) := by
  intro t ht0 htC
  apply isOpen_iff_mem_nhds.mpr
  intro y ⟨x, hx, hxy⟩

  have hstrict := hft_strict t ht0 htC x hx
  have hsurj := hft_surj t ht0 htC x hx
  -- map f_t t (𝓝 x) = 𝓝 (f_t t x)
  have hmap := hstrict.map_nhds_eq_of_surj hsurj
  -- The image of interior (closedBall 0 1) is in nhds (f_t t x)
  rw [← hmap]
  apply Filter.image_mem_map
  exact interior_mem_nhds.mpr hx
```

[05/16/2026 09:27:28 +00:00] User:
statement and proof of hft_nonsingular

Response:
We need to show that the derivative of `f_t t` at `x` is a unit in the ring of continuous linear maps, using the diagonal dominance result.

---

## Statement

```lean
have hft_nonsingular : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    IsUnit (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) := by
```

---

## Proof

```lean
  intro t ht0 htC x hx
  -- Get the matrix representation
  have hdet := hdet_nonzero t ht0 htC x hx
  -- Connect matrix det to linear map det
  have hlindet : LinearMap.det
      (↑(ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) ≠ 0 := by
    rw [LinearMap.det_toMatrix b.toBasis]
    convert hdet using 2
    simp [J, LinearMap.toMatrix_add, LinearMap.toMatrix_smul]
  -- A linear map with nonzero determinant is a unit
  rwa [LinearMap.isUnit_iff_det_ne_zero] at hlindet
```

---

## Key Lemmas Used

| Lemma | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `hdet_nonzero` | Matrix determinant is nonzero |
| `LinearMap.det_toMatrix` | Connects `LinearMap.det` to matrix det |
| `LinearMap.isUnit_iff_det_ne_zero` | Nonzero det implies unit |

---

## If `LinearMap.isUnit_iff_det_ne_zero` Does Not Exist

```lean
#check LinearMap.isUnit_iff_det_ne_zero
-- or
#check Matrix.isUnit_iff_det_ne_zero
```

Try the matrix version instead:

```lean
  have hmat_unit : IsUnit (J t x) := by
    rwa [Matrix.isUnit_iff_det_ne_zero]
  -- Lift to the linear map
  exact (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis).isUnit_iff.mp hmat_unit
```


## Breaking Down the Steps

- `obtain ⟨u, hu⟩` — extracts the unit `u` and proof `↑u = id + t • fderiv ℝ g x`
- `rw [LinearMap.range_eq_top]` — converts `range = ⊤` to `Function.Surjective`
- `rw [← hu]` — rewrites the goal to use `↑u` instead
- `ContinuousLinearMap.IsInvertible.surjective ⟨u, hu⟩` — applies the theorem, where `⟨u, hu⟩ : (↑u).IsInvertible`

---

## Note on `IsInvertible`

`ContinuousLinearMap.IsInvertible` is defined as:

```lean
structure ContinuousLinearMap.IsInvertible (f : M →L[R] M₂) where
  inv : M₂ →L[R] M
  ...
```

So `⟨u, hu⟩` constructs the `IsInvertible` instance from the unit `u` with `hu : ↑u = f`.

[05/16/2026 17:06:24 +00:00] User:

    Set.MapsTo (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by

this should follow from ft being an interpolation between f and g, i.e. a point of the image is a weighted average of two points that are each themsleves in B^n

Response:
The key insight is that `f_t t x = x + t • (f x - x) = (1 - t) • x + t • f x`, which is a convex combination of `x ∈ closedBall 0 1` and `f x ∈ sphere 0 1 ⊆ closedBall 0 1`.

---

## Proof

```lean
have hft_maps : ∀ t ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) 1,
    Set.MapsTo (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  intro t ⟨ht0, ht1⟩ x hx
  simp only [f_t, g]
  -- Rewrite as convex combination
  have hconv : x + t • (f x - x) = (1 - t) • x + t • f x := by
    simp [smul_sub, add_comm]
    module_tac
  rw [hconv]
  -- Both x and f x are in closedBall 0 1
  have hfx : f x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by
    have := hf_maps (Set.mem_image_of_mem f hx)
    exact mem_closedBall.mpr (mem_sphere.mp this).le
  -- The convex combination is in closedBall 0 1
  apply convex_closedBall (0 : E) 1
  · exact hx
  · exact hfx
  · linarith
  · exact ht0
  · linarith
```

---

## Key Steps

### `hconv` — Rewrite as Convex Combination

$$x + t(f(x) - x) = (1-t)x + tf(x)$$

### `hfx` — `f x ∈ closedBall 0 1`

`f` maps `closedBall 0 1` to `sphere 0 1` by `hf_maps`, and `sphere 0 1 ⊆ closedBall 0 1`.

### `convex_closedBall` — Convexity

`convex_closedBall` says `closedBall 0 1` is convex, so any convex combination of two points in it is also in it. The arguments are:
- `hx : x ∈ closedBall 0 1`
- `hfx : f x ∈ closedBall 0 1`
- `1 - t ≥ 0` from `ht1`
- `t ≥ 0` from `ht0`
- `(1 - t) + t = 1` by `linarith`

## The Key Definitions

| Name | Definition | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| `G_t` | `f_t t00 '' interior (closedBall 0 1)` | The open set |
| `e` | Point in `closedBall 0 1 \ G_t` | Starting point outside `G_t` |
| `p` | Point in `G_t` | Endpoint inside `G_t` |
| `seg s` | `e + s • (p - e)` | Line segment from `e` to `p` |
| `b` | `sSup {s | seg s ∈ G_t}` | Exit point of segment from `G_t` |

---

## The Two `sorry`s

### `hGt_ne_ball`

`G_t ≠ closedBall 0 1` because `G_t` is open and `closedBall 0 1` is not, or because `f_t t00` maps into the interior and misses the boundary.

### `Set.exists_mem_not_mem_of_ne_univ`

This lemma may not exist. The correct approach is:

```lean

  by_contra h
  push_neg at h
  have : closedBall (0 : E) 1 ⊆ G_t := h
  exact hGt_ne_ball (le_antisymm hGt_subset this)
```

```lean
    ∃ e ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, e ∉ G_t t := by
```

Wait — this is not quite the right statement. The point `seg t ht0 htC ht1 (b t ht0 htC ht1)` is the supremum of the set `S`, and we want to show it is in the image of `f_t t`. Let me restate:

---

## Correct Statement

`b` is the supremum of `{s | seg s ∈ G_t}`, and `G_t = f_t t '' interior (closedBall 0 1) ⊆ f_t t '' closedBall 0 1`. So the boundary point `seg (b t ...)` should be in the closed image:

```lean
have hb_in_image : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    ∃ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    f_t t x = seg t ht0 htC ht1 (b t ht0 htC ht1) := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  -- The image of closedBall under f_t t is compact hence closed
  have hclosed := hft_image_closed t ht0 ht1.le
  -- G_t ⊆ f_t t '' closedBall 0 1
  have hGt_sub : G_t t ⊆ f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by
    intro y ⟨x, hx, hxy⟩
    exact ⟨x, interior_subset hx, hxy⟩
  -- The supremum is a limit of points in G_t
  -- which are in the closed image, so the limit is also in the closed image
  have hmem : seg t ht0 htC ht1 (b t ht0 htC ht1) ∈
      f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by
    apply hclosed.mem_of_closure_mem
    apply closure_mono hGt_sub
    -- b is in the closure of {s | seg s ∈ G_t}
    -- so seg b is in the closure of G_t
    apply ContinuousAt.image_closure
    · exact (hseg_cont t ht0 htC ht1).continuousAt
    · exact isClosed_Icc.closure_subset (hb_mem_Icc t ht0 htC ht1)
  exact hmem
```

---

## More Direct Version

Since `f_t t '' closedBall 0 1` is compact and `G_t t ⊆ f_t t '' closedBall 0 1`, and `seg (b t ...)` is a limit point of `G_t t`:

```lean
have hb_in_image : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    ∃ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    f_t t x = seg t ht0 htC ht1 (b t ht0 htC ht1) := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  have hclosed := hft_image_closed t ht0 ht1.le
  -- seg b is a limit of points in S hence in G_t
  have hlim : seg t ht0 htC ht1 (b t ht0 htC ht1) ∈
      closure (seg t ht0 htC ht1 '' S t ht0 htC ht1) := by
    apply subset_closure
    apply Set.mem_image_of_mem
    exact csSup_mem (hS_nonempty t ht0 htC ht1) (hS_bddAbove t ht0 htC ht1)
  have hGt_sub_image : seg t ht0 htC ht1 '' S t ht0 htC ht1 ⊆
      f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by
    rintro y ⟨s, ⟨_, hs⟩, rfl⟩
    exact hGt_sub t ht0 htC.le hs
  have hmem := hclosed.closure_subset (closure_mono hGt_sub_image hlim)
  exact hmem
```

[05/17/2026 16:08:06 +00:00] User:
a strange error has occurred, 

after including

have hseg_cont : ∀ t ht0 htC ht1, Continuous (seg t ht0 htC ht1) := by
    intro t ht0 htC ht1
    unfold seg
    fun_prop
in particular even if fun_prop is replaced with sorry, for every other have and let statement in the theorem, the error

don't know how to synthesize placeholder
context:
appears



Response:
This is a known Lean 4 issue where a `let` or `have` with dependent arguments causes Lean to lose track of metavariables throughout the rest of the proof. The issue is that `seg` is defined as a `let` with multiple proof arguments `ht0 htC ht1`, and `hseg_cont` references it with those arguments, causing Lean to get confused about implicit arguments everywhere else.

---

## The Fix — Use `show` to Restate the Type Explicitly

```lean
have hseg_cont : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    Continuous (fun s : ℝ => e t ht0 htC ht1 + s • (g t ht0 htC.le - e t ht0 htC ht1)) := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  fun_prop
```

By inlining the definition of `seg` rather than referencing it by name, Lean does not need to unify the dependent arguments.

---

## Root Cause

The problem is that `seg` is a `let` binding with type:

```
seg : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 → ℝ → E
```

When Lean sees `seg t ht0 htC ht1` in `hseg_cont`, it tries to elaborate the proof arguments `ht0 htC ht1` and creates metavariables for their types. These metavariables then leak into the rest of the proof context, causing the `don't know how to synthesize placeholder` errors everywhere.

---

## General Rule

Avoid referencing `let` bindings that take **proof arguments** in `have` statements. Either:

1. **Inline the definition** as shown above
2. **Use `def`** outside the theorem instead of `let` inside
3. **Avoid proof-valued arguments** in `let` bindings by separating the data from the proofs

[05/17/2026 16:27:09 +00:00] User:
inlining seg still lead to the same errors

Response:
The issue is deeper — it is the `let` bindings with proof arguments (`e`, `g`, `seg`) that are causing the metavariable leakage throughout the proof. The fix is to replace the problematic `let` bindings with `obtain` or `have` statements that extract the data without carrying proof arguments.

---

## The Core Problem

```lean
-- These let bindings carry proof arguments and cause metavariable leakage
let e := fun t ht0 htC ht1 => ...
let g := fun t ht0 htC => ...
let seg := fun t ht0 htC ht1 s => ...
```

---

## Fix — Work at a Fixed `t` 

Instead of quantifying over all `t` with proof arguments, fix `t = t00` and work with concrete values:

```lean
-- Fix t = t00 throughout
let t := t00
have ht0 : 0 ≤ t := ht00_nonneg
have htC : t < t0 := ht00_lt
have ht1 : t < 1 := by linarith
-- Now extract e, g, seg as concrete terms without proof arguments
obtain ⟨e, he_ball, he_Gt⟩ := hGt_ne t ht0 htC ht1
let p := (hGt_nonempty t ht0 htC.le).some
have hp : p ∈ G_t t := (hGt_nonempty t ht0 htC.le).some_mem
let seg : ℝ → E := fun s => e + s • (p - e)
have hseg_cont : Continuous seg := by unfold_let seg; fun_prop
have hseg0 : seg 0 = e := by simp [seg]
have hseg1 : seg 1 = p := by simp [seg]
let S : Set ℝ := {s ∈ Set.Icc 0 1 | seg s ∈ G_t t}
let b : ℝ := sSup S
```

---

## Why This Works

By fixing `t = t00` upfront, all the subsequent definitions (`e`, `p`, `seg`, `S`, `b`) become concrete terms with no proof arguments. This eliminates the metavariable leakage entirely.

---

## Restructuring the Proof

The overall structure becomes:

```lean
-- 1. Establish all universal statements first
have hGt_open : ∀ t ..., IsOpen (G_t t) := ...
have hGt_subset : ∀ t ..., G_t t ⊆ closedBall 0 1 := ...
have hGt_nonempty : ∀ t ..., (G_t t).Nonempty := ...
have hGt_ne_ball : ∀ t ..., G_t t ≠ closedBall 0 1 := ...
have hft_nonsingular : ∀ t ..., IsUnit (...) := ...

-- 2. Fix t = t00 and work concretely
let t := t00
...
-- 3. Define e, p, seg, S, b concretely
obtain ⟨e, he_ball, he_Gt⟩ := ...
let p := ...
let seg : ℝ → E := ...
let S : Set ℝ := ...
let b : ℝ := sSup S
-- 4. Derive contradiction
...
```

This separation between the universal setup and the concrete argument eliminates all metavariable issues.

[05/17/2026 16:33:12 +00:00] User:
there is a reason to carry around \forall t <t0, and that is because later in the proof, we consider an integral I(t) that is both the volume of the ball and a polynomial. this then allows us to conclude that I(1) is the volume of the unit ball while another argument shows I(1)=0, leading to a contradiction

Response:
That is a good reason to keep the universal quantification. The issue is specifically with `let` bindings that carry proof arguments. The fix is to use `choose` instead of `let` to extract the witnesses without carrying proof arguments.

---

## Fix — Use `choose` Instead of `let`

```lean
-- Instead of
let e := fun t ht0 htC ht1 => (hGt_ne t ht0 htC ht1).choose

-- Use choose to extract e as a function without proof arguments
have hGt_ne' : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 →
    ∃ e ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, e ∉ G_t t := hGt_ne
choose e he_ball he_Gt using hGt_ne'
```

Now `e : ℝ → (0 ≤ ·) → (· < t0) → (· < 1) → E` but without being a `let` binding, Lean handles the arguments correctly.

---

## Similarly for `g`

```lean
have hGt_nonempty' : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∃ p : E, p ∈ G_t t := fun t ht0 htC =>
  (hGt_nonempty t ht0 htC).imp (fun x hx => hx)
choose p hp using hGt_nonempty'
```

---

## Then `seg`, `S`, `b` as `have` Statements

```lean
-- seg is now a have not a let
have hseg_def : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    ∀ s : ℝ, e t ht0 htC ht1 + s • (p t ht0 htC.le - e t ht0 htC ht1) ∈ E :=
  fun t ht0 htC ht1 s => Set.mem_univ _
-- Define seg as a plain function for each fixed t
have hseg_cont : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    Continuous (fun s : ℝ =>
      e t ht0 htC ht1 + s • (p t ht0 htC.le - e t ht0 htC ht1)) := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  fun_prop
```

---

## Why `choose` Works Where `let` Fails

`choose` produces a definition at the **declaration level** rather than as a local `let` binding. This means Lean treats `e`, `p` as proper functions rather than local abbreviations, avoiding the metavariable leakage that occurs when `let` bindings with proof arguments are referenced in subsequent `have` statements.

[05/17/2026 16:41:28 +00:00] User:
e and g have been changed, but the error still occurs, what exactly has to be done with the others

Response:
The remaining `let` bindings with proof arguments that need to be changed are:

```lean
let seg := fun t ht0 htC ht1 s => ...
let S := fun t ht0 htC ht1 => ...
let b := fun t ht0 htC ht1 => ...
```

---

## Fix — Convert All to `def` Outside the Theorem

The most robust fix is to move these definitions outside the theorem entirely:

```lean
private def seg (e p : E) (s : ℝ) : E := e + s • (p - e)

private def S (e p : E) (U : Set E) : Set ℝ :=
  {s ∈ Set.Icc 0 1 | seg e p s ∈ U}

private noncomputable def b (e p : E) (U : Set E) : ℝ :=
  sSup (S e p U)
```

Then inside the theorem use them as:

```lean
-- No proof arguments, just data arguments
let seg_t := seg (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le)
let S_t := S (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le) (G_t t)
let b_t := b (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le) (G_t t)
```

---

## Why This Works

By moving the definitions outside the theorem, the proof arguments `ht0 htC ht1` are no longer baked into the definition. Inside the theorem, `seg_t`, `S_t`, `b_t` are `let` bindings that take only **data** arguments (`e`, `p`, `G_t t`), not proof arguments. This eliminates the metavariable leakage entirely.

---

## If Moving Outside Is Not Desired

The minimal fix inside the theorem is to replace each `let` with a `have` that states the defining property rather than the definition:

```lean
-- Instead of
let seg := fun t ht0 htC ht1 s =>
  e t ht0 htC ht1 + s • (p t ht0 htC.le - e t ht0 htC ht1)

-- Use
have hseg : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    ∀ s : ℝ, ∃ y : E,
    y = e t ht0 htC ht1 + s • (p t ht0 htC.le - e t ht0 htC ht1) :=
  fun t ht0 htC ht1 s => ⟨_, rfl⟩
```

But this is unwieldy. The `def` approach outside the theorem is strongly preferred.

[05/17/2026 16:42:58 +00:00] User:
is there not a definition in mathlib that could be used for seg?

Response:
Yes. The line segment between two points is already defined in Mathlib as part of the convexity library:

```lean
#check AffineMap.lineMap
-- AffineMap.lineMap (p₀ p₁ : P) : ℝ →ᵃ[ℝ] P
-- lineMap p₀ p₁ t = p₀ + t • (p₁ - p₀)
```

Or more directly:

```lean
#check segment
-- segment ℝ p q = {p + t • (q - p) | t ∈ Set.Icc 0 1}
```

---

## Using `AffineMap.lineMap`

```lean
-- seg is just lineMap e p
let seg := fun t ht0 htC ht1 =>
  AffineMap.lineMap (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le)
```

`AffineMap.lineMap p₀ p₁ : ℝ →ᵃ[ℝ] E` satisfies:
- `lineMap p₀ p₁ 0 = p₀`
- `lineMap p₀ p₁ 1 = p₁`
- Continuous by `AffineMap.continuous_lineMap`

---

## Key Properties Already in Mathlib

```lean
#check AffineMap.lineMap_apply_zero
-- AffineMap.lineMap p₀ p₁ 0 = p₀

#check AffineMap.lineMap_apply_one
-- AffineMap.lineMap p₀ p₁ 1 = p₁

#check AffineMap.lineMap_continuous
-- Continuous (AffineMap.lineMap p₀ p₁)
```

---

## Advantage Over Custom `seg`

Since `AffineMap.lineMap` is a proper Mathlib definition rather than a local `let`, it avoids the metavariable leakage issue entirely. The proof arguments `ht0 htC ht1` only appear in the arguments `e t ht0 htC ht1` and `p t ht0 htC.le`, not in the definition of the segment itself.

[05/17/2026 16:45:44 +00:00] User:
using this definition, what should hseg_cont become?

Response:
```lean
have hseg_cont : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
```

[05/17/2026 18:12:48 +00:00] User:

Response:
This is the key step — since `b` is the supremum of `S`, it is not in `G_t` (which is open), so `x` must be on the boundary.

---

## Step 1 — `b` is Not in `G_t`

```lean
have hb_not_Gt : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    AffineMap.lineMap (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le)
      (b t ht0 htC ht1) ∉ G_t t := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1 hb_in
  -- b is the sup of S, so b + ε ∉ S for small ε
  -- but if seg b ∈ G_t which is open, then seg (b + ε) ∈ G_t for small ε
  -- contradicting b being the sup
  have hGt_open_t := hGt_open t ht0 htC
  obtain ⟨ε, hε, hball⟩ := Metric.isOpen_iff.mp hGt_open_t _ hb_in
  have hb_val := hb_mem_Icc t ht0 htC ht1
  -- Find s > b in S
  have hlt : b t ht0 htC ht1 < b t ht0 htC ht1 + ε / 2 := by linarith
  have hs_in_S : b t ht0 htC ht1 + ε / 2 ∈ S t ht0 htC ht1 := by
    constructor
    · constructor
      · linarith [hb_val.1]
      · sorry -- need b + ε/2 ≤ 1
    · apply hball
      simp [Metric.mem_ball, dist_eq_norm]
      sorry -- need ‖lineMap (b + ε/2) - lineMap b‖ < ε
  linarith [le_csSup (hS_bddAbove t ht0 htC ht1) hs_in_S]
```

---

## Step 2 — `x` is Not in the Interior

```lean
have hx_not_interior : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    f_t t x = AffineMap.lineMap (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le)
      (b t ht0 htC ht1) →
    x ∉ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1 x hx hfx hx_int
  apply hb_not_Gt t ht0 htC ht1
  rw [← hfx]
  exact ⟨x, hx_int, rfl⟩
```

---

## Step 3 — `x` is on the Boundary

```lean
have hx_boundary : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    f_t t x = AffineMap.lineMap (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le)
      (b t ht0 htC ht1) →
    ‖x‖ = 1 := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1 x hx hfx
  have hx_not_int := hx_not_interior t ht0 htC ht1 x hx hfx
  rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne'] at hx_not_int
  simp only [mem_ball, dist_zero_right, not_lt] at hx_not_int
  exact le_antisymm (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp hx) hx_not_int
```

## Step 4 — `f_t t x = x` Since `x` is on the Sphere

```lean
have hx_fixed : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,

    f_t t x = x := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1 x hx hfx

    simp [mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm]
    exact hx_boundary t ht0 htC ht1 x hx hfx
  exact hft_fixed t x hx_sphere
```

[05/17/2026 18:15:33 +00:00] User:
there is a sorry in hb_not_gt, does something need to be altered in this?

Response:
Yes. The two `sorry`s in `hb_not_Gt` need to be addressed. Let's look at them:

---

## Sorry 1 — `b + ε/2 ≤ 1`

This requires that `b ≤ 1` (from `hb_val.2`) and `ε` is small enough. But we cannot guarantee `b + ε/2 ≤ 1` without shrinking `ε`. Fix by using `min (b + ε/2) 1` or shrinking `ε`:

```lean
-- Use ε' = min ε (2 * (1 - b)) / 2 to ensure b + ε' ≤ 1
let ε' := min ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1) / 2
have hε'_pos : 0 < ε' := by
  apply div_pos _ two_pos
  exact lt_min hε (by linarith [hb_val.2])
have hb_lt : b t ht0 htC ht1 + ε' ≤ 1 := by
  unfold_let ε'
  linarith [min_le_right ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1)]
```

---

## Sorry 2 — Norm Bound for the Line Map

The norm of `lineMap (b + ε') - lineMap b` needs to be less than `ε`. Since `lineMap` is affine:

$$\text{lineMap}(b + \varepsilon') - \text{lineMap}(b) = \varepsilon' \cdot (p - e)$$

```lean
have hnorm : ‖AffineMap.lineMap (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le)
    (b t ht0 htC ht1 + ε') -
    AffineMap.lineMap (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le)
    (b t ht0 htC ht1)‖ < ε := by
  rw [AffineMap.lineMap_apply, AffineMap.lineMap_apply]
  simp only [vsub_eq_sub, vadd_eq_add]
  ring_nf
  rw [norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg hε'_pos.le]
  calc ε' * ‖p t ht0 htC.le - e t ht0 htC ht1‖
      ≤ ε' * 2 := by
          apply mul_le_mul_of_nonneg_left _ hε'_pos.le
          -- p and e are both in closedBall 0 1 so ‖p - e‖ ≤ 2
          have hp_ball := hp t ht0 htC.le
          have he_ball' := he_ball t ht0 htC ht1
          calc ‖p t ht0 htC.le - e t ht0 htC ht1‖
              ≤ ‖p t ht0 htC.le‖ + ‖e t ht0 htC ht1‖ := norm_sub_le _ _
            _ ≤ 1 + 1 := by
                apply add_le_add
                · exact mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp
                    (hGt_subset t ht0 htC.le hp_ball)
                · exact mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp he_ball'
            _ = 2 := by norm_num
    _ < ε := by
          unfold_let ε'
          linarith [min_le_left ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1)]
```

---

## Full Fixed `hb_not_Gt`

```lean

    AffineMap.lineMap (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le)

  have hb_val := hb_mem_Icc t ht0 htC ht1
  let ε' := min ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1) / 2
  have hε'_pos : 0 < ε' := by
    apply div_pos _ two_pos
    exact lt_min hε (by linarith [hb_val.2])
  have hb_lt : b t ht0 htC ht1 + ε' ≤ 1 := by
    unfold_let ε'
    linarith [min_le_right ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1)]
  have hs_in_S : b t ht0 htC ht1 + ε' ∈ S t ht0 htC ht1 := by
    constructor

    · apply hball

      ring_nf
      rw [norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg hε'_pos.le]
      calc ε' * ‖p t ht0 htC.le - e t ht0 htC ht1‖
          ≤ ε' * 2 := by
              apply mul_le_mul_of_nonneg_left _ hε'_pos.le
              have := norm_sub_le (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1)
              have hp_norm := mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp

        _ < ε := by
```

[05/17/2026 18:25:45 +00:00] User:

Response:
The goal is `0 < min ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1)`. We need `0 < ε` and `0 < 1 - b t ht0 htC ht1`. The second requires `b < 1`, but `hb_val.2` only gives `b ≤ 1`.

## The Issue

`b` could equal `1` since `hb_val : b ∈ Set.Icc 0 1` only gives `b ≤ 1`. We need `b < 1` which requires additional reasoning.

---

## Fix — Show `b < 1`

`b < 1` because `e ∉ G_t` but `seg 0 = e`, so `0 ∉ S`, meaning `b` cannot be `1` since `S ⊆ (0, 1]` with `0` excluded... 

Actually the cleaner argument is that `seg 1 = p ∈ G_t` so `1 ∈ S`, and `seg 0 = e ∉ G_t`. Since `G_t` is open and `e ∉ G_t`, there exists `δ > 0` such that `seg s ∉ G_t` for `s ∈ [0, δ)`. So `b ≥ δ > 0` but we need `b < 1`.

The issue is `b < 1` is not obvious. Instead, avoid needing it by using a different `ε'`:

```lean
-- Instead of shrinking ε to avoid going past 1,
-- just cap at min (b + ε/2) 1 and check membership
let s' := min (b t ht0 htC ht1 + ε / 2) 1
have hs'_le : s' ≤ 1 := min_le_right _ _
have hs'_gt : b t ht0 htC ht1 < s' := by
  unfold_let s'
  exact lt_min (by linarith) (by linarith [hb_val.2])
have hs'_close : dist
    (AffineMap.lineMap (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le) s')
    (AffineMap.lineMap (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le)
      (b t ht0 htC ht1)) < ε := by
  rw [AffineMap.lineMap_apply, AffineMap.lineMap_apply]
  simp only [dist_eq_norm]
  ring_nf
  rw [norm_smul]
  calc |s' - b t ht0 htC ht1| * ‖p t ht0 htC.le - e t ht0 htC ht1‖
      ≤ (ε / 2) * 2 := by
          apply mul_le_mul
          · rw [abs_of_pos (by linarith [hs'_gt])]
            unfold_let s'
            linarith [min_le_left (b t ht0 htC ht1 + ε / 2) 1]
          · have hp_norm := mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp
              (hGt_subset t ht0 htC.le (hp t ht0 htC.le))
            have he_norm := mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp (he_ball t ht0 htC ht1)
            linarith [norm_sub_le (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1)]
          · positivity
          · positivity
    _ = ε := by ring
have hs'_in_S : s' ∈ S t ht0 htC ht1 := by
  constructor
  · exact ⟨by linarith [hb_val.1, hs'_gt], hs'_le⟩
  · exact hball hs'_close
linarith [le_csSup (hS_bddAbove t ht0 htC ht1) hs'_in_S]
```

[05/17/2026 18:28:48 +00:00] User:
in hs'_gt

exact lt_min (by linarith) (by linarith [hb_val.2])

Response:
The second `linarith` is trying to prove `b t ht0 htC ht1 < 1`, but `hb_val.2` only gives `b ≤ 1`. We need a separate argument for `b < 1`.

---

## Show `b < 1` Separately

`b < 1` because `1 ∈ S` (since `seg 1 = p ∈ G_t`) and `b = sSup S ≤ 1`, but actually `b` could equal `1`. The real argument is:

`e ∉ G_t` and `G_t` is open, so there exists a neighbourhood of `e` not in `G_t`. Since `seg 0 = e`, for small `s > 0`, `seg s ∉ G_t`. This means `0 ∉ S` and the infimum of `S` is positive. But this does not directly give `b < 1`.

---

## Simpler Fix — Handle `b = 1` Separately

```lean
have hs'_gt : b t ht0 htC ht1 < s' := by
  unfold_let s'
  apply lt_min
  · linarith
  · rcases eq_or_lt_of_le hb_val.2 with hb1 | hb1
    · -- b = 1, but then seg 1 = p ∈ G_t so 1 ∈ S
      -- and b = sSup S ≥ 1, contradiction with b being sup
      exfalso
      have h1_in_S : (1 : ℝ) ∈ S t ht0 htC ht1 := by
        exact ⟨⟨by linarith [hb_val.1], le_refl 1⟩, by
```

[05/17/2026 18:33:47 +00:00] User:

Response:
You are right. There is no reason `b` cannot equal `1`. If `b = 1` then `seg 1 = p ∈ G_t`, so `1 ∈ S` and `b = sSup S = 1` is perfectly consistent. In that case `hb_in : seg b ∈ G_t` means `p ∈ G_t` which is true, so there is no contradiction from `b = 1`.

---

## The Real Issue

The argument `hb_not_Gt` is trying to show `seg b ∉ G_t` by finding a point `s' > b` in `S`. But if `b = 1` then there is no `s' > b` in `[0, 1]`.

---

## Fix — Handle `b = 1` Directly

If `b = 1` then `seg b = p ∈ G_t`, which contradicts `hb_in` being the assumption we are trying to derive `False` from... wait, `hb_in` **is** `seg b ∈ G_t`. So `hb_not_Gt` is trying to prove `seg b ∉ G_t` by contradiction, and `hb_in` is the hypothesis `seg b ∈ G_t`.

The issue is that when `b = 1`, `seg b = p ∈ G_t` is **consistent** — there is no contradiction. So `hb_not_Gt` is actually **false** when `b = 1`.

---

## Rethink the Argument

The correct statement should be that `b` is the **infimum** of `{s | seg s ∉ G_t}` rather than the supremum of `S`. Or alternatively define:

```lean
-- S should be the set of s where seg s is NOT in G_t
let S : ∀ t ht0 htC ht1, Set ℝ :=
  fun t ht0 htC ht1 => {s ∈ Set.Icc 0 1 | AffineMap.lineMap
    (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le) s ∉ G_t t}
-- b = inf S (the first time seg leaves G_t... 
-- wait, seg starts outside G_t at s=0)
```

---

## Correct Setup

Recall:
- `seg 0 = e ∉ G_t`
- `seg 1 = p ∈ G_t`

So the segment **starts outside** `G_t` and **ends inside** `G_t`. The boundary point should be:

```lean
-- S = {s ∈ [0,1] | seg s ∈ G_t}  -- nonempty since 1 ∈ S
-- b = inf S  -- first time segment enters G_t
let b := sInf (S t ht0 htC ht1)
```

Then:
- `b > 0` since `e ∉ G_t` and `G_t` is open
- `seg b ∉ G_t` since `b = inf S` and `G_t` is open
- `seg b` is in the closure of `G_t`

---

## Revised Definitions

```lean
let S : Set ℝ := {s ∈ Set.Icc 0 1 |
  AffineMap.lineMap (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le) s ∈ G_t t}
let b : ℝ := sInf S
```

---

## `S` is Nonempty — `1 ∈ S`

```lean
have hS_nonempty : S.Nonempty :=
  ⟨1, ⟨Set.right_mem_Icc.mpr le_rfl, by rw [hseg1]; exact hp t ht0 htC.le⟩⟩
```

---

## `b` is Bounded Below by `0`

```lean
have hS_bddBelow : BddBelow S :=
  ⟨0, fun s hs => hs.1.1⟩
```

## `b ∉ S` Since `G_t` is Open

```lean
have hb_not_S : b ∉ S := by
  intro hb_in
  -- b = inf S and b ∈ S means b ∈ G_t which is open
  -- so there exists ε > 0 with ball (seg b) ε ⊆ G_t
  -- meaning seg (b - ε') ∈ G_t for small ε', contradicting b = inf S
  obtain ⟨ε, hε, hball⟩ := Metric.isOpen_iff.mp (hGt_open t ht0 htC) _ hb_in.2
  have hb_val := csInf_mem_Icc hS_nonempty hS_bddBelow
  let ε' := min ε (b - 0) / 2
  have hε'_pos : 0 < ε' := by
    apply div_pos _ two_pos
    exact lt_min hε (by
      rcases eq_or_lt_of_le hb_val.1 with hb0 | hb0
      · -- b = 0 means seg 0 = e ∈ G_t, contradicting he_Gt
        exfalso
        rw [← hb0] at hb_in
        simp [hseg0] at hb_in
        exact he_Gt t ht0 htC ht1 hb_in
      · linarith)
  have hs'_in_S : b - ε' ∈ S := by
    constructor
    · exact ⟨by linarith [hb_val.1], by linarith [hb_val.2]⟩
    · apply hball
      simp [Metric.mem_ball, dist_eq_norm, AffineMap.lineMap_apply]
      sorry
  linarith [csInf_le hS_bddBelow hs'_in_S]
```

---

## Summary of Changes

| Before | After |
|---|---|
| `b = sSup {s \| seg s ∈ G_t}` | `b = sInf {s \| seg s ∈ G_t}` |
| `seg 0 = e ∉ G_t`, `seg 1 = p ∈ G_t` | Same |
| `b` is last point in `G_t` | `b` is first point in `G_t` |
| `b = 1` is consistent | `b = 0` leads to contradiction via `he_Gt` |

[05/23/2026 15:10:04 +00:00] User:

Response:
The argument is: if `seg b ∈ G_t` then since `G_t` is open, there exists `ε > 0` such that `seg (b + ε') ∈ G_t` for small `ε'`, contradicting `b = sSup S`.

```lean
have hb_not_Gt : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1)
      (b t ht0 htC ht1) ∉ G_t t := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1 hb_in
  have hGt_open_t := hGt_open t ht0 htC
  obtain ⟨ε, hε, hball⟩ := Metric.isOpen_iff.mp hGt_open_t _ hb_in
  have hb_val := hb_mem_Icc t ht0 htC ht1
  -- seg 1 = e ∉ G_t so b < 1
  have hb_lt_one : b t ht0 htC ht1 < 1 := by
    rcases eq_or_lt_of_le hb_val.2 with hb1 | hb1
    · exfalso
      rw [← hb1] at hb_in
      simp only [AffineMap.lineMap_apply_one] at hb_in
      exact he_Gt t ht0 htC ht1 hb_in
    · exact hb1
  -- Pick s' = b + ε' where ε' is small enough
  let ε' := min ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1) / 2
  have hε'_pos : 0 < ε' := by
    apply div_pos _ two_pos
    exact lt_min hε (by linarith)
  have hs'_le : b t ht0 htC ht1 + ε' ≤ 1 := by
    unfold_let ε'
    linarith [min_le_right ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1)]
  -- seg (b + ε') is close to seg b
  have hs'_close : dist
      (AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1)
        (b t ht0 htC ht1 + ε'))
      (AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1)
        (b t ht0 htC ht1)) < ε := by
    rw [AffineMap.lineMap_apply, AffineMap.lineMap_apply, dist_eq_norm]
    simp only [vadd_eq_add, vsub_eq_sub]
    ring_nf
    rw [norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg hε'_pos.le]
    have hpe : ‖e t ht0 htC ht1 - p t ht0 htC.le‖ ≤ 2 := by
      have hp_norm := mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp
        (hGt_subset t ht0 htC.le (hp t ht0 htC.le))
      have he_norm := mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp (he_ball t ht0 htC ht1)
      linarith [norm_sub_le (e t ht0 htC ht1) (p t ht0 htC.le)]
    calc ε' * ‖e t ht0 htC ht1 - p t ht0 htC.le‖
        ≤ ε' * 2 := by nlinarith
      _ < ε := by
          unfold_let ε'
          linarith [min_le_left ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1)]
  -- seg (b + ε') ∈ G_t
  have hs'_in_S : b t ht0 htC ht1 + ε' ∈ S t ht0 htC ht1 := by
    exact ⟨⟨by linarith [hb_val.1], hs'_le⟩, hball hs'_close⟩
  -- contradicts b = sSup S
  linarith [le_csSup (hS_bddAbove t ht0 htC ht1) hs'_in_S]
```

[05/23/2026 15:36:27 +00:00] User:

Response:
The goal is `min ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1) / 2 * 2 < ε`. This simplifies to `min ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1) < ε`, which follows from `min ε _ ≤ ε` and the fact that we need strict inequality from `hε`:

```lean
calc min ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1) / 2 * 2
    = min ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1) := by ring
  _ ≤ ε := min_le_left _ _
  _ < ε + ε := by linarith
```

Wait — that does not work either. The goal is strict `< ε` not `≤ ε`. Use:

```lean
calc min ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1) / 2 * 2
    = min ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1) := by ring
  _ ≤ ε := min_le_left _ _
```

But this gives `≤` not `<`. The strict inequality requires `min ε (1 - b) < ε`, i.e. `1 - b < ε` or we need another argument.

---

## Fix — Use `hpe` to Get Strict Inequality

```lean
calc ε' * ‖e t ht0 htC ht1 - p t ht0 htC.le‖
    ≤ ε' * 2 := by nlinarith
  _ = min ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1) := by unfold_let ε'; ring
  _ ≤ ε := min_le_left _ _
  _ = ε := rfl
```

This still gives `≤`. The issue is that `ε' * 2 < ε` requires `min ε (1 - b) < ε`, which needs `1 - b < ε`. This is not guaranteed.

---

## Correct Fix — Use `ε / 2` Directly in the Bound

The cleanest fix is to not use `hpe` at all and bound differently:

```lean
calc ε' * ‖e t ht0 htC ht1 - p t ht0 htC.le‖
    < ε := by
        have : ε' < ε / 2 := by
          unfold_let ε'
          linarith [min_le_left ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1)]
        nlinarith
```

Wait — this requires `‖e - p‖ ≤ 2` and `ε' < ε/2` to give `ε' * ‖e - p‖ < ε/2 * 2 = ε`. Use:

```lean
calc ε' * ‖e t ht0 htC ht1 - p t ht0 htC.le‖
    ≤ ε' * 2 := by nlinarith
  _ < (ε / 2) * 2 := by
      apply mul_lt_mul_of_pos_right _ two_pos
      unfold_let ε'
      linarith [min_le_left ε (1 - b t ht0 htC ht1)]
  _ = ε := by ring
```

[05/24/2026 14:33:09 +00:00] User:
next, want to show that as f_t maps S^n-1 to itself, f_t maps B^n bijectively to itself

Response:
The key steps are:

1. `f_t t` maps `closedBall 0 1` to itself (`hft_maps`)
2. `f_t t` is injective on `closedBall 0 1` (`hft_inj`)
3. Together these give a bijection

---

## Statement and Proof

```lean
have hft_bij : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    Set.BijOn (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  intro t ht0 htC
  constructor
  · -- f_t t maps closedBall to closedBall
    exact hft_maps t ⟨ht0, htC.le⟩
  constructor
  · -- f_t t is injective on closedBall
    exact hft_inj t ht0 htC
  · -- f_t t is surjective onto closedBall
    intro y hy
    -- y is in the image since f_t t maps B^n to B^n bijectively
    -- by invariance of domain, the image is open
    -- the image is also closed (compact image of compact set)
    -- the image contains the sphere (fixed by f_t t)
    -- by connectedness the image is all of B^n
    have himage_open : IsOpen (f_t t '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) :=
      hGt_open t ht0 htC
    have himage_closed : IsClosed (f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
      hft_image_closed t ht0 htC.le
    have himage_subset : f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1 ⊆ closedBall (0 : E) 1 :=
      hft_image_subset t ht0 htC.le
    have hsphere_fixed : ∀ x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1, f_t t x = x := by
      intro x hx
      simp only [f_t, g]
      rw [hf_fixed x (mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mp hx ▸ hf_maps x
        (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mpr (mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mp hx).le))]
      simp
    have hsphere_subset : sphere (0 : E) 1 ⊆ f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by
      intro x hx
      exact ⟨x, mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mpr (mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mp hx).le,
        hsphere_fixed x hx⟩
    sorry
```

---

## The Surjectivity Argument

The surjectivity is the hard part. The image `f_t t '' closedBall 0 1` is:
- Closed (compact image)
- Contains `G_t = f_t t '' interior (closedBall 0 1)` which is open
- Contains the sphere `S^(n-1)`
- Contained in `closedBall 0 1`

By connectedness of `closedBall 0 1`, the image must be all of `closedBall 0 1`. But this requires showing the image is clopen in `closedBall 0 1`, which needs more work.

---

## Alternative — Use the Boundary Point Argument

Rather than proving full bijectivity, use the boundary point `x` with `‖x‖ = 1` and `f_t t x = x` to derive the contradiction directly:

```lean
-- x is on the sphere and f_t t x = x
-- but f_t t x = seg b which is in the closure of G_t
-- and G_t ⊆ interior (closedBall 0 1)
-- so seg b is in the closure of the interior, not on the sphere
-- contradiction
have hclosure_interior : closure (interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) =
    closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by
  exact closure_interior_closedBall 0 one_pos.ne'
have hb_in_closed : AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1)
    (b t ht0 htC ht1) ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by
  rw [← hclosure_interior]
  exact closure_mono (hGt_subset t ht0 htC.le) hb_closure
```

[05/24/2026 16:05:21 +00:00] User:
want to show that e must lie on the boundary

Response:
`e` is in `closedBall 0 1` but not in `G_t`, and `G_t` contains the interior of `closedBall 0 1`... wait, that is not quite right. `G_t = f_t t '' interior (closedBall 0 1)` is not the same as `interior (closedBall 0 1)`.

The argument for `e` being on the boundary comes from `hx_boundary` applied to `e`:

---

## The Argument

We have:
- `f_t t x = seg b` (from `hb_in_image`)
- `f_t t x = x` (from `hx_fixed`, since `x` is on the sphere)
- `seg b ∉ G_t` (from `hb_not_Gt`)
- `x ∉ interior (closedBall 0 1)` (since `f_t t x ∉ G_t`)
- `x ∈ closedBall 0 1` (from `hb_in_image`)
- Therefore `‖x‖ = 1`

Now for `e`:

```lean
have he_boundary : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    ‖e t ht0 htC ht1‖ = 1 := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  -- e ∉ G_t and G_t = f_t t '' interior (closedBall 0 1)
  -- so e is not in the image of the interior
  -- but e ∈ closedBall 0 1
  -- we need to show e is not in the interior of the image
  -- which by invariance of domain equals the image of the interior
  -- so e ∉ f_t t '' interior (closedBall 0 1) = G_t ✓
  -- now use hft_inj to show the preimage of e is on the sphere
  have he_in_ball := he_ball t ht0 htC ht1
  have he_not_Gt := he_Gt t ht0 htC ht1
  -- e is in closedBall but not in G_t = f_t t '' interior (closedBall 0 1)
  -- by hft_maps, f_t t maps sphere to sphere
  -- so if ‖e‖ < 1 then e ∈ interior (closedBall 0 1)
  -- by invariance of domain e ∈ G_t, contradiction
  by_contra he_not_sphere
  have he_lt : ‖e t ht0 htC ht1‖ < 1 := by
    rcases lt_or_eq_of_le (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp he_in_ball) with h | h
    · exact h
    · exact absurd h.symm he_not_sphere
  have he_interior : e t ht0 htC ht1 ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne']
    exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mpr he_lt
  -- f_t t is injective so there exists x with f_t t x = e
  -- but we need e itself to be in G_t
  -- actually e ∈ interior (closedBall 0 1) and G_t = f_t t '' interior
  -- we need f_t t (f_t t)⁻¹ e = e ∈ G_t
  -- this requires surjectivity onto the interior which we don't have yet
  sorry
```

---

## The Missing Piece

The argument requires that `interior (closedBall 0 1) ⊆ G_t`, i.e. that `f_t t` maps the interior **onto** the interior. This is exactly the surjectivity we were trying to prove.

---

## Alternative Direct Argument

Instead of going through `e`, use the boundary point `x` from `hb_in_image` directly:

```lean
-- x is on the boundary: ‖x‖ = 1
-- f_t t x = x since x ∈ sphere
-- but f_t t x = seg b ∈ closure (G_t)
-- G_t ⊆ interior (closedBall 0 1)
-- so seg b ∈ closure (interior (closedBall 0 1)) = closedBall 0 1
-- and seg b = x with ‖x‖ = 1
-- but closure (G_t) ⊆ closedBall 0 1 and x is on the boundary
-- now f_t t fixes the sphere, so f_t t x = x
-- but x = seg b ∈ closure G_t ⊆ closure (interior B^n)
-- the key contradiction: seg b ∈ G_t (from hb_closure) 
-- but hb_not_Gt says seg b ∉ G_t
-- so seg b ∈ closure G_t \ G_t = frontier G_t
-- and f_t t x = seg b, x on sphere
-- hf_maps says f x ∈ sphere, f_t interpolates, so f_t t x should be interior
-- this is the contradiction
have hcontra : False := by
  obtain ⟨x, hx_ball, hfx⟩ := hb_in_image t ht0 htC ht1
  have hx_norm := hx_boundary t ht0 htC ht1 x hx_ball hfx
  have hx_fixed := hx_fixed t ht0 htC ht1 x hx_ball hfx
  -- f_t t x = x and ‖x‖ = 1
  -- but f_t t x = seg b ∈ closure G_t
  -- and seg b ∉ G_t
  -- so x ∈ closure G_t \ G_t
  have hx_in_closure : x ∈ closure (G_t t) := hfx ▸ hb_closure t ht0 htC ht1
  have hx_not_Gt : x ∉ G_t t := hfx ▸ hb_not_Gt t ht0 htC ht1
  -- x ∈ frontier G_t
  have hx_frontier : x ∈ frontier (G_t t) :=
    ⟨hx_in_closure, fun hx_int => hx_not_Gt (interior_subset hx_int)⟩
  -- but x is on the sphere and f_t t fixes the sphere
  -- f_t t x = x ∈ sphere ⊆ boundary of B^n
  -- G_t ⊆ interior B^n so frontier G_t ⊆ closure (interior B^n) = B^n
  -- need x ∉ G_t and x ∈ closure G_t to derive contradiction with
  -- x being fixed by f_t t
  -- The contradiction: x ∈ sphere, f_t t x = x
  -- but G_t = f_t t '' interior B^n ⊆ interior B^n (by invariance of domain)
  -- so x ∉ G_t means x ∉ f_t t '' interior B^n
  -- meaning no interior point maps to x
  -- but x is on the sphere, not interior
  -- this is consistent... we need a different contradiction
  sorry
exact hcontra
```

---

## The Real Contradiction

The proof needs the integral argument `I(t)` you mentioned earlier — showing `I(t)` is both the volume of the ball and a polynomial that equals `0` at `t = 1`. The boundary point argument alone is not sufficient to derive `False` without the integral.

[05/24/2026 19:00:36 +00:00] User:
if e were not on the boundary, it would imply that, with b being on the segment between e and g, b was not on the boundary

Response:
That is the key insight. If `e` is in the interior, then the entire segment from `p` (in `G_t ⊆` interior) to `e` (also interior) stays in the interior, so `b` (on the segment) would also be in the interior. But `b` is on the boundary — contradiction.

---

## The Argument

```lean
have he_boundary : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    ‖e t ht0 htC ht1‖ = 1 := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  have he_in_ball := he_ball t ht0 htC ht1
  by_contra he_not_sphere
  -- e is in the interior of B^n
  have he_lt : ‖e t ht0 htC ht1‖ < 1 :=
    lt_of_le_of_ne (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp he_in_ball) he_not_sphere
  have he_interior : e t ht0 htC ht1 ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne']
    exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mpr he_lt
  -- p is also in the interior since p ∈ G_t ⊆ interior B^n
  have hp_interior : p t ht0 htC.le ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    apply interior_mono (hGt_subset t ht0 htC.le)
    exact (hp t ht0 htC.le).1
  -- The segment from p to e stays in the interior since interior B^n is convex
  have hinterior_convex : Convex ℝ (interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) :=
    (convex_closedBall 0 1).interior
  have hseg_interior : ∀ s ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) 1,
      AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1) s ∈
      interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    intro s hs
    apply hinterior_convex.lineMap_mem hp_interior he_interior
    exact hs
  -- In particular seg b is in the interior
  have hb_interior : AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1)
      (b t ht0 htC ht1) ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    hseg_interior _ (hb_mem_Icc t ht0 htC ht1)
  -- But seg b ∈ G_t since G_t = f_t t '' interior B^n
  -- and f_t t is a local homeomorphism on the interior
  -- Actually we need seg b ∈ G_t to contradict hb_not_Gt
  -- seg b is in interior B^n, and G_t is open and dense in interior B^n?
  -- No - we need a different argument here
  sorry
```

---

## The Missing Step

The issue is that `seg b ∈ interior (closedBall 0 1)` does not directly give `seg b ∈ G_t`. We need to know that `f_t t` maps the interior **onto** itself.

However, there is a simpler argument: if `e` is in the interior, then since `G_t` is open and `f_t t` is a local homeomorphism, the preimage of `e` under `f_t t` exists in the interior. But we need surjectivity.

---

## Actually Simpler — Use `hb_not_Gt` and `hb_closure`

The contradiction is more direct:

```lean
  -- seg b ∈ closure G_t (from hb_closure)
  -- G_t ⊆ f_t t '' interior B^n ⊆ interior B^n (by invariance of domain)
  -- so closure G_t ⊆ closure (interior B^n) = closedBall 0 1
  -- but seg b ∈ interior B^n (from hseg_interior)
  -- so seg b ∈ interior B^n and seg b ∈ closure G_t
  -- now G_t is open so seg b ∈ G_t (since interior B^n is open
  -- and seg b is in the interior, and G_t covers the interior)
  -- This contradicts hb_not_Gt
  have hb_in_Gt : AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1)
      (b t ht0 htC ht1) ∈ G_t t := by
    -- seg b ∈ interior B^n and G_t is open dense in interior B^n
    -- Actually: f_t t is injective and maps interior to G_t
    -- and seg b ∈ interior B^n means there exists x with f_t t x = seg b
    -- and x ∈ interior B^n so seg b ∈ G_t
    sorry
  exact hb_not_Gt t ht0 htC ht1 hb_in_Gt
```

The `sorry` requires surjectivity of `f_t t` onto the interior, which brings us back to the same problem. The integral argument `I(t)` is needed to complete this.

[05/24/2026 19:04:01 +00:00] User:
seg b ∈ interior (closedBall 0 1) would imply that the norm is less than 1 though, would it not?

Response:
Yes! And we already have `hx_boundary` which says `‖x‖ = 1` where `x` is the preimage of `seg b`. But if `seg b` is in the interior then `‖seg b‖ < 1`, and `f_t t x = seg b` with `f_t t x = x` (since `x` is on the sphere) gives `‖x‖ = ‖seg b‖ < 1`, contradicting `‖x‖ = 1`.

---

## The Contradiction

```lean
have he_boundary : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    ‖e t ht0 htC ht1‖ = 1 := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  have he_in_ball := he_ball t ht0 htC ht1
  by_contra he_not_sphere
  have he_lt : ‖e t ht0 htC ht1‖ < 1 :=
    lt_of_le_of_ne (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp he_in_ball) he_not_sphere
  have he_interior : e t ht0 htC ht1 ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne']
    exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mpr he_lt
  have hp_interior : p t ht0 htC.le ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    interior_mono (hGt_subset t ht0 htC.le) (hp t ht0 htC.le).1
  have hinterior_convex : Convex ℝ (interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) :=
    (convex_closedBall 0 1).interior
  have hb_interior : AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1)
      (b t ht0 htC ht1) ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    hinterior_convex.lineMap_mem hp_interior he_interior
      (hb_mem_Icc t ht0 htC ht1)
  -- seg b is in the interior so ‖seg b‖ < 1
  have hb_norm : ‖AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1)
      (b t ht0 htC ht1)‖ < 1 := by
    rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne'] at hb_interior
    exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mp hb_interior
  -- But f_t t x = seg b and f_t t x = x with ‖x‖ = 1
  obtain ⟨x, hx_ball, hfx⟩ := hb_in_image t ht0 htC ht1
  have hx_norm := hx_boundary t ht0 htC ht1 x hx_ball hfx
  have hx_fixed := hx_fixed t ht0 htC ht1 x hx_ball hfx
  -- f_t t x = x so ‖seg b‖ = ‖x‖ = 1
  rw [← hfx, hx_fixed] at hb_norm
  linarith [hx_norm]
```

`G_t` is open so every point of `G_t` is an interior point of `G_t`, and since `G_t ⊆ closedBall 0 1`, every interior point of `G_t` is an interior point of `closedBall 0 1`:

```lean
have hp_interior : p t ht0 htC.le ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  apply interior_mono (hGt_subset t ht0 htC.le)
  rw [(hGt_open t ht0 htC).interior_eq]
```

[05/24/2026 20:33:01 +00:00] User:

Response:
No, the code does not need to be altered. The argument is:

- `e` was chosen as **any** point in `closedBall 0 1 \ G_t`
- We showed `‖e‖ = 1`, i.e. `e ∈ sphere 0 1`
- Since `e` was arbitrary in `closedBall 0 1 \ G_t`, this means `closedBall 0 1 \ G_t ⊆ sphere 0 1`
- Equivalently `interior (closedBall 0 1) ⊆ G_t`
- Combined with `G_t ⊆ interior (closedBall 0 1)`, we get `G_t = interior (closedBall 0 1)`

## The Deduction

```lean
have hGt_eq_interior : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 →
    G_t t = interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  apply Set.eq_of_subset_of_subset
  · -- G_t ⊆ interior B^n
    intro y hy
    apply interior_mono (hGt_subset t ht0 htC.le)
    rw [(hGt_open t ht0 htC).interior_eq]
    exact hy
  · -- interior B^n ⊆ G_t
    intro y hy
    by_contra hy_not_Gt
    -- y ∈ interior B^n but y ∉ G_t
    -- so y ∈ closedBall 0 1 \ G_t
    have hy_ball : y ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1 := interior_subset hy
    -- by he_boundary applied to y, ‖y‖ = 1
    -- but y ∈ interior B^n so ‖y‖ < 1, contradiction
    have hy_norm_lt : ‖y‖ < 1 := by

      exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mp hy

    -- we need to apply the same argument to y
    -- but he_boundary was proved for the specific e chosen
    -- the proof of he_boundary works for ANY point in closedBall \ G_t
    -- so we can repeat it for y

      -- same argument as he_boundary but for y instead of e
      sorry

```

## Why the Code Does Not Need to Change

The proof of `he_boundary` works for **any** point in `closedBall 0 1 \ G_t` — it never used any special property of `e` beyond:
- `e ∈ closedBall 0 1` 
- `e ∉ G_t`

So rather than reproving it, generalise `he_boundary` to work for any such point:

```lean
have hboundary_general : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 →
    ∀ y ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, y ∉ G_t t → ‖y‖ = 1 := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1 y hy_ball hy_not_Gt
  -- exact same proof as he_boundary but with y in place of e
  by_contra hy_not_sphere
  have hy_lt : ‖y‖ < 1 :=
    lt_of_le_of_ne (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp hy_ball) hy_not_sphere
  have hy_interior : y ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne']
    exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mpr hy_lt
  have hp_interior : p t ht0 htC.le ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    apply interior_mono (hGt_subset t ht0 htC.le)
    rw [(hGt_open t ht0 htC).interior_eq]
    exact hp t ht0 htC.le
  have hinterior_convex : Convex ℝ (interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) :=
    (convex_closedBall 0 1).interior
  -- Now we need to redo the segment argument with y in place of e
  -- This requires redefining seg, S, b for y
  -- which is why the code needs to be more general
  sorry
```

---

## The Real Issue

The segment argument (`seg`, `S`, `b`) was defined using the **specific** `e` chosen. To apply it to an arbitrary `y`, we need `seg`, `S`, `b` to take the endpoint as a parameter rather than using the specific `e`.

---

## Recommended Restructuring

Define `seg`, `S`, `b` with the endpoint as an explicit parameter:

```lean
-- Outside the theorem or as general have statements
let seg' : E → E → ℝ → E := fun start finish s =>
  AffineMap.lineMap start finish s
let S' : E → E → Set E → Set ℝ := fun start finish U =>
  {s ∈ Set.Icc 0 1 | AffineMap.lineMap start finish s ∈ U}
let b' : E → E → Set E → ℝ := fun start finish U =>
  sSup (S' start finish U)
```

Then the boundary argument becomes:

```lean
have hboundary_general : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 →
    ∀ y ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, y ∉ G_t t → ‖y‖ = 1 := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1 y hy_ball hy_not_Gt
  -- Apply the segment argument with p as start and y as finish
  -- using S' and b' parameterised by y
  sorry
```

This avoids duplicating the proof and makes the argument work for any `y`.

[05/24/2026 20:43:19 +00:00] User:
should Seg not be replaced?

Response:
Yes. Since `AffineMap.lineMap` is already the Mathlib definition of the line segment, `seg'` is just `AffineMap.lineMap` itself. So there is no need for `seg'` at all — just use `AffineMap.lineMap` directly everywhere with the endpoints as explicit arguments:

---

## Replace `seg` with `AffineMap.lineMap` Directly

```lean
-- Instead of
let seg := fun t ht0 htC ht1 => AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1)

-- Just use AffineMap.lineMap directly with explicit endpoints
-- S takes the endpoints explicitly
let S : E → E → Set ℝ := fun start finish =>
  {s ∈ Set.Icc 0 1 | AffineMap.lineMap start finish s ∈ G_t t}

let b : E → E → ℝ := fun start finish =>
  sSup (S start finish)
```

---

## Then the Boundary Argument Generalises

```lean
have hboundary_general : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 →
    ∀ y ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, y ∉ G_t t → ‖y‖ = 1 := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1 y hy_ball hy_not_Gt
  -- Apply segment argument from p to y
  let S_y := S (p t ht0 htC.le) y
  let b_y := b (p t ht0 htC.le) y
  -- S_y is nonempty since 0 ∈ S_y (lineMap p y 0 = p ∈ G_t)
  have hS_nonempty : S_y.Nonempty :=
    ⟨0, ⟨⟨le_refl 0, zero_le_one⟩, by
      simp [S_y, S, AffineMap.lineMap_apply_zero]
      exact hp t ht0 htC.le⟩⟩
  -- S_y is bounded above by 1
  have hS_bddAbove : BddAbove S_y :=
    ⟨1, fun s hs => hs.1.2⟩
  -- b_y ∈ [0, 1]
  have hb_mem : b_y ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) 1 := by
    constructor
    · exact le_csSup_of_le hS_bddAbove hS_nonempty.some_mem
        hS_nonempty.some_mem.1.1
    · exact csSup_le hS_nonempty (fun s hs => hs.1.2)
  -- lineMap p y b_y ∈ closure G_t
  have hb_closure : AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) y b_y ∈
      closure (G_t t) := by
    have hb_clos : b_y ∈ closure S_y :=
      csSup_mem_closure hS_nonempty hS_bddAbove
    apply ContinuousWithinAt.mem_closure (s := S_y)
    · exact AffineMap.lineMap_continuous.continuousWithinAt
    · exact hb_clos
    · intro s hs; exact hs.2
  -- lineMap p y b_y ∉ G_t
  have hb_not_Gt : AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) y b_y ∉ G_t t := by
    intro hb_in
    obtain ⟨ε, hε, hball⟩ := Metric.isOpen_iff.mp (hGt_open t ht0 htC) _ hb_in
    have hb_lt_one : b_y < 1 := by
      rcases eq_or_lt_of_le hb_mem.2 with hb1 | hb1
      · exfalso
        rw [← hb1, AffineMap.lineMap_apply_one] at hb_in
        exact hy_not_Gt hb_in
      · exact hb1
    let ε' := min ε (1 - b_y) / 3
    have hε'_pos : 0 < ε' := by
      apply div_pos _ (by norm_num)
      exact lt_min hε (by linarith)
    have hs'_le : b_y + ε' ≤ 1 := by
      unfold_let ε'; linarith [min_le_right ε (1 - b_y)]
    have hs'_close : dist
        (AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) y (b_y + ε'))
        (AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) y b_y) < ε := by
      rw [AffineMap.lineMap_apply, AffineMap.lineMap_apply, dist_eq_norm]
      simp only [vadd_eq_add, vsub_eq_sub]
      have hsimp : (b_y + ε') • (y - p t ht0 htC.le) + p t ht0 htC.le -
          (b_y • (y - p t ht0 htC.le) + p t ht0 htC.le) =
          ε' • (y - p t ht0 htC.le) := by
        simp [add_smul]; abel
      rw [hsimp, norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg hε'_pos.le]
      have hpe : ‖y - p t ht0 htC.le‖ ≤ 2 := by
        have hp_norm := mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp
          (hGt_subset t ht0 htC.le (hp t ht0 htC.le))
        linarith [norm_sub_le y (p t ht0 htC.le),
          mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp hy_ball]
      calc ε' * ‖y - p t ht0 htC.le‖
          ≤ ε' * 2 := by nlinarith
        _ < (min ε (1 - b_y) / 3) * 2 * (3 / 2) := by
            unfold_let ε'
            nlinarith [min_le_left ε (1 - b_y)]
        _ = min ε (1 - b_y) := by ring
        _ ≤ ε := min_le_left _ _
    linarith [le_csSup hS_bddAbove
      (show b_y + ε' ∈ S_y from ⟨⟨by linarith [hb_mem.1], hs'_le⟩,
        hball hs'_close⟩)]
  -- Get preimage x of lineMap p y b_y
  have hb_in_image : ∃ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      f_t t x = AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) y b_y := by
    have hclosed := hft_image_closed t ht0 ht1.le
    have hGt_sub_image : G_t t ⊆ f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1 :=
      fun z ⟨w, hw, hwz⟩ => ⟨w, interior_subset hw, hwz⟩
    exact hclosed.closure_subset
      (closure_mono hGt_sub_image hb_closure)
  obtain ⟨x, hx_ball, hfx⟩ := hb_in_image
  -- x is on the sphere
  have hx_not_interior : x ∉ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    intro hx_int
    exact hb_not_Gt ⟨x, hx_int, hfx⟩
  have hx_norm : ‖x‖ = 1 := by
    rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne'] at hx_not_interior
    simp only [mem_ball, dist_zero_right, not_lt] at hx_not_interior
    exact le_antisymm (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp hx_ball) hx_not_interior
  -- f_t t x = x since x is on the sphere
  have hx_fixed : f_t t x = x := by
    simp only [f_t, g]
    have hx_sphere : x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1 :=
      mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mpr hx_norm
    rw [hf_fixed x hx_sphere, sub_self, smul_zero, add_zero]
  -- lineMap p y b_y = x with ‖x‖ = 1
  -- but if y is in interior then lineMap p y b_y is in interior so ‖·‖ < 1
  by_contra hy_not_sphere
  have hy_lt : ‖y‖ < 1 :=
    lt_of_le_of_ne (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp hy_ball) hy_not_sphere
  have hy_interior : y ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne']
    exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mpr hy_lt
  have hp_interior : p t ht0 htC.le ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    apply interior_mono (hGt_subset t ht0 htC.le)
    rw [(hGt_open t ht0 htC).interior_eq]
    exact hp t ht0 htC.le
  have hb_interior : AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) y b_y ∈
      interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    (convex_closedBall 0 1).interior.lineMap_mem hp_interior hy_interior
      hb_mem
  have hb_norm : ‖AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) y b_y‖ < 1 := by
    rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne'] at hb_interior
    exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mp hb_interior
  rw [← hfx, hx_fixed] at hb_norm
  linarith
```

[05/24/2026 20:46:53 +00:00] User:
currently S is

let S : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 → Set ℝ :=
    fun t ht0 htC ht1 =>
    {s ∈ Set.Icc 0 1 | AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1) (s : ℝ) ∈ G_t t}

because the set is dependent on the value of t chosen, because we want to later say the integral is constant as t varies, should this not be included in t?

Response:
Yes, you are right. `S` depends on `t` through both `G_t t` and the endpoints `p t ...` and `e t ...`. The current definition already captures this since `t` is the first argument. However the proof arguments `ht0 htC ht1` are the problematic ones.

The cleaner definition takes `t` as data and the endpoints explicitly, separating the data from the proofs:

---

## Revised `S` Taking Endpoints Explicitly

```lean
let S : ℝ → E → E → Set ℝ := fun t start finish =>
  {s ∈ Set.Icc 0 1 | AffineMap.lineMap start finish s ∈ G_t t}
```

Then instantiate it with the specific endpoints:

```lean
-- For the specific e and p chosen
have hS_inst : ∀ t : ℝ, ∀ ht0 : 0 ≤ t, ∀ htC : t < t0, ∀ ht1 : t < 1,
    S t (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1) =
    {s ∈ Set.Icc 0 1 |
      AffineMap.lineMap (p t ht0 htC.le) (e t ht0 htC ht1) s ∈ G_t t} :=
  fun t ht0 htC ht1 => rfl
```

---

## Similarly for `b`

```lean
let b : ℝ → E → E → ℝ := fun t start finish =>
  sSup (S t start finish)
```

---

## Why This Is Better

| Before | After |
|---|---|
| `S t ht0 htC ht1` — carries proof args | `S t start finish` — only data args |
| Cannot reuse for arbitrary `y` | Can reuse for any endpoints |
| Causes metavariable leakage | No metavariable leakage |
| `b` depends on proofs | `b` depends only on data |

---

## The Integral `I(t)`

With this definition, `I(t)` can be defined cleanly as:

```lean
let I : ℝ → ℝ := fun t =>
  ∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)
```

Since `f_t t` depends only on `t` as data (not proofs), `I` is a well-defined function `ℝ → ℝ` that can be shown to be a polynomial and evaluated at `t = 0` and `t = 1`.

## Then `hGt_eq_interior` Follows Cleanly

```lean
have hGt_eq_interior : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 →
    G_t t = interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  apply Set.eq_of_subset_of_subset
  · -- G_t ⊆ interior B^n
    intro y hy
    apply interior_mono (hGt_subset t ht0 htC.le)
    rw [(hGt_open t ht0 htC).interior_eq]
    exact hy
  · -- interior B^n ⊆ G_t
    intro y hy
    by_contra hy_not_Gt
    have hy_ball : y ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1 := interior_subset hy
    have hy_norm_lt : ‖y‖ < 1 := by
      rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne'] at hy
      exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mp hy
    have hy_norm_eq : ‖y‖ = 1 :=
      hboundary_general t ht0 htC ht1 y hy_ball hy_not_Gt
    linarith
```

## Summary

The `choose e` approach was a dead end because it fixed a specific `e` that could not be reused. The correct structure is:

1. Remove `choose e he_ball he_Gt`
2. Move all the segment machinery (`S`, `b`, closure arguments) inside `hboundary_general`
3. State `hboundary_general` as the main lemma: any point in `closedBall 0 1 \ G_t` has norm `1`
4. Derive `hGt_eq_interior` from `hboundary_general`
5. Use `hGt_eq_interior` for the rest of the proof

## Where This Belongs

The `hboundary_general` proof is **self-contained** — it derives `‖e‖ = 1` from just:
- `hf_maps`, `hf_fixed`, `hft_cont`, `hGt_open`, `hGt_subset`
- The local definitions `G_t`, `f_t`, `g`

It does **not** need the bijectivity of `f_t`. So keeping it as a standalone `have` before the bijectivity argument is correct.

After `hx_fixed`, the proof of `hboundary_general` should conclude:

```lean

    by_contra he_not_sphere
    have he_lt : ‖e‖ < 1 :=
      lt_of_le_of_ne (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp he_ball) he_not_sphere

      rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne']
      exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mpr he_lt
```

[05/24/2026 22:01:13 +00:00] User:

```lean
have hGt_eq_interior : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 →
    G_t t = interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  apply Set.eq_of_subset_of_subset
  · -- G_t ⊆ interior B^n
    intro y hy
    apply interior_mono (hGt_subset t ht0 ht1.le)
    rw [(hGt_open t ht0 htC).interior_eq]
    exact hy
  · -- interior B^n ⊆ G_t
    intro y hy
    by_contra hy_not_Gt
    have hy_ball : y ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1 := interior_subset hy
    have hy_norm_lt : ‖y‖ < 1 := by
      rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne'] at hy
      exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mp hy
    have hy_norm_eq : ‖y‖ = 1 :=
      hboundary_general t ht0 htC ht1 y hy_ball hy_not_Gt
    linarith
```

---

## Why Each Step Works

### `G_t ⊆ interior B^n`

- `hGt_subset` gives `G_t t ⊆ closedBall 0 1`
- `interior_mono` lifts this to `interior (G_t t) ⊆ interior (closedBall 0 1)`
- `(hGt_open t ht0 htC).interior_eq` gives `interior (G_t t) = G_t t` since `G_t t` is open
- Together: `G_t t ⊆ interior (closedBall 0 1)`

### `interior B^n ⊆ G_t`

- Take `y ∈ interior (closedBall 0 1)`, assume `y ∉ G_t t`
- `hy_norm_lt : ‖y‖ < 1` from `y ∈ interior (closedBall 0 1)`
- `hboundary_general` gives `‖y‖ = 1`
- `linarith` derives `False` from `‖y‖ < 1` and `‖y‖ = 1`

```lean
have hft_bij : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 →
    Set.BijOn (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  refine ⟨?_, ?_, ?_⟩
  · -- MapsTo: f_t t maps closedBall to closedBall
    exact hft_maps t ⟨ht0, ht1.le⟩
  · -- InjOn: f_t t is injective on closedBall
    exact hft_inj t ht0 htC
  · -- SurjOn: f_t t maps closedBall onto closedBall
    intro y hy
    -- Split into interior and boundary cases
    rcases eq_or_lt_of_le (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp hy) with hy1 | hy1
    · -- y is on the sphere: f_t t y = y by hft_fixed
      refine ⟨y, hy, ?_⟩
      simp only [f_t, g]
      rw [hf_fixed y (mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mpr hy1.symm)]
      simp
    · -- y is in the interior: use hGt_eq_interior
      have hy_interior : y ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
        rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne']

      obtain ⟨x, hx_int, hfx⟩ := hy_interior
      exact ⟨x, interior_subset hx_int, hfx⟩
```

## The Change of Variables Formula

The key Mathlib theorem connecting `I(t)` to the volume is:

```lean
#check MeasureTheory.integral_image_eq_integral_abs_det_fderiv_smul
```

Which gives for a bijection `f_t t`:

$$I(t) = \int_{B^n} |\det Df_t| \, dx = \text{vol}(f_t(B^n)) = \text{vol}(B^n)$$

since `f_t t` is bijective on `closedBall 0 1` for `t < t0`:

```lean
have hI_const : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 →
    I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  simp only [I]
  rw [← MeasureTheory.integral_image_eq_integral_abs_det_fderiv_smul]
  · simp [(hft_bij t ht0 htC ht1).image_eq]
  · sorry -- f_t t is injective
  · sorry -- f_t t is differentiable
```

## Search Strategy

For Bochner integral lemmas, the naming convention is:

| Goal | Search term |
|---|---|
| `∫ _ in s, c` | `integral_const` |
| `∫ _ in s, 1` | `setIntegral_one` or `integral_one` |
| `∫⁻ _ in s, 1` | `setLIntegral_one` |
| Convert `∫⁻` to `∫` | `integral_toReal` |

So `MeasureTheory.setIntegral_one` is the most direct lemma for your goal.

```lean
have hcontra : False := by
  have hball_pos : 0 < (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
    apply ENNReal.toReal_pos
    · exact (measure_closedBall_pos volume (0 : E) one_pos).ne'
```

[05/24/2026 22:57:32 +00:00] User:
the argument is that as I(t) is constant on the interval t = 0 to t0, and I(t) is a polynomial, it is in fact constant for all t

Response:
The argument is:

1. `I(t)` is constant on `[0, t0)` (from `hI_const`)
2. `I(t)` is a polynomial in `t` (from the differentiability of `f_t`)
3. A polynomial that is constant on an interval is constant everywhere
4. Therefore `I(1) = I(0) = vol(B^n)`
5. But `I(1) = 0`, contradiction

---

## The Key Lemma

A polynomial constant on an open interval is constant everywhere:

```lean
#check Polynomial.funext
#check Set.eqOn_of_forall_eq
```

More directly, if a continuous function equals a constant on a dense set it equals that constant everywhere. Since `[0, t0)` has an accumulation point, the polynomial is determined:

```lean
have hI_const_all : ∀ t : ℝ, I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  -- I is analytic (polynomial) in t
  -- I equals vol(B^n) on [0, t0)
  -- a real analytic function constant on an interval is constant everywhere
  have hI_eq_on : Set.EqOn I (fun _ => (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal)
      (Set.Ico 0 t0) := by
    intro t ⟨ht0, htC⟩
    exact hI_const t ht0 htC (by linarith)
  -- I is continuous
  have hI_cont : Continuous I := by sorry
  -- The constant function is continuous
  -- They agree on [0, t0) which has an accumulation point
  -- so they agree everywhere by analytic continuation
  have haccum : AccPt 0 (Filter.principal (Set.Ico 0 t0)) := by
    rw [accPt_iff_nhds]
    intro U hU
    obtain ⟨ε, hε, hball⟩ := Metric.mem_nhds_iff.mp hU
    exact ⟨min (t0 / 2) (ε / 2), by
      simp [Set.mem_Ico]
      constructor
      · positivity
      · linarith,
      hball (by simp [dist_eq_norm]; linarith [min_le_right (t0/2) (ε/2)])⟩
  exact fun t => by
    have := hI_cont.continuousAt
    sorry
```

---

```lean
have hI_poly : ∃ P : Polynomial ℝ, ∀ t : ℝ, I t = P.eval t := by
  sorry
obtain ⟨P, hP⟩ := hI_poly
have hP_const : P = Polynomial.C ((volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal) := by
  apply Polynomial.funext
  intro t
  -- P agrees with the constant polynomial on [0, t0)
  -- polynomials agreeing on infinitely many points are equal
  sorry
have hI1 : I 1 = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  rw [hP 1, hP_const]
  simp
```

## Cleanest Route — Analytic Continuation via `AnalyticOn`

```lean
have hI_analytic : AnalyticOn ℝ I Set.univ := by sorry
have hI_const_all : ∀ t : ℝ, I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  have hconst_analytic : AnalyticOn ℝ
      (fun _ => (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal) Set.univ :=
    analyticOn_const
  apply fun t => (hI_analytic.eq_of_frequently_eq hconst_analytic
    (Set.univ_mem) ?_).symm ▸ rfl
  apply Filter.Frequently.mono (f := Filter.atTop)
  · intro t ht
    exact hI_eq_on ht
  · exact Filter.frequently_atTop.mpr (fun n => ⟨n, le_refl n, rfl⟩)
```

---

## Recommendation

The most rigorous route in Mathlib is:

```lean
have hI_const_all : ∀ t : ℝ, I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  have hI_sub : ∀ t ∈ Set.Ico (0 : ℝ) t0,
      I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal :=
    fun t ⟨ht0, htC⟩ => hI_const t ht0 htC (by linarith)
  -- I - const is analytic and zero on [0, t0)
  -- so zero everywhere by identity theorem
  have hI_sub_zero : ∀ t : ℝ, I t - (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal = 0 := by
    apply AnalyticOn.eq_zero_of_frequently_eq_zero (hI_analytic.sub analyticOn_const)
    apply Filter.frequently_of_forall
    exact fun t => by
      rcases lt_or_le t t0 with ht | ht
      · rcases lt_or_le 0 t with h0 | h0
        · exact sub_eq_zero.mpr (hI_sub t ⟨h0.le, ht⟩)
        · sorry
      · sorry
  intro t
  linarith [hI_sub_zero t]
```

The two `sorry`s handle the cases `t ≤ 0` and `t ≥ t0`, which require extending the constancy result. Share how `I` is defined as a polynomial and we can complete this precisely.

[05/24/2026 23:18:29 +00:00] User:
f_1 dot f_1 =1

df_i/dxi dot fi=0

this gives det(df1/dx1, df1/dx2, ... df1/dxn)= 0

Response:
This is the key computation showing `I(1) = 0`. The argument is:

- `f : B^n → S^(n-1)` means `‖f(x)‖ = 1` for all `x ∈ B^n`
- Differentiating `‖f(x)‖² = 1` gives `⟪f(x), Df(x) v⟫ = 0` for all `v`
- So each column `Df(x) eᵢ` is orthogonal to `f(x)`
- But `f(x)` is also a column direction, so the matrix `(Df(x) e₁, ..., Df(x) eₙ)` has all columns orthogonal to `f(x)`
- This means the columns are linearly dependent (they all lie in the hyperplane orthogonal to `f(x)`)
- Therefore `det(Df(x)) = 0`

---

## The Key Lemma

```lean
have hdet_zero : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t 1) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) = 0 := by
  intro x hx
  -- f_t 1 = f
  have hft1 : f_t 1 = f := by
    ext y
    simp [f_t, g]
  rw [hft1]
  -- ‖f x‖ = 1
  have hfx_sphere : f x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1 :=
    hf_maps x hx
  have hfx_norm : ‖f x‖ = 1 :=
    mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mp hfx_sphere
  -- Differentiating ‖f x‖² = 1 gives ⟪f x, Df(x) v⟫ = 0
  have horth : ∀ v : E, ⟪f x, fderiv ℝ f x v⟫_ℝ = 0 := by
    intro v
    have hconst : HasDerivAt (fun t : ℝ => ‖f (x + t • v)‖ ^ 2) 0 0 := by
      have := (hf_diff.hasDerivAt (x := x)).comp_hasDerivAt 0
        (hasDerivAt_id 0 |>.const_smul v |>.const_add x)
      sorry
    sorry
  -- All columns of Df(x) are orthogonal to f(x)
  -- So the image of Df(x) lies in (span {f x})⊥
  -- which has dimension n-1 < n
  -- Therefore det(Df(x)) = 0
  have hrange : LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) ≤
      (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ := by
    intro y hy
    obtain ⟨v, hv⟩ := hy
    rw [Submodule.mem_orthogonal_singleton_iff_inner_left]
    rw [← hv]
    exact horth v
  have hrank : finrank ℝ (LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)) < finrank ℝ E := by
    apply lt_of_le_of_lt (Submodule.finrank_le_finrank_of_le hrange)
    have hfx_ne : f x ≠ 0 := by
      intro h
      rw [h, norm_zero] at hfx_norm
      linarith
    rw [Submodule.finrank_orthogonal_span_singleton hfx_ne]
    omega
  -- A linear map whose range has dimension < n has det = 0
  exact LinearMap.det_eq_zero_of_range_lt_top (by
    rwa [← Submodule.finrank_lt_finrank_iff_lt_top])
```

---

## The Proof of `horth`

The correct proof differentiates `‖f(x)‖² = 1`:

```lean
have horth : ∀ v : E, @inner ℝ E _ (f x) (fderiv ℝ f x v) = 0 := by
  intro v
  have hf_diff_at : DifferentiableAt ℝ f x :=
    hf_diff.differentiable (by norm_num) |>.differentiableAt
  -- ‖f(·)‖² is constant 1 on closedBall
  -- so its derivative is 0
  have hconst : ∀ y ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, ‖f y‖ ^ 2 = 1 := by
    intro y hy
    rw [← mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mp (hf_maps y hy)]
    simp
  have hderiv_zero : fderiv ℝ (fun y => ‖f y‖ ^ 2) x = 0 := by
    apply fderiv_const_of_forall_mem (s := closedBall 0 1)
    · exact hx
    · exact isOpen_interior
    · intro y hy
      exact hconst y (interior_subset hy)
  -- fderiv of ‖f(·)‖² = 2 ⟪f(·), Df(·)⟫
  have hderiv_eq : fderiv ℝ (fun y => ‖f y‖ ^ 2) x v =
      2 * @inner ℝ E _ (f x) (fderiv ℝ f x v) := by
    have := (hf_diff_at.norm_sq).fderiv
    rw [this]
    simp [inner_fderiv_sq]
  linarith [congr_fun (congr_arg DFunLike.coe hderiv_zero) v,
            hderiv_eq]
```

```lean
have hf_differentiable : DifferentiableAt ℝ f x :=
  hf_diff.differentiable (by norm_num) |>.differentiableAt

have hf_hasFDerivAt : HasFDerivAt f (fderiv ℝ f x) x :=
  hf_differentiable.hasFDerivAt
```

## What It Needs to Say Mathematically

Differentiating `‖f(x)‖² = 1` with respect to `x` in direction `v`:

$$\frac{d}{dt}\bigg|_{t=0} \|f(x + tv)\|^2 = 2\langle f(x), Df(x)v \rangle = 0$$

---

## Suggested Proof Path

```lean
have horth : ∀ v : E, inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f x) (fderiv ℝ f x v) = (0 : ℝ) := by
  intro v
  have hf_diff_at : DifferentiableAt ℝ f x :=
    hf_diff.differentiable (by norm_num) |>.differentiableAt
  -- The function t ↦ ‖f(x + tv)‖² is constant 1
  have hconst : ∀ t : ℝ, ‖f (x + t • v)‖ ^ 2 = 1 := by
    intro t
    have hmem : x + t • v ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by sorry
    exact sq_eq_one_iff_of_ne_neg_one.mpr (Or.inl
      (mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mp (hf_maps hmem)))
  -- Its derivative at t = 0 is 0
  have hderiv : HasDerivAt (fun t : ℝ => ‖f (x + t • v)‖ ^ 2) 0 0 := by
    have := (hasDerivAt_const (0 : ℝ) (1 : ℝ)).congr_fun
      (fun t => (hconst t).symm) 0
    exact this
  -- Compute the derivative explicitly as 2⟪f x, Df(x) v⟫
  have hderiv_eq : HasDerivAt (fun t : ℝ => ‖f (x + t • v)‖ ^ 2)
      (2 * inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f x) (fderiv ℝ f x v)) 0 := by
    have hcomp : HasDerivAt (fun t : ℝ => f (x + t • v))
        (fderiv ℝ f x v) 0 := by
      have := hf_diff_at.hasFDerivAt.comp_hasDerivAt 0
        ((hasDerivAt_id (0 : ℝ)).smul_const v |>.const_add x)
      simp at this
      exact this
    have hnorm_sq : HasDerivAt (fun y : E => ‖y‖ ^ 2)
        (2 • (innerSL ℝ (f x))) (f x) := by
      exact hasDerivAt_norm_sq (f x)
    have := hnorm_sq.comp 0 hcomp
    simp [ContinuousLinearMap.comp_apply] at this
    convert this using 1
    simp [real_inner_comm, mul_comm]
  -- Equate the two derivatives
  have := hderiv.unique hderiv_eq
  linarith
```

---

## The Main `sorry`

The `sorry` for `hmem : x + t • v ∈ closedBall 0 1` is the problematic part — the function `t ↦ x + tv` does not stay in `closedBall 0 1` for all `t`. 

The fix is to not require `hconst` for all `t`, but only use the fact that `‖f‖² = 1` on `closedBall 0 1` and differentiate using the chain rule at `t = 0` where `x + 0 • v = x ∈ closedBall 0 1`:

```lean
  -- Instead of hconst for all t, use that f maps to sphere
  -- and differentiate the composition at t = 0
  have hfx_norm_sq : ‖f x‖ ^ 2 = 1 := by
    have := hf_maps hx
    rw [mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm] at this
    simp [this]
  -- The function ‖f(·)‖² = 1 on closedBall 0 1
  -- so its fderiv at x is 0
  have hfderiv_norm_sq : fderiv ℝ (fun y => ‖f y‖ ^ 2) x = 0 := by
    have hconst_on : ∀ y ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
        (fun y => ‖f y‖ ^ 2) y = 1 := by
      intro y hy
      have := hf_maps (interior_subset hy)
      rw [mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm] at this
      simp [this]
    have hx_int : x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
      rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne']
      exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mpr (by
        rcases eq_or_lt_of_le (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp hx) with h | h
        · sorry -- x on boundary, need separate argument
        · exact h)
    apply fderiv_const_of_mem_nhds
    · exact hconst_on
    · exact isOpen_interior.mem_nhds hx_int
  -- Apply this to direction v
  have hv : fderiv ℝ (fun y => ‖f y‖ ^ 2) x v = 0 :=
    congr_fun (congr_arg DFunLike.coe hfderiv_norm_sq) v
  -- Compute fderiv of ‖f(·)‖² using chain rule
  have hchain : fderiv ℝ (fun y => ‖f y‖ ^ 2) x v =
      2 * inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f x) (fderiv ℝ f x v) := by
    have hdiff : DifferentiableAt ℝ (fun y => ‖f y‖ ^ 2) x :=
      (hf_diff_at.norm_sq)
    rw [show (fun y => ‖f y‖ ^ 2) = (fun y => ‖y‖ ^ 2) ∘ f from rfl]
    rw [fderiv.comp x (differentiableAt_norm_sq (f x)) hf_diff_at]
    simp [fderiv_norm_sq, innerSL_apply, real_inner_comm]
  linarith [hv, hchain]
```

Response:
The issue is that `hf_maps` has type `Set.MapsTo f (closedBall 0 1) (sphere 0 1)`, which means it takes a membership proof, not a point. The correct application is:

```lean

    (fun y => ‖f y‖ ^ 2) y = 1 := by
  intro y hy
  have hmem : y ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1 := interior_subset hy
  have hfy := hf_maps hmem
  rw [mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm] at hfy
  simp [hfy]
```

---

## Why the Error Occurred

`Set.MapsTo f s t` unfolds to `∀ x ∈ s, f x ∈ t`, so `hf_maps` takes:
1. A point `x : E`
2. A proof `hx : x ∈ closedBall 0 1`

The original code wrote `hf_maps (interior_subset hy)` which passed the membership proof as the first argument (the point), causing the type mismatch. The fix is to pass `y` and `interior_subset hy` separately:

```lean
have hfy := hf_maps y (interior_subset hy)
-- or equivalently
have hfy : f y ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1 := hf_maps (interior_subset hy)
```

Wait — `Set.MapsTo` is defined as `∀ ⦃x⦄, x ∈ s → f x ∈ t`, so `x` is implicit. The correct call is just:

```lean
have hfy : f y ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1 := hf_maps (interior_subset hy)
```

This passes only the membership proof, with `y` inferred implicitly.
