[05/26/2026 00:45:21 +00:00] User:
without lean, why is f1 dot f1 = 1

Response:
Because `f` maps the closed ball `B^n` into the sphere `S^(n-1)`, which means every point in the image has norm exactly 1.

More precisely:

- `hf_maps : ∀ x ∈ closedBall 0 1, f x ∈ sphere 0 1`
- `sphere 0 1 = {y : E | ‖y‖ = 1}`
- So `‖f(x)‖ = 1` for all `x ∈ closedBall 0 1`
- Therefore `‖f(x)‖² = ⟪f(x), f(x)⟫_ℝ = 1`

---

## Why This Gives `det(Df(x)) = 0`

Differentiating `⟪f(x), f(x)⟫_ℝ = 1` with respect to `x` in any direction `v`:

$$\frac{d}{dt}\bigg|_{t=0} \langle f(x + tv), f(x + tv) \rangle = 0$$

By the product rule for inner products:

$$2\langle f(x), Df(x)v \rangle = 0$$

So every column `Df(x)eᵢ` of the Jacobian is **orthogonal to `f(x)`**. This means the image of `Df(x)` lies in the hyperplane:

$$H = \{v \in E \mid \langle f(x), v \rangle = 0\}$$

which has dimension `n - 1`. Since `Df(x) : E → E` maps an `n`-dimensional space into an `(n-1)`-dimensional subspace, it cannot be injective, so:

$$\det(Df(x)) = 0$$

[05/26/2026 00:49:00 +00:00] User:
what, with some lean and further explanation included, is needed to get from f1 . f1 = 1 to differentiating both sides w.r.t to x1 to obtain df/dxi . f = 0

Response:
The key steps are:

---

## 1. `f · f = 1` as a Function

We have the constant function:

```lean
have hconst : ∀ y ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, 
    inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f y) (f y) = 1 := by
  intro y hy
  have := hf_maps y hy
  rw [mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm] at this
  rw [real_inner_self_eq_norm_sq]
  simp [this]
```

---

## 2. The Function `y ↦ ⟪f(y), f(y)⟫` is Constant on `interior(B^n)`

```lean
have hconst_inner : ∀ y ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
    (fun y => inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f y) (f y)) y = 1 :=
  fun y hy => hconst y (interior_subset hy)
```

---

## 3. The Derivative of a Constant is Zero

Since `y ↦ ⟪f(y), f(y)⟫` equals `1` on the open set `interior(B^n)`, its Fréchet derivative at any interior point `x` is zero:

```lean
have hfderiv_inner_zero : fderiv ℝ (fun y => inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f y) (f y)) x = 0 := by
  apply fderiv_const_of_mem_nhds (c := 1)
  · exact hconst_inner
  · exact isOpen_interior.mem_nhds hx
```

---

## 4. Computing the Derivative via the Chain Rule

The derivative of `y ↦ ⟪f(y), f(y)⟫` at `x` in direction `v` is computed by the product rule for inner products:

$$\frac{d}{dt}\bigg|_{t=0} \langle f(x+tv), f(x+tv) \rangle = \langle Df(x)v, f(x) \rangle + \langle f(x), Df(x)v \rangle = 2\langle f(x), Df(x)v \rangle$$

In Lean:

```lean
have hderiv_eq : ∀ v : E, 
    fderiv ℝ (fun y => inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f y) (f y)) x v =
    2 * inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f x) (fderiv ℝ f x v) := by
  intro v
  have hf_diff_at : DifferentiableAt ℝ f x :=
    hf_diff.differentiable (by norm_num) |>.differentiableAt
  -- The derivative of ⟪f(·), f(·)⟫ = ⟪Df(·)v, f(·)⟫ + ⟪f(·), Df(·)v⟫
  have := (hf_diff_at.inner hf_diff_at).hasFDerivAt.fderiv
  rw [this]
  simp [fderiv_inner, real_inner_comm]
  ring
```

---

## 5. Combining Steps 3 and 4

Since the derivative is both `0` (step 3) and `2⟪f(x), Df(x)v⟫` (step 4):

```lean
have horth : ∀ v : E, inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f x) (fderiv ℝ f x v) = 0 := by
  intro v
  have hzero : fderiv ℝ (fun y => inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f y) (f y)) x v = 0 :=
    congr_fun (congr_arg DFunLike.coe hfderiv_inner_zero) v
  have heq := hderiv_eq v
  linarith
```

---

## Summary of the Chain

$$\underbrace{\langle f(y), f(y) \rangle = 1}_{\text{constant on } B^n}$$

$$\Downarrow \text{ derivative of constant = 0}$$

$$\underbrace{\frac{d}{dt}\bigg|_{t=0} \langle f(x+tv), f(x+tv) \rangle = 0}_{\text{fderiv = 0}}$$

$$\Downarrow \text{ product rule for inner product}$$

$$\underbrace{2\langle f(x), Df(x)v \rangle = 0}_{\text{orthogonality}}$$

$$\Downarrow \text{ for all } v$$

$$\underbrace{\text{image}(Df(x)) \subseteq f(x)^\perp}_{\text{rank} \leq n-1}$$

$$\Downarrow$$

$$\underbrace{\det(Df(x)) = 0}_{\text{rank deficient}}$$

[05/26/2026 00:53:42 +00:00] User:

The statement should be changed to only quantify over interior points, and `hx` should be `hx : x ∈ interior (closedBall 0 1)` so that `isOpen_interior.mem_nhds hx` works directly:

```lean

    LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t 1) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) = 0 := by
  intro x hx
  have hft1 : f_t 1 = f := by
    ext y; simp [f_t, g]
  rw [hft1]
  have hfx_sphere : f x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1 :=
    hf_maps x (interior_subset hx)
  have hfx_norm : ‖f x‖ = 1 := mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mp hfx_sphere
  have hconst_on : ∀ y ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
      (fun y => inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f y) (f y)) y = 1 := by
    intro y hy

    rw [real_inner_self_eq_norm_sq]
    simp [hfy]

    apply hasFDerivAt_zero_of_eventually_const (1 : ℝ)
    apply Filter.eventually_of_mem (isOpen_interior.mem_nhds hx)
    exact hconst_on
```

| Before | After |
|---|---|
| `∀ x ∈ closedBall 0 1` | `∀ x ∈ interior (closedBall 0 1)` |
| `hx : x ∈ closedBall 0 1` | `hx : x ∈ interior (closedBall 0 1)` |
| `hf_maps x hx` | `hf_maps x (interior_subset hx)` |
| `‖f y‖² = 1` | `⟪f y, f y⟫ = 1` (more direct for differentiation) |
| `isOpen_interior.mem_nhds hx` fails | `isOpen_interior.mem_nhds hx` works |

## Step 1 — Extract `horth` from `hfderiv_inner_zero`

```lean
have horth : ∀ v : E, inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f x) (fderiv ℝ f x v) = 0 := by
  intro v
  have hf_diff_at : DifferentiableAt ℝ f x :=
    hf_diff.differentiable (by norm_num) |>.differentiableAt
  -- Compute fderiv of ⟪f(·), f(·)⟫ using chain rule
  have hchain : fderiv ℝ (fun y => inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f y) (f y)) x v =
      2 * inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f x) (fderiv ℝ f x v) := by
    have hd := (hf_diff_at.inner hf_diff_at).hasFDerivAt.fderiv
    rw [show (fun y => inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f y) (f y)) =
        (fun y => inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f y) (f y)) from rfl] at hd
    rw [hd]
    simp [ContinuousLinearMap.add_apply, real_inner_comm]
    ring
  have hzero : fderiv ℝ (fun y => inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f y) (f y)) x v = 0 :=
    congr_fun (congr_arg DFunLike.coe hfderiv_inner_zero) v
```

[05/26/2026 14:12:39 +00:00] User:
what, intuitively does horth tell us, (if we were to try and represent it with vectors and matrices)

and in lean do we argue for the desired result that the determinant is zero? we should have that as, thinking of fderiv a matrix that each row is orthogonal, and so it has zero determinant

Response:
## Intuition

`horth` says:

$$\langle f(x), Df(x) \cdot v \rangle = 0 \quad \forall v \in \mathbb{R}^n$$

In matrix terms, if we write `f(x)` as a column vector and `Df(x)` as an `n × n` matrix, this says:

$$f(x)^T \cdot Df(x) \cdot v = 0 \quad \forall v$$

which means:

$$f(x)^T \cdot Df(x) = 0$$

i.e. **every row of `Df(x)` is orthogonal to `f(x)`**. Equivalently, **every column of `Df(x)` is orthogonal to `f(x)`**.

So the image of `Df(x)` lies entirely in the hyperplane:

$$H = \{w \in \mathbb{R}^n \mid \langle f(x), w \rangle = 0\}$$

which has dimension `n - 1`. Since `Df(x)` maps `ℝⁿ` into an `(n-1)`-dimensional subspace, it cannot be surjective, hence it is not invertible, hence:

$$\det(Df(x)) = 0$$

---

## In Lean

The argument goes:

### Step 1 — Image of `fderiv ℝ f x` lies in `(f x)⊥`

```lean
have hrange : ∀ v : E, fderiv ℝ f x v ∈ (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ := by
  intro v
  rw [Submodule.mem_orthogonal_singleton_iff_inner_left]
  exact horth v
```

### Step 2 — `(f x)⊥` has dimension `n - 1`

```lean
have hfx_ne : f x ≠ 0 := by
  intro h
  rw [h, norm_zero] at hfx_norm
  linarith
have hdim : finrank ℝ (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ = n - 1 := by
  rw [Submodule.finrank_orthogonal_span_singleton hfx_ne]
```

### Step 3 — `fderiv ℝ f x` is not injective

```lean
have hrange_le : LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) ≤
    (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ := by
  intro w hw
  obtain ⟨v, hv⟩ := hw
  rw [← hv]
  exact hrange v
have hrank_lt : finrank ℝ (LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)) < n := by
  calc finrank ℝ (LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E))
      ≤ finrank ℝ (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ :=
          Submodule.finrank_le_finrank_of_le hrange_le
    _ = n - 1 := hdim
    _ < n := Nat.sub_lt (Module.finrank_pos) one_pos
have hnotinj : ¬ Function.Injective (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) := by
  intro hinj
  have := LinearMap.finrank_range_of_injective hinj
  linarith
```

### Step 4 — Det is Zero

```lean

  rwa [LinearMap.det_eq_zero_iff_not_injective]
```

The correct way to show `finrank` is monotone for submodules is:

```lean
Submodule.finrank_mono
```

or via the inclusion map. Try:

```lean
have hrank_lt : Module.finrank ℝ (LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)) < n := by
  calc Module.finrank ℝ (LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E))
      ≤ Module.finrank ℝ (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ :=
          Submodule.finrank_mono hrange_le
    _ = n - 1 := hdim
    _ < n := Nat.sub_lt Module.finrank_pos one_pos
```

---

## If `Submodule.finrank_mono` Does Not Exist

Use `Submodule.finrank_le_finrank_of_le` via the rank comparison:

```lean
have hrank_lt : Module.finrank ℝ (LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)) < n := by
  have hle : Module.finrank ℝ (LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)) ≤
      Module.finrank ℝ (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ := by
    apply Module.finrank_le_finrank_of_rank_le_rank
    · exact Submodule.rank_mono hrange_le
    · exact (Submodule.finite_dimensional_of_finrank_eq_succ
        (by rw [hdim]; omega)).rank_lt_aleph0
  linarith [hdim.symm ▸ hle, Nat.sub_lt Module.finrank_pos one_pos]
```

---

## Most Direct — Avoid the Intermediate Step

```lean
have hrank_lt : Module.finrank ℝ (LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)) < n := by
  have hle : Module.finrank ℝ (LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)) ≤ n - 1 := by
    calc Module.finrank ℝ (LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E))
        ≤ Module.finrank ℝ (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ :=
            Submodule.finrank_mono hrange_le
      _ = n - 1 := hdim
  linarith [Nat.sub_lt Module.finrank_pos one_pos]
```

## Or in One Step

```lean
have hdet : LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) = 0 := by
  rw [LinearMap.det_eq_zero_iff_ker_ne_bot, Ne, LinearMap.ker_eq_bot]
  exact hnotinj
```

---

## Why This Works

The chain is:

$$\det(Df(x)) = 0 \iff \ker(Df(x)) \neq \bot \iff \neg\text{Injective}(Df(x))$$

- `LinearMap.det_eq_zero_iff_ker_ne_bot` gives the first equivalence
- `LinearMap.ker_eq_bot` gives `ker f = ⊥ ↔ Injective f`, so `ker f ≠ ⊥ ↔ ¬Injective f`
- `hnotinj : ¬Function.Injective (fderiv ℝ f x)` closes the goal

## Fix — Provide the `Fact` Instance

---

## Why This Is Needed

`finrank_orthogonal_span_singleton` [doc1] has signature:

```lean
theorem finrank_orthogonal_span_singleton 
    [Fact (finrank 𝕜 E = n + 1)] {v : E} (hv : v ≠ 0) :
    finrank 𝕜 (span 𝕜 {v})ᗮ = n
```

It requires `Fact (finrank ℝ E = n + 1)` as a typeclass instance [doc1]. The `haveI` provides this instance locally with `n - 1 + 1 = n` closed by `omega` [doc1].

---

## Alternative — Use `Submodule.finrank_add_finrank_orthogonal` Instead

Avoid the `Fact` requirement entirely by using the dimension sum formula [doc1]:

```lean
have hdim : Module.finrank ℝ (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ = n - 1 := by
  have hspan : Module.finrank ℝ (Submodule.span ℝ {f x}) = 1 := by
    rw [Module.finrank_span_singleton hfx_ne]
  have hsum := Submodule.finrank_add_finrank_orthogonal (K := Submodule.span ℝ {f x})
  omega
```

This uses `finrank(K) + finrank(Kᗮ) = finrank(E)` [doc1], which gives `1 + finrank(Kᗮ) = n`, so `finrank(Kᗮ) = n - 1` by `omega`.

```lean
    rw [Filter.mem_ae_iff]
    simp only [Set.compl_compl]
    exact Measure.addHaar_sphere_of_ne_zero volume 0 one_ne_zero
  · -- The integrand is zero on the interior
```

Response:
The goal is asking for the measure of the complement of `ball 0 1` within `closedBall 0 1`, which is just the sphere `sphere 0 1`:

```lean

  rw [show (ball (0 : E) 1)ᶜ ∩ closedBall (0 : E) 1 = sphere (0 : E) 1 from by
    ext x
    simp [mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm, mem_ball_zero_iff, mem_closedBall_zero_iff,
      not_lt, le_antisymm_iff]]
  exact Measure.addHaar_sphere_of_ne_zero volume 0 one_ne_zero
```

---

## Why This Works

$$(\text{ball } 0 \, 1)^c \cap \text{closedBall } 0 \, 1 = \{x \mid \|x\| \geq 1\} \cap \{x \mid \|x\| \leq 1\} = \{x \mid \|x\| = 1\} = \text{sphere } 0 \, 1$$

The `simp` with `le_antisymm_iff` handles `‖x‖ ≥ 1 ∧ ‖x‖ ≤ 1 ↔ ‖x‖ = 1`.

Response:
The key idea is that `f_t t` is a bijection on `closedBall 0 1` for `t < t0`, so by the change of variables formula, the integral of the Jacobian equals the volume of the image, which equals the volume of `closedBall 0 1`.

---

## The Change of Variables Formula

```lean
have hI_const : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 →
    I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  simp only [I]
  -- f_t t is bijective on closedBall 0 1
  have hbij := hft_bij t ht0 htC ht1
  -- f_t t is differentiable
  have hft_diff : ∀ x, HasFDerivAt (f_t t) 
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x :=
    hft_strict_fderiv t ht0 htC
  -- Use change of variables
  rw [← hbij.image_eq]
  rw [← MeasureTheory.integral_image_eq_integral_abs_det_fderiv_smul volume
    (fun x _ => (hft_diff x).differentiableAt) hbij.injOn]
  simp [abs_of_pos]
  sorry
```

---

## More Direct — Use That the Image Has the Same Volume

Since `f_t t` is a bijection from `closedBall 0 1` to itself:

```lean
have hI_const : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 →
    I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1
  simp only [I]
  have hbij := hft_bij t ht0 htC ht1
  -- The integral of det(Df_t) over B^n equals vol(f_t(B^n)) = vol(B^n)
  have himage_eq : f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1 = closedBall (0 : E) 1 :=
    hbij.image_eq
  rw [show ∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) =
      (volume (f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal from by
    rw [MeasureTheory.integral_det_fderiv_eq_volume_image]
    · exact fun x _ => (hft_strict_fderiv t ht0 htC x).differentiableAt
    · exact hbij.injOn]
  rw [himage_eq]
```

## The Key Mathlib Theorem

```lean
#check MeasureTheory.integral_abs_det_fderiv_eq_addHaar_image
#check MeasureTheory.addHaar_image_le_lintegral_abs_det_fderiv
#check MeasureTheory.lintegral_abs_det_fderiv_eq_addHaar_image
```

The most relevant is:

```lean
#check MeasureTheory.integral_image_eq_integral_abs_det_fderiv_smul
```

Which for a function `f` injective on `s` with `f '' s = s` gives:

$$\int_s |\det Df| \, d\mu = \mu(f(s)) = \mu(s)$$

---

## Recommendation

The proof requires connecting `I(t) = ∫ det(Df_t)` to `vol(B^n)` via the change of variables theorem. The exact Mathlib lemma needed is:

```lean
#check MeasureTheory.integral_det_fderiv_smul_eq_volume
```

Run `exact?` or `apply?` after `simp only [I]` to find the precise lemma available in your Mathlib version.

[05/27/2026 12:49:59 +00:00] User:
theorem MeasureTheory.integral_image_eq_integral_abs_det_fderiv_smul {E : Type u_1} {F : Type u_2} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [NormedSpace ℝ E] [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] [NormedAddCommGroup F] [NormedSpace ℝ F] {s : Set E} {f : E → E} {f' : E → E →L[ℝ] E} [MeasurableSpace E] [BorelSpace E] (μ : Measure E) [μ.IsAddHaarMeasure] (hs : MeasurableSet s) (hf' : ∀ x ∈ s, HasFDerivWithinAt f (f' x) s x) (hf : Set.InjOn f s) (g : E → F) :
∫ (x : E) in f '' s, g x ∂μ = ∫ (x : E) in s, |(f' x).det| • g (f x) ∂μ

Change of variable formula for differentiable functions: if a function f is injective and differentiable on a measurable set s, then the Bochner integral of a function g : E → F on f '' s coincides with the integral of |(f' x).det| • g ∘ f on s.

is the change of variables formula

```lean

    I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by

      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) (closedBall 0 1) x :=
    fun x hx => (hft_strict_fderiv t ht0 htC x hx).hasFDerivAt.hasFDerivWithinAt
  -- Apply change of variables with g = 1
  have hcov := MeasureTheory.integral_image_eq_integral_abs_det_fderiv_smul
    volume measurableSet_closedBall hft_diffwithin hbij.injOn (fun _ => (1 : ℝ))
  rw [hbij.image_eq] at hcov
  simp only [smul_eq_mul, mul_one] at hcov
  rw [MeasureTheory.integral_one, MeasureTheory.integral_one] at hcov
  -- hcov : vol(B^n) = ∫ |det(Df_t)| 
  -- but we need ∫ det(Df_t) = vol(B^n)
  -- det is positive since f_t t is orientation preserving
```

## The Remaining Issue

The change of variables gives `∫ |det(Df_t)|` but `I(t) = ∫ det(Df_t)`. We need to show `det(Df_t(x)) > 0` to remove the absolute value. This follows from:

- At `t = 0`, `det(Df_0) = det(id) = 1 > 0`
- `det(Df_t)` is continuous in `t`
- `det(Df_t) ≠ 0` for `t < t0` (from `hft_nonsingular`)
- By connectedness, `det(Df_t) > 0` for all `t < t0`

```lean
have hdet_pos : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    0 < LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) := by
  sorry
```

```lean

    |(ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det| =
    LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) := by

    LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) =
    ∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,

  · exact (habs_eq x hx).symm
```

## Root Cause

The timeout is caused by Lean trying to unify the derivative expression `ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x` with what `HasStrictFDerivAt.hasFDerivAt` produces. The elaborator gets stuck in a loop checking definitional equality. Increasing heartbeats or using `apply` instead of `:=` avoids the loop.

## The Three Steps Needed

### Step 1 — Rewrite `fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x` as `id + t • fderiv ℝ g x`

Using `this` which says `HasStrictFDerivAt (f_t t) (id + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x`:

```lean

    (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) = 
    (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x : E →L[ℝ] E) := by
  intro x hx
  congr 1
  exact (this x hx).hasFDerivAt.fderiv
```

Since `det(id + t • Dg(x)) > 0` (the map is orientation preserving for small `t`):

```lean

    |(ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det| =
    (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det := by
  intro x hx
  exact abs_of_pos (hdet_pos x hx)
```

### Step 3 — Connect `volume.real` to `(volume).toReal`

```lean

    (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := rfl
```

[05/27/2026 14:27:06 +00:00] User:

Response:
Let me search for information about this timeout issue.
The timeout is not about the mathematical content — you are right that `ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x` is just the sum of two terms of type `E →L[ℝ] E`. The issue is a **typeclass elaboration problem** [doc1][doc2].

---

## Why the Timeout Occurs

When Lean sees `ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x`, it needs to find:

1. An `Add` instance for `E →L[ℝ] E`
2. An `SMul ℝ (E →L[ℝ] E)` instance for the `t •` part
3. Then unify the result with `E →ₗ[ℝ] E` via a coercion

The coercion from `E →L[ℝ] E` to `E →ₗ[ℝ] E` triggers a long chain of instance searches [doc1], and when combined with the `+` and `•` operations, Lean gets stuck in a loop trying to resolve which `Add` instance to use [doc2].

---

## The Fix — Avoid the Coercion in the Statement

Instead of coercing to `E →ₗ[ℝ] E`, keep everything as `E →L[ℝ] E` and only coerce when applying `LinearMap.det`:

```lean
have hfderiv_eq : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x = 
    ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x := by
  intro x hx
  exact (this x hx).hasFDerivAt.fderiv
```

Then when you need `LinearMap.det`, coerce at the point of use:

```lean
LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)
= LinearMap.det ((ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x : E →L[ℝ] E) : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)
```

---

## Alternative — Use `set_option maxHeartbeats`

```lean
set_option maxHeartbeats 800000 in
have hfderiv_eq : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) = 
    ((ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x : E →L[ℝ] E) : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) := by
  intro x hx
  congr 1
  exact (this x hx).hasFDerivAt.fderiv
```

---

## Root Cause Summary

| Issue | Cause |
|---|---|
| Timeout | Coercion `E →L[ℝ] E → E →ₗ[ℝ] E` triggers long instance search |
| Why `+` makes it worse | `Add (E →L[ℝ] E)` and `Add (E →ₗ[ℝ] E)` are different instances |
| Fix | Keep types as `E →L[ℝ] E` throughout, coerce only at point of use |

## Why `hstrict` Was Unknown

```lean

```

This tries to partially apply `hft_strict_fderiv` to `t ht0 htC`, but since `hft_strict_fderiv` uses `∀ x ∈ ...` (which is `∀ x, x ∈ ... →`), Lean may not accept the partial application as a standalone term. Providing all arguments `t ht0 htC x hx` at once avoids this.

---

## Root Cause

The `whnf` timeout suggests that `HasStrictFDerivAt.hasFDerivAt` triggers reduction of the derivative term `ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x`, which involves:

- `fderiv ℝ g x` — requires unfolding `g`
- `g` is a `let` binding: `fun x => f x - x`
- Unfolding `g` triggers unfolding of `f_t`, which triggers more unfolding

The fix is to **prevent unfolding** of `g` by using `change` or `show`:

```lean
have h2 : HasFDerivAt (f_t t) (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x := by
  have := h1.hasFDerivAt
  convert this using 1
```

Or unfold `g` explicitly before the elaboration:

```lean
simp only [g] at h1
have h2 := h1.hasFDerivAt
```

## Most Likely Root Cause

The real issue is that `hft_strict_fderiv` was proved using `ContDiff.hasStrictFDerivAt`, which internally uses a different representation of the derivative than `ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x`. When Lean tries to unify these two representations, it gets stuck.

Check what `h1` actually says after `simp only [g, f_t] at h1`:


[05/28/2026 13:04:19 +00:00] User:

Response:
## The Difference

- `E →L[ℝ] E` — **ContinuousLinearMap**: a linear map that is also continuous, bundled with a continuity proof
- `E →ₗ[ℝ] E` — **LinearMap**: just a linear map, no continuity requirement

`fderiv ℝ f x` has type `E →L[ℝ] E` (continuous linear map), but `LinearMap.det` expects `E →ₗ[ℝ] E` (plain linear map). The coercion `(fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)` forgets the continuity.

---

## Why This Causes the Timeout

When Lean sees:
```lean
LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)
```

It needs to:
1. Elaborate `fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →L[ℝ] E`
2. Apply the coercion `E →L[ℝ] E → E →ₗ[ℝ] E`
3. Find `LinearMap.det` for `E →ₗ[ℝ] E`

Step 2 requires finding `ContinuousLinearMap.toLinearMap` which triggers instance search on `E →L[ℝ] E`, causing the loop.

---

## Fix — Use `ContinuousLinearMap.det` Instead

Check if there is a `det` directly for `E →L[ℝ] E`:

```lean

```

Or define `I` using `ContinuousLinearMap.det` directly:

```lean

  ∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x).det ∂volume
```

This avoids the coercion entirely since `.det` on `E →L[ℝ] E` should be directly available.

[05/28/2026 16:59:09 +00:00] User:
rfl did not close the goal
⊢ LinearMap.det ↑(fderiv ℝ (fun y ↦ y + t • (f y - y)) x) = |(ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det|

there's no lemma stating that the determinant is positive, state and show, with an explanation of why

Response:
## Why the Determinant is Positive

At `t = 0`, `f_t 0 = id` so `fderiv ℝ (f_t 0) x = id` and `det(id) = 1 > 0`. As `t` varies continuously from `0` to `t0`, the determinant varies continuously and is never zero (since `f_t t` is a local homeomorphism for `t < t0`). By the intermediate value theorem, since `det > 0` at `t = 0` and `det ≠ 0` throughout, `det > 0` for all `t ∈ [0, t0)`.

---

## Statement and Proof

```lean
have hdet_pos : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    0 < (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det := by
  intro x hx
  -- The determinant is nonzero since the map is a unit
  have hunit := hft_nonsingular t ht0 htC x hx
  have hdet_ne : (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det ≠ 0 := by
    intro h
    rw [ContinuousLinearMap.det] at h
    have := LinearMap.isUnit_iff_det_ne_zero.mpr
    sorry
  -- The determinant is positive by continuity from t = 0
  -- At t = 0, det = 1 > 0
  have hdet_zero : (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + (0 : ℝ) • fderiv ℝ g x).det = 1 := by
    simp [ContinuousLinearMap.det]
  -- det is continuous in t
  have hdet_cont : Continuous (fun s =>
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det) := by
    fun_prop
  -- det is never zero on [0, t]
  have hdet_never_zero : ∀ s ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) t,
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det ≠ 0 := by
    intro s hs
    have hunit_s := hft_nonsingular s hs.1 (lt_of_le_of_lt hs.2 htC) x hx
    intro h
    apply hunit_s.ne_zero
    ext v
    simp [ContinuousLinearMap.ext_iff]
    sorry
  -- By IVT, det > 0 throughout since det(0) = 1 > 0 and det never crosses 0
  have hpos_zero : 0 < (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + (0 : ℝ) • fderiv ℝ g x).det := by
    rw [hdet_zero]; norm_num
  exact pos_of_ne_zero_of_nonneg_of_continuous_of_pos
    hdet_cont (Set.left_mem_Icc.mpr ht0)
    (Set.right_mem_Icc.mpr le_rfl)
    hdet_never_zero hpos_zero
```

---

## Cleaner Approach — Use `IsConnected` and Continuity

The cleanest argument avoids IVT directly:

```lean
have hdet_pos : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    0 < (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det := by
  intro x hx
  -- det is a continuous function of s on [0, t]
  -- det(s) ≠ 0 for all s ∈ [0, t] (since f_t s is nonsingular)
  -- det(0) = 1 > 0
  -- so det(t) > 0 by connectedness
  have hcont : ContinuousOn (fun s =>
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det)
      (Set.Icc 0 t) := by fun_prop
  have hne_zero : ∀ s ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) t,
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det ≠ 0 := by
    intro s ⟨hs0, hst⟩
    have hunit_s := hft_nonsingular s hs0 (hst.trans_lt htC) x hx
    rwa [Ne, ← ContinuousLinearMap.isUnit_iff_ne_zero_det]
  have hpos_at_zero : 0 < (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E +
      (0 : ℝ) • fderiv ℝ g x).det := by
    simp
  -- Since det is continuous, never zero, and positive at 0,
  -- it must be positive at t
  have hconn := isPreconnected_Icc (a := (0:ℝ)) (b := t)
  by_contra hle
  push_neg at hle
  have hlt : (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det < 0 :=
    lt_of_le_of_ne hle (hne_zero t ⟨ht0, le_refl t⟩)
  -- IVT gives a zero, contradiction
  obtain ⟨s, hs_mem, hs_zero⟩ := intermediate_value_Icc ht0 hcont
    (le_of_lt hpos_at_zero) (le_of_lt hlt) (le_refl 0)
  exact hne_zero s hs_mem hs_zero
```

theorem cont_diff_ball_to_sphere_no_fixed [Nontrivial E]
    (f : E → E) (hf_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 f)
    (hf_maps : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1)
    (hf_fixed : ∀ x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1, f x = x) : False := by
  -- change cont_diff to ContDiffOn closedBall (0 : E) 1
  let g : E → E := fun x => f x - x
  let f_t : ℝ → E → E := fun t x => x + t • g x
  have hgcont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g := hf_diff.sub contDiff_id
  have hg_lipschitz : ∃ K : NNReal, LipschitzOnWith K g (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    apply ContDiffOn.exists_lipschitzOnWith
    · exact hgcont_diff.contDiffOn
    · norm_num
    · exact convex_closedBall 0 1
    · exact isCompact_closedBall 0 1

  have hft_cont : ∀ t : ℝ, Continuous (f_t t) := by fun_prop
  obtain ⟨C, hC⟩ := hg_lipschitz
  have hfx : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ closedBall 0 1 := by
    intro x
    rw [mem_closedBall_zero_iff]
    intro hx
    exact le_of_eq (hf_maps x (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mpr hx))
  have hft_maps : ∀ t ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) 1,
      Set.MapsTo (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    intro t ⟨ht0, ht1⟩ x hx
    simp only [f_t, g]
    rw [smul_sub, add_sub_assoc' x, add_sub_right_comm]
    have : (1 - t) • x = x - t • x := by
      rw [sub_smul]
      simp
    rw [← this]
    have h1t : 0 ≤ 1 - t := sub_nonneg_of_le ht1

```lean
lemma injOn_of_lipschitz_lt_one ...
lemma mapsTo_interpolation ...

-- Main theorem uses the lemmas
set_option maxHeartbeats 800000 in
theorem cont_diff_ball_to_sphere_no_fixed [Nontrivial E]
    (f : E → E) (hf_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 f)
    (hf_maps : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1)
    (hf_fixed : ∀ x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1, f x = x) : False := by
  let g : E → E := fun x => f x - x
  let f_t : ℝ → E → E := fun t x => x + t • g x
  have hgcont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g := hf_diff.sub contDiff_id
  obtain ⟨C, hC⟩ : ∃ K : NNReal, LipschitzOnWith K g (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    apply ContDiffOn.exists_lipschitzOnWith hgcont_diff.contDiffOn (by norm_num)
      (convex_closedBall 0 1) (isCompact_closedBall 0 1)
  have hfx : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ closedBall 0 1 :=
    fun x hx => mem_closedBall.mpr (le_of_eq (hf_maps x (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mpr
      (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp hx))))
  have hft_maps : ∀ t ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) 1,
      Set.MapsTo (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    fun t ⟨ht0, ht1⟩ => mapsTo_interpolation hfx ht0 ht1
  have hft_inj : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < 1 / C →
      Set.InjOn (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    fun t ht0 htC => injOn_of_lipschitz_lt_one hC ht0 htC
  ...
```

## Why

```lean
lemma mapsTo_interpolation {f : E → E}
    (hfx : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ closedBall 0 1)
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) (ht1 : t ≤ 1) :
    Set.MapsTo (fun x => x + t • (f x - x)) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1)
```

So it takes `hfx`, `ht0`, `ht1` directly without needing to bundle them into `Set.Icc`. The `.le` converts `ht1 : t < 1` to `t ≤ 1` if needed.

Response:
These can be extracted as lemmas that depend only on `g` and `hgcont_diff`:

```lean
lemma hasFDerivAt_interpolation {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {f g : E → E} (hgcont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g)
    (t : ℝ) (x : E) :
    HasFDerivAt (fun x => x + t • g x)
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x := by
  have hid : HasFDerivAt id (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E) x := hasFDerivAt_id x
  have hg_diff : HasFDerivAt g (fderiv ℝ g x) x :=
    (hgcont_diff.differentiable (by norm_num)).differentiableAt.hasFDerivAt
  exact HasFDerivAt.fun_add hid (hg_diff.const_smul t)

lemma fderiv_bound_of_contDiff {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E} (hgcont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g) :
    ∃ M : ℝ, 0 ≤ M ∧ ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ ≤ M := by
  have hcont : ContinuousOn (fun x => ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    (hgcont_diff.continuous_fderiv (by norm_num)).continuousOn.norm
  obtain ⟨x, _, hmax⟩ := (isCompact_closedBall (0 : E) 1).exists_isMaxOn (by simp) hcont
  exact ⟨‖fderiv ℝ g x‖, norm_nonneg _, fun y hy => hmax hy⟩

lemma smul_fderiv_bound_of_contDiff {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E} (hgcont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g) :
    ∃ t0 : ℝ, 0 < t0 ∧ ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, ‖t • fderiv ℝ g x‖ < 1 := by
  obtain ⟨M, hM0, hM⟩ := fderiv_bound_of_contDiff hgcont_diff
  refine ⟨1 / (M + 1), by positivity, fun t ht0 htM x hx => ?_⟩
  rw [norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
  have hMx : ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ ≤ M := hM x hx
  have hMpos : 0 < M + 1 := by linarith
  have htM : t * (M + 1) < 1 :=
    calc t * (M + 1) < (1 / (M + 1)) * (M + 1) := by
          apply mul_lt_mul_of_pos_right htM hMpos
      _ = 1 := by field_simp
  calc t * ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖
      ≤ t * M := by nlinarith
    _ < 1 := by nlinarith
```

Response:
These can be extracted as lemmas depending only on `b`, `n`, `g`, and `J`:

```lean
lemma J_diag {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E}
    (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ E)
    (J : ℝ → E → Matrix (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ)
    (hJ : ∀ t x, J t x = LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x))
    (t : ℝ) (x : E) (k : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) :
    J t x k k = 1 + t * (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)) k k := by
  rw [hJ]
  have hid_diag : (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis LinearMap.id) k k = 1 := by
    rw [LinearMap.toMatrix_id_eq_basis_toMatrix, Module.Basis.toMatrix_self b.toBasis]
    exact Matrix.one_apply_eq k
  rw [← hid_diag]
  simp only [ContinuousLinearMap.coe_id, map_add, LinearMap.toMatrix_id_eq_basis_toMatrix,
    OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis, map_smul, Matrix.add_apply, Matrix.smul_apply, smul_eq_mul]

lemma A_bound_of_contDiff {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E} (hgcont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g)
    (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ E) :
    let n := Module.finrank ℝ E
    let A : ℝ → E → Matrix (Fin n) (Fin n) ℝ :=
      fun _ x => LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)
    ∃ M : ℝ, 0 ≤ M ∧ ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      ∀ k j : Fin n, ‖A 0 x k j‖ ≤ M := by
  obtain ⟨M, hM0, hM⟩ := fderiv_bound_of_contDiff hgcont_diff
  refine ⟨M, hM0, fun x hx k j => ?_⟩
  simp only [LinearMap.toMatrix_apply, OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis,
    ContinuousLinearMap.coe_coe, OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis_repr_apply]
  have hstep1 : ‖b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)) k‖ ≤
      ‖b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))‖ := by
    change ‖(b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)) :
      PiLp 2 (fun _ : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E) => ℝ)).ofLp k‖ ≤
      ‖(b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)) :
      PiLp 2 (fun _ : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E) => ℝ))‖
    exact PiLp.norm_apply_le _ k
  calc ‖(b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))).ofLp k‖
      ≤ ‖b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))‖ := hstep1
    _ = ‖(fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)‖ := b.repr.norm_map _
    _ ≤ ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ * ‖b.toBasis j‖ := ContinuousLinearMap.le_opNorm _ _
    _ = ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ * 1 := by
        congr 1
        simp [OrthonormalBasis.norm_eq_one]
    _ ≤ M := by
        simp only [mul_one]
        exact hM x hx
```

## Lemma 1 — Sum Bound

```lean
lemma sum_offdiag_bound {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E}
    (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ E)
    (J : ℝ → E → Matrix (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ)
    (hJ : ∀ t x, J t x = LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x))
    {M : ℝ} (hM0 : 0 ≤ M)
    (hM : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      ∀ k j : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E),
      ‖(LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖ ≤ M)
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) {x : E} (hx : x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1)
    (k : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) :
    ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖ ≤
      t * Module.finrank ℝ E * M := by
  let n := Module.finrank ℝ E
  have hsum_eq : ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖ =
      ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k,
      t * ‖((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis) (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖ := by
    apply Finset.sum_congr rfl
    intro j hj
    have hjk : j ≠ k := (Finset.mem_erase.mp hj).1
    rw [J_offdiag b J hJ t x k j hjk, norm_mul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
  have hentry_bound : ∀ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k,
      t * ‖((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis) (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖ ≤ t * M :=
    fun j _ => mul_le_mul_of_nonneg_left (hM x hx k j) ht0
  rw [hsum_eq]
  calc ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k,
        t * ‖((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis) (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖
      ≤ ∑ _ ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, t * M :=
          Finset.sum_le_sum hentry_bound
    _ = (Finset.univ.erase k).card • (t * M) := by rw [Finset.sum_const]
    _ ≤ t * n * M := by
        have hn : (↑(n - 1) : ℝ) ≤ ↑n := by exact_mod_cast Nat.sub_le n 1
        have htM : 0 ≤ t * M := mul_nonneg ht0 hM0
        simp only [Finset.mem_univ, Finset.card_erase_of_mem, Finset.card_univ,
          Fintype.card_fin, nsmul_eq_mul]
        nlinarith
```

## Lemma 2 — Diagonal Bound

```lean
lemma diag_bound_of_lt {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E}
    (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ E)
    {M : ℝ} (hM0 : 0 ≤ M)
    (hM : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      ∀ k j : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E),
      ‖(LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖ ≤ M)
    {t0 : ℝ} (ht0_def : t0 = 1 / ((Module.finrank ℝ E + 1) * (M + 1)))
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) (htC : t < t0)
    {x : E} (hx : x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1)
    (k : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) :
    let A := fun (_ : ℝ) (x : E) =>
      LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)
    t * Module.finrank ℝ E * M < ‖1 + t * A 0 x k k‖ := by
  intro A
  have h1 : 1 - t * M ≤ ‖1 + t * A 0 x k k‖ := by
    have hrev : ‖(1 : ℝ)‖ - ‖t * A 0 x k k‖ ≤ ‖1 + t * A 0 x k k‖ :=
      @norm_sub_le_norm_add ℝ _ (1 : ℝ) (t * A 0 x k k)
    have hentry : ‖t * A 0 x k k‖ ≤ t * M := by
      rw [norm_mul, Real.norm_of_nonneg ht0]
      exact mul_le_mul_of_nonneg_left (hM x hx k k) ht0
    linarith [norm_one]
  have ht_bound : t * Module.finrank ℝ E * M < 1 - t * M := by
    have hpos : 0 < (↑(Module.finrank ℝ E) + 1) * (M + 1) := by positivity
    have : t * ((↑(Module.finrank ℝ E) + 1) * (M + 1)) < 1 := by
      calc t * ((↑(Module.finrank ℝ E) + 1) * (M + 1))
          < t0 * ((↑(Module.finrank ℝ E) + 1) * (M + 1)) := by
              apply mul_lt_mul_of_pos_right htC; positivity
        _ = 1 := by rw [ht0_def]; field_simp
    nlinarith
  linarith
```

## Lemma 3 — Diagonal Dominance

```lean
lemma diag_dom_of_lt {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E}
    (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ E)
    (J : ℝ → E → Matrix (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ)
    (hJ : ∀ t x, J t x = LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x))
    {M : ℝ} (hM0 : 0 ≤ M)
    (hM : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      ∀ k j : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E),
      ‖(LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖ ≤ M)
    {t0 : ℝ} (ht0_def : t0 = 1 / ((Module.finrank ℝ E + 1) * (M + 1)))
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) (htC : t < t0)
    {x : E} (hx : x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1)
    (k : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) :
    ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖ < ‖J t x k k‖ := by
  have hsum := sum_offdiag_bound b J hJ hM0 hM ht0 hx k
  have hdiag_bd := diag_bound_of_lt b hM0 hM ht0_def ht0 htC hx k
  rw [J_diag b J hJ t x k]
  linarith
```

```lean
lemma isUnit_of_diag_dom {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E}

      ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, ∀ k : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E),
      ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖ < ‖J t x k k‖)

    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E}
    (hnonsingular : IsUnit (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + fderiv ℝ g · ))

  rw [← hu, LinearMap.range_eq_top]
```

```lean

  (min_le_left _ _).trans (min_le_left _ _)

  (min_le_left _ _).trans (min_le_right _ _)

  (min_le_right _ _).trans (min_le_left _ _)
have ht0_lt_one : t0 ≤ 1 :=
  (min_le_right _ _).trans (min_le_right _ _)
```

## Fix `isUnit_of_diag_dom` Signature

Change the lemma to take `hdiag_dom` as a hypothesis about the specific `t` rather than requiring `t < 1`:

```lean
lemma isUnit_of_diag_dom {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E}
    (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ E)
    (J : ℝ → E → Matrix (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ)
    (hJ : ∀ t x, J t x = LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x))
    {t : ℝ} {x : E} (hx : x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1)
    (hdom : ∀ k : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E),
      ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖ < ‖J t x k k‖) :
    IsUnit (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) := by
  have hmat_unit : IsUnit (J t x) := by
    rw [Matrix.isUnit_iff_isUnit_det]
    simp only [isUnit_iff_ne_zero, ne_eq]
    exact det_ne_zero_of_sum_row_lt_diag hdom
  have hJeq : LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis
      (↑(ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) = J t x := by
    simp [hJ]
  have hcoe : IsUnit (↑(ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) := by
    rwa [← LinearMap.isUnit_toMatrix_iff b.toBasis, hJeq]
  simp only [ContinuousLinearMap.coe_add, ContinuousLinearMap.coe_id,
    ContinuousLinearMap.coe_smul] at hcoe
  exact ContinuousLinearMap.isUnit_iff_isUnit_toLinearMap.mpr hcoe
```

```lean
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,

  fun t ht0 htC x hx =>
    isUnit_of_diag_dom b J (fun t x => rfl) hx
      (hdiag_dom t ht0 htC x hx)
```

```lean
lemma isOpen_image_interior {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] [CompleteSpace E] {f_t : ℝ → E → E} {g : E → E}
    (hft_strict_fderiv : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < 1 →
      ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      HasStrictFDerivAt (f_t t)
        (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x)
    (hft_surj : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < 1 →
      ∀ x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).range = ⊤)
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) (htC : t < 1) :
    IsOpen (f_t t '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) := by
  apply isOpen_iff_mem_nhds.mpr
  intro y ⟨x, hx, hxy⟩
  have hstrict := hft_strict_fderiv t ht0 htC x (interior_subset hx)
  have hmap := hstrict.map_nhds_eq_of_surj (hft_surj t ht0 htC x hx)
  rw [← hxy, ← hmap]
  exact Filter.image_mem_map (interior_mem_nhds.mpr (mem_interior_iff_mem_nhds.mp hx))

lemma image_interior_subset {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {f : E → E}
    (hfx : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ closedBall 0 1)
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) (ht1 : t ≤ 1) :
    (fun x => x + t • (f x - x)) '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) ⊆
    closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by
  intro y ⟨x, hx, hxy⟩
  rw [← hxy]
  exact mapsTo_interpolation hfx ht0 ht1 (interior_subset hx)

lemma image_interior_ne_closedBall {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] [Nontrivial E]
    {S : Set E} (hS_open : IsOpen S) (hS_sub : S ⊆ closedBall (0 : E) 1) :
    S ≠ closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by
  intro heq
  rw [heq, ← interior_eq_iff_isOpen, interior_closedBall'] at hS_open
  have hne : ball (0 : E) 1 ≠ closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by
    intro heq
    obtain ⟨x, hx⟩ := exists_norm_eq E (zero_le_one' ℝ)
    have hmem : x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1 := by simp [mem_closedBall, hx]
    have hnotmem : x ∉ ball (0 : E) 1 := by simp [mem_ball, hx]
    rw [← heq] at hmem
    exact hnotmem hmem
  exact hne hS_open

lemma exists_not_mem_image_interior {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] [Nontrivial E] {f : E → E}
    (hfx : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ closedBall 0 1)
    (hS_open : IsOpen ((fun x => x + 1 • (f x - x)) '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)))
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) (htC : t < 1) (ht1 : t ≤ 1) :
    ∃ e ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    e ∉ (fun x => x + t • (f x - x)) '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  have hne := image_interior_ne_closedBall hS_open
      (image_interior_subset hfx (by linarith) ht1)
  by_contra! h
  exact hne (le_antisymm (image_interior_subset hfx ht0 ht1) (fun x hx => h x hx))
```

## Fix `exists_not_mem_image_interior`

The problem is that `hS_open` is stated for `1 •` but we want it for general `t •`. Remove the `hS_open` argument and compute it inside:

```lean
lemma exists_not_mem_image_interior {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] [Nontrivial E] {f : E → E}
    (hfx : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ closedBall 0 1)
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) (ht1 : t ≤ 1)
    (hS_open : IsOpen ((fun x => x + t • (f x - x)) '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1))) :
    ∃ e ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    e ∉ (fun x => x + t • (f x - x)) '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  have hne := image_interior_ne_closedBall hS_open
      (image_interior_subset hfx ht0 ht1)
  by_contra! h
  exact hne (le_antisymm (image_interior_subset hfx ht0 ht1) (fun x hx => h x hx))
```

## Fix — Change `isOpen_image_interior` to Take `t < t0` Indirectly

The simplest fix is to not pass the surjectivity and strict fderiv with the `t < 1` bound, but instead pass them already specialized:

```lean
have hGt_open : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → IsOpen (G_t t) := by
  intro t ht0 htC
  apply isOpen_image_interior
  · intro t' ht0' htC' x hx
    exact hft_strict_fderiv t' ht0' htC' x hx
  · intro t' ht0' htC' x hx
    exact hft_surj t' ht0' htC' x hx
  · exact ht0
  · exact htC.trans_le ht0_lt_one
```

## Or Change `isOpen_image_interior` Signature

Change the lemma to take `t0` as a parameter and use `t < t0` throughout:

```lean
lemma isOpen_image_interior {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] [CompleteSpace E] {f_t : ℝ → E → E} {g : E → E}
    {t0 : ℝ}
    (hft_strict_fderiv : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
      ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      HasStrictFDerivAt (f_t t)
        (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x)
    (hft_surj : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 →
      ∀ x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).range = ⊤)
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) (htC : t < t0) :
    IsOpen (f_t t '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) := by
  apply isOpen_iff_mem_nhds.mpr
  intro y ⟨x, hx, hxy⟩
  have hstrict := hft_strict_fderiv t ht0 htC x (interior_subset hx)
  have hmap := hstrict.map_nhds_eq_of_surj (hft_surj t ht0 htC x hx)
  rw [← hxy, ← hmap]
  exact Filter.image_mem_map (interior_mem_nhds.mpr (mem_interior_iff_mem_nhds.mp hx))
```

## Wait — The Issue is Different

`isOpen_image_interior` passes `htC' : t' < 1` to `hft_strict_fderiv` which expects `t' < t0`. We cannot derive `t' < t0` from `t' < 1` in general.

The fix is to change `isOpen_image_interior` to not quantify over `t'` internally, but instead take the specific `t`:

```lean
lemma isOpen_image_interior {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] [CompleteSpace E] {f_t : ℝ → E → E} {g : E → E}
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t)
    (hft_strict : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      HasStrictFDerivAt (f_t t)
        (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x)
    (hft_surj : ∀ x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).range = ⊤) :
    IsOpen (f_t t '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) := by
  apply isOpen_iff_mem_nhds.mpr
  intro y ⟨x, hx, hxy⟩
  have hstrict := hft_strict x (interior_subset hx)
  have hmap := hstrict.map_nhds_eq_of_surj (hft_surj x hx)
  rw [← hxy, ← hmap]
  exact Filter.image_mem_map (interior_mem_nhds.mpr (mem_interior_iff_mem_nhds.mp hx))
```

## Lemma 1 — Supremum of Segment is in Closure of Image

```lean
lemma sSup_segment_mem_closure_image {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {f_t : ℝ → E → E} {t : ℝ}
    {p e : E} {G : Set E}
    (hG_open : IsOpen G) (hG_sub : G ⊆ f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1)
    (hp : p ∈ G) (he_not : e ∉ G)
    (hft_closed : IsClosed (f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1)) :
    let S : Set ℝ := {s ∈ Set.Icc 0 1 | AffineMap.lineMap p e s ∈ G}
    let b := sSup S
    AffineMap.lineMap p e b ∉ G ∧
    AffineMap.lineMap p e b ∈ closure G ∧
    ∃ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f_t t x = AffineMap.lineMap p e b := by
  intro S b
  have hseg_cont : Continuous (AffineMap.lineMap p e : ℝ → E) :=
    AffineMap.lineMap_continuous
  have hseg0 : AffineMap.lineMap p e (0 : ℝ) = p := AffineMap.lineMap_apply_zero _ _
  have hseg1 : AffineMap.lineMap p e (1 : ℝ) = e := AffineMap.lineMap_apply_one _ _
  have hS_nonempty : S.Nonempty := ⟨0, by simp [Set.mem_Icc], hseg0 ▸ hp⟩
  have hS_bddAbove : BddAbove S := ⟨1, fun s hs => hs.1.2⟩
  have hb_mem_Icc : b ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) 1 := by
    constructor
    · exact le_csSup_of_le hS_bddAbove
        ⟨by simp [Set.mem_Icc], hseg0 ▸ hp⟩ (by norm_num)
    · exact csSup_le hS_nonempty (fun c hc => hc.1.2)
  have hb_not_Gt : AffineMap.lineMap p e b ∉ G := by
    intro hb_in
    obtain ⟨ε, hε, hball⟩ := Metric.isOpen_iff.mp hG_open _ hb_in
    have hb_lt_one : b < 1 := by
      rcases eq_or_lt_of_le hb_mem_Icc.2 with hb1 | hb1
      · exfalso; rw [hb1, hseg1] at hb_in; exact he_not hb_in
      · exact hb1
    let ε' := min ε (1 - b) / 3
    have hε'_pos : 0 < ε' := by
      apply div_pos _ (by linarith)
      exact lt_min hε (by linarith)
    have hs'_le : b + ε' ≤ 1 := by unfold_let ε'; linarith [min_le_right ε (1 - b)]
    have hs'_close : dist (AffineMap.lineMap p e (b + ε'))
        (AffineMap.lineMap p e b) < ε := by
      rw [AffineMap.lineMap_apply, AffineMap.lineMap_apply, dist_eq_norm]
      simp only [vadd_eq_add, vsub_eq_sub]
      ring_nf
      have hsimp : (b + ε') • (e - p) + p - (b • (e - p) + p) = ε' • (e - p) := by
        simp [add_smul]; abel
      rw [hsimp, norm_smul, Real.norm_of_nonneg hε'_pos.le]
      have hpe : ‖e - p‖ ≤ 2 := by
        have hp_norm := mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp (hG_sub hp |>.choose_spec.1)
        sorry -- need bound on ‖p‖ and ‖e‖
      calc ε' * ‖e - p‖
          ≤ ε' * 2 := by nlinarith
        _ ≤ (min ε (1 - b) / 3) * 2 := by unfold_let ε'; linarith
        _ < ε := by linarith [min_le_left ε (1 - b)]
    linarith [le_csSup hS_bddAbove
      (show b + ε' ∈ S from ⟨⟨by linarith [hb_mem_Icc.1], hs'_le⟩, hball hs'_close⟩)]
  have hb_closure : AffineMap.lineMap p e b ∈ closure G := by
    apply ContinuousWithinAt.mem_closure (s := S)
    · exact hseg_cont.continuousWithinAt
    · exact csSup_mem_closure hS_nonempty hS_bddAbove
    · exact fun s hs => hs.2
  have hb_in_image : ∃ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      f_t t x = AffineMap.lineMap p e b :=
    hft_closed.closure_subset (closure_mono hG_sub hb_closure)
  exact ⟨hb_not_Gt, hb_closure, hb_in_image⟩
```

## Lemma 2 — Preimage of Boundary Point is on Sphere

```lean
lemma preimage_boundary_of_not_interior {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E]
    [InnerProductSpace ℝ E] [FiniteDimensional ℝ E]
    {f_t : ℝ → E → E} {t : ℝ} {y : E}
    (hf_fixed : ∀ x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1, f_t t x = x)
    {x : E} (hx : x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1)
    (hfx : f_t t x = y)
    (hx_not_int : x ∉ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) :
    ‖x‖ = 1 ∧ f_t t x = x := by
  rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne'] at hx_not_int
  simp only [mem_ball, dist_zero_right, not_lt] at hx_not_int
  have hx_norm : ‖x‖ = 1 :=
    le_antisymm (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp hx) hx_not_int
  have hx_sphere : x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1 := mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mpr hx_norm
  exact ⟨hx_norm, hf_fixed x hx_sphere⟩
```

---

## Lemma 3 — Main Boundary Lemma

```lean
lemma norm_eq_one_of_not_mem_image {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E]
    [InnerProductSpace ℝ E] [FiniteDimensional ℝ E]
    {f : E → E} {f_t : ℝ → E → E} {g : E → E} {t : ℝ}
    (hf_fixed : ∀ x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1, f_t t x = x)
    {G : Set E}
    (hG_open : IsOpen G)
    (hG_sub : G ⊆ f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1)
    (hG_sub_ball : G ⊆ closedBall (0 : E) 1)
    (hft_closed : IsClosed (f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1))
    (hG_nonempty : G.Nonempty)
    {e : E} (he_ball : e ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1) (he_not : e ∉ G) :
    ‖e‖ = 1 := by
  obtain ⟨p, hp⟩ := hG_nonempty
  obtain ⟨hb_not, hb_closure, hb_in_image⟩ :=
    sSup_segment_mem_closure_image hG_open hG_sub hp he_not hft_closed
  obtain ⟨x, hx_ball, hfx⟩ := hb_in_image
  have hx_not_int : x ∉ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    intro hx_int
    exact hb_not ⟨x, hx_int, hfx⟩
  obtain ⟨hx_norm, hx_fix⟩ := preimage_boundary_of_not_interior hf_fixed hx_ball hfx hx_not_int
  by_contra he_not_sphere
  have he_lt : ‖e‖ < 1 :=
    lt_of_le_of_ne (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp he_ball) he_not_sphere
  have he_interior : e ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne']
    exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mpr he_lt
  have hp_interior : p ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    interior_mono hG_sub_ball (hG_open.interior_eq ▸ hp)
  have hb_interior : AffineMap.lineMap p e (sSup _) ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    (convex_closedBall 0 1).interior.lineMap_mem hp_interior he_interior
      (by sorry) -- hb_mem_Icc
  have hb_norm : ‖AffineMap.lineMap p e (sSup _)‖ < 1 := by
    rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne'] at hb_interior
    exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mp hb_interior
  rw [← hfx, hx_fix] at hb_norm
  linarith
```

---

## Then in the Main Theorem


The sorry needs to show `‖e - p‖ ≤ 2`. We know both `e` and `p` are in `closedBall 0 1`, so `‖e‖ ≤ 1` and `‖p‖ ≤ 1`, giving `‖e - p‖ ≤ ‖e‖ + ‖p‖ ≤ 2`:

```lean

  have he_norm : ‖e‖ ≤ 1 := mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp he_ball
  have hp_norm : ‖p‖ ≤ 1 := by
    have := hG_sub hp
    obtain ⟨x, hx, hfx⟩ := this
    exact mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp hx
  calc ‖e - p‖ ≤ ‖e‖ + ‖p‖ := norm_sub_le e p
    _ ≤ 1 + 1 := add_le_add he_norm hp_norm
    _ = 2 := by norm_num
```


```lean

  linarith [norm_sub_le e p]
```

## Fix — Update `norm_eq_one_of_not_mem_image`

The lemma needs `hG_sub_ball` as a hypothesis and `hb_mem_Icc` needs to come from the `obtain`:

```lean
lemma norm_eq_one_of_not_mem_image {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E]
    [InnerProductSpace ℝ E] [FiniteDimensional ℝ E]
    {f_t : ℝ → E → E} {t : ℝ}
    (hf_fixed : ∀ x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1, f_t t x = x)
    {G : Set E}
    (hG_open : IsOpen G)
    (hG_sub : G ⊆ f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1)
    (hG_sub_ball : G ⊆ closedBall (0 : E) 1)
    (hft_closed : IsClosed (f_t t '' closedBall (0 : E) 1))
    (hG_nonempty : G.Nonempty)
    {e : E} (he_ball : e ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1) (he_not : e ∉ G) :
    ‖e‖ = 1 := by
  obtain ⟨p, hp⟩ := hG_nonempty
  obtain ⟨hb_not, hb_closure, hb_in_image, hb_mem_Icc⟩ :=
    sSup_segment_mem_closure_image hG_open hG_sub hG_sub_ball hp he_not he_ball hft_closed
  obtain ⟨x, hx_ball, hfx⟩ := hb_in_image
  have hx_not_int : x ∉ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    intro hx_int
    exact hb_not ⟨x, hx_int, hfx⟩
  obtain ⟨hx_norm, hx_fix⟩ := preimage_boundary_of_not_interior hf_fixed hx_ball hfx hx_not_int
  by_contra he_not_sphere
  have he_lt : ‖e‖ < 1 :=
    lt_of_le_of_ne (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp he_ball) he_not_sphere
  have he_interior : e ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne']
    exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mpr he_lt
  have hp_interior : p ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    interior_mono hG_sub_ball (hG_open.interior_eq ▸ hp)
  have hb_interior : AffineMap.lineMap p e (sSup _) ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
    (convex_closedBall 0 1).interior.lineMap_mem hp_interior he_interior hb_mem_Icc
  have hb_norm : ‖AffineMap.lineMap p e (sSup _)‖ < 1 := by
    rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne'] at hb_interior
    exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mp hb_interior
  rw [← hfx, hx_fix] at hb_norm
  linarith
```

```lean
lemma Gt_eq_interior {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] [Nontrivial E] {f_t : ℝ → E → E} {t : ℝ}
    {G : Set E}
    (hG_open : IsOpen G)
    (hG_sub : G ⊆ closedBall (0 : E) 1)
    (hboundary : ∀ e ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, e ∉ G → ‖e‖ = 1) :
    G = interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  apply Set.eq_of_subset_of_subset
  · intro y hy
    apply interior_mono hG_sub
    rw [hG_open.interior_eq]
    exact hy
  · intro y hy
    by_contra hy_not_Gt
    have hy_ball : y ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1 := interior_subset hy
    have hy_norm_lt : ‖y‖ < 1 := by
      rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne'] at hy
      exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mp hy
    have hy_norm_eq : ‖y‖ = 1 := hboundary y hy_ball hy_not_Gt
    linarith

lemma bijOn_of_Gt_eq_interior {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {f : E → E} {f_t : ℝ → E → E} {g : E → E} {C : NNReal}
    (hfx : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ closedBall 0 1)
    (hf_fixed : ∀ x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1, f_t 1 x = x)
    (hC : LipschitzOnWith C g (closedBall (0 : E) 1))
    (hGt_eq : f_t 1 '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) = interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1))
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) (ht1 : t ≤ 1) (ht1c : t < 1 / C) :
    Set.BijOn (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  refine ⟨mapsTo_interpolation hfx ht0 ht1, injOn_of_lipschitz_lt_one hC ht0 ht1c, ?_⟩
  intro y hy
  rcases eq_or_lt_of_le (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp hy) with hy1 | hy1
  · refine ⟨y, hy, ?_⟩
    simp only [f_t, g]
    rw [hf_fixed y (mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mpr hy1)]
    simp
  · have hy_interior : y ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
      rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne']
      exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mpr hy1
    rw [← hGt_eq] at hy_interior
```

Response:
The issue is that `f_t t` needs to be definitionally equal to `fun x => x + t • (f x - x)` and `fun x => x + t • g x`. Add a hypothesis that connects `f_t t` to its definition:

```lean
lemma bijOn_of_Gt_eq_interior {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {f : E → E} {f_t : ℝ → E → E} {g : E → E} {C : NNReal}
    (hft_def : ∀ t x, f_t t x = x + t • g x)
    (hg_def : ∀ x, g x = f x - x)
    (hfx : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ closedBall 0 1)
    (hf_fixed : ∀ x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1, f_t t x = x)
    (hC : LipschitzOnWith C g (closedBall (0 : E) 1))
    (hGt_eq : f_t t '' interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) = interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1))
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) (ht1 : t ≤ 1) (ht1c : t < 1 / C) :
    Set.BijOn (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
  have hmaps : Set.MapsTo (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    intro x hx
    rw [hft_def]
    rw [show g x = f x - x from hg_def x]
    exact mapsTo_interpolation hfx ht0 ht1 hx
  have hinj : Set.InjOn (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
    intro x hx y hy hxy
    simp only [hft_def] at hxy
    exact injOn_of_lipschitz_lt_one hC ht0 ht1c hx hy hxy
  refine ⟨hmaps, hinj, ?_⟩
  intro y hy
  rcases eq_or_lt_of_le (mem_closedBall_zero_iff.mp hy) with hy1 | hy1
  · exact ⟨y, hy, hf_fixed y (mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mpr hy1)⟩
  · have hy_interior : y ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1) := by
      rw [interior_closedBall (0 : E) one_pos.ne']
      exact mem_ball_zero_iff.mpr hy1
    rw [← hGt_eq] at hy_interior
    obtain ⟨x, hx_int, hfx⟩ := hy_interior
    exact ⟨x, interior_subset hx_int, hfx⟩
```

```lean
    Set.BijOn (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) :=
  fun t ht0 htC ht1 ht1c =>
    bijOn_of_Gt_eq_interior
      (fun t x => rfl)  -- hft_def
      (fun x => rfl)    -- hg_def
      hfx
      (fun x hx => by simp [f_t, g, hf_fixed x hx])
      hC
      (hGt_eq_interior t ht0 htC ht1)
      ht0 ht1.le ht1c
```

why should it be that the determinant is strictly positive

Response:
The determinant is strictly positive because:

1. At `t = 0`, `f_t 0 = id` so `fderiv ℝ (f_t 0) x = id` and `det(id) = 1 > 0`
2. The determinant varies **continuously** in `t`
3. The determinant is **never zero** for `t ∈ [0, t0)` since `f_t t` is a local homeomorphism (nonsingular Jacobian)
4. By the **intermediate value theorem**, since `det > 0` at `t = 0` and `det ≠ 0` throughout `[0, t]`, it must remain `> 0`

---

## The Proof

```lean
have hdet_pos : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    0 < (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det := by
  intro x hx
  -- det is continuous in s on [0, t]
  have hdet_cont : ContinuousOn
      (fun s => (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det)
      (Set.Icc 0 t) := by
    apply ContinuousOn.det
    fun_prop
  -- det is never zero on [0, t]
  have hdet_ne_zero : ∀ s ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) t,
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det ≠ 0 := by
    intro s ⟨hs0, hst⟩
    have hunit := hft_nonsingular s hs0 (hst.trans_lt htC) x hx
    intro h
    apply hunit.ne_zero
    ext v
    have := congr_arg (· v) (ContinuousLinearMap.det_eq_zero_iff.mp h)
    simp at this
    exact this
  -- det at s = 0 is 1 > 0
  have hdet_zero : (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + (0 : ℝ) • fderiv ℝ g x).det = 1 := by
    simp
  -- By IVT, det > 0 throughout
  by_contra hle
  push_neg at hle
  have hlt : (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det < 0 :=
    lt_of_le_of_ne hle (hdet_ne_zero t ⟨ht0, le_refl t⟩)
  have hpos : (0 : ℝ) < (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + (0 : ℝ) • fderiv ℝ g x).det := by
    rw [hdet_zero]; norm_num
  obtain ⟨s, hs_mem, hs_zero⟩ :=
    intermediate_value_Icc ht0 hdet_cont
      (Set.mem_Icc.mpr ⟨le_refl 0, ht0⟩)
      (Set.mem_Icc.mpr ⟨ht0, le_refl t⟩)
      (Set.mem_Icc.mpr ⟨le_of_lt hlt, le_of_lt hpos⟩)
  exact hdet_ne_zero s hs_mem hs_zero
```

```lean
    (fun s => (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det)
    (Set.Icc 0 t) := by

```

## Or More Directly with `fun_prop`

```lean
have hdet_cont : ContinuousOn
    (fun s => (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det)
    (Set.Icc 0 t) := by
  apply Continuous.continuousOn
  apply ContinuousLinearMap.continuous_det.comp
  fun_prop
```

---

## Why This Works

- `fun s => ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x` is continuous in `s` since it is affine in `s`
- `ContinuousLinearMap.continuous_det` says `fun f => f.det` is continuous on `E →L[ℝ] E`
- Composing gives continuity of `fun s => (id + s • Dg(x)).det`

ContinuousLinearMap.det_eq_zero_iff.mp doesn't exist, but one of the above should be appropriate?

Response:
The goal after `apply hunit.ne_zero` would be to show the map itself is zero, which follows from `det = 0` implying the kernel is nontrivial. But actually the simpler approach is to use `hft_nonsingular` which gives `IsUnit`, and `IsUnit` directly implies `det ≠ 0`:

```lean
have hdet_ne_zero : ∀ s ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) t,
    (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det ≠ 0 := by
  intro s ⟨hs0, hst⟩
  have hunit := hft_nonsingular s hs0 (hst.trans_lt htC) x hx
  -- IsUnit implies det ≠ 0
  rwa [Ne, ← ContinuousLinearMap.isUnit_iff_ne_zero_det] at hunit
```

```lean
have hdet_ne_zero : ∀ s ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) t,
    (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det ≠ 0 := by
  intro s ⟨hs0, hst⟩
  have hunit := hft_nonsingular s hs0 (hst.trans_lt htC) x hx
  obtain ⟨u, hu⟩ := hunit
  intro h
  have : (u : E →L[ℝ] E).det = 0 := hu ▸ h
  have hdet_unit : IsUnit ((u : E →L[ℝ] E).det) := by
    exact u.isUnit.map (ContinuousLinearMap.detMonoidHom)
  rw [this] at hdet_unit
  exact not_isUnit_zero hdet_unit
```

## Why This Works

`LinearMap.det_toMatrix b.toBasis f` gives:

$$\det(\text{toMatrix}(b, b, f)) = \text{LinearMap.det}(f)$$

So rewriting with it changes the goal from:

```
((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis) ↑(...)).det = 0
```

to:

```
LinearMap.det (↑(ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x)) = 0
```

And `h : (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det = 0` is exactly `LinearMap.det` of the coercion (since `ContinuousLinearMap.det` is defined as `LinearMap.det` of the underlying linear map), so `exact_mod_cast h` closes it.

theorem intermediate_value_Icc {α : Type u} [TopologicalSpace α] [ConditionallyCompleteLinearOrder α] [OrderTopology α] [DenselyOrdered α] {δ : Type u_1} [LinearOrder δ] [TopologicalSpace δ] [OrderClosedTopology δ] {a b : α} (hab : a ≤ b) {f : α → δ} (hf : ContinuousOn f (Set.Icc a b)) :

Response:
So `intermediate_value_Icc` gives `Set.Icc (f a) (f b) ⊆ f '' Set.Icc a b`. We need `0` to be in `Set.Icc (det at 0) (det at t)`, but since `det at 0 > 0` and `det at t < 0`, we need `intermediate_value_Icc'` which handles the case `f b ≤ t ≤ f a`:

```lean
exfalso
have hmem : (0 : ℝ) ∈ 
    (fun s => (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det) '' 
    Set.Icc 0 t := by
  apply intermediate_value_Icc' ht0 hdet_cont
  exact Set.mem_Icc.mpr ⟨le_of_lt hlt, le_of_lt hpos_at_zero⟩
obtain ⟨s, hs_mem, hs_zero⟩ := hmem
exact hdet_ne_zero s hs_mem hs_zero
```

---

## Why `intermediate_value_Icc'`

Since `det(0) > 0` and `det(t) < 0`:

$$\text{det}(t) < 0 \leq \text{det}(0)$$

So `0 ∈ Set.Icc (det(t)) (det(0))` which is what `intermediate_value_Icc'` gives:

```lean
#check @intermediate_value_Icc'
-- Set.Icc (f b) (f a) ⊆ f '' Set.Icc a b
-- when hab : a ≤ b and hf : ContinuousOn f (Icc a b)
```

```lean

    LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (fun y => y + t • (f y - y)) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) =
```

```lean
    simp [ContinuousLinearMap.det]
  · -- x not in ball, but we still need the equality
    -- both sides are equal since fderiv agrees with hderiv_eq2 everywhere
    rw [show fderiv ℝ (fun y => y + t • (f y - y)) x =
        ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x from by
      have := hasFDerivAt_interpolation hgcont_diff t x
      exact this.fderiv]
    rw [abs_of_pos (by
      -- det is positive everywhere, not just on the ball
      -- use continuity argument or direct computation
      sorry)]
    simp [ContinuousLinearMap.det]
```

## Simpler — Prove for All `x` Directly

Since `hasFDerivAt_interpolation` holds for all `x : E` (not just those in the ball), and `hdet_pos` needs to be extended to all `x`:

```lean

    fderiv ℝ (fun y => y + t • (f y - y)) x =
    ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x :=
  fun x => (hasFDerivAt_interpolation hgcont_diff t x).fderiv

    LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (fun y => y + t • (f y - y)) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) =
    ∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    |(ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det| := by

  · exact hdet_pos x (by
      -- need x ∈ closedBall 0 1 for hdet_pos
      -- but hdet_pos only holds on the ball
      -- use measure theory: a.e. x is in the ball under restrict
      sorry)
```

## `hI_cont` — Continuity of `I`

`I t = ∫ x in closedBall 0 1, det(fderiv (f_t t) x)` is continuous in `t` by continuity of the integrand:

```lean
have hI_cont : Continuous I := by
  simp only [I]
  apply MeasureTheory.continuous_integral_of_dominated

    sorry

    fun_prop
```

## `hI_const_all` — Constancy of `I`

Since `I` is continuous and constant on `[0, t0)`, it is constant everywhere by the identity theorem for continuous functions:

```lean
have hI_const_all : ∀ t : ℝ, I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  have hconst_on : ∀ t ∈ Set.Ico (0 : ℝ) t0, I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
    intro t ⟨ht0, htC⟩
    exact hI_const t ht0 htC (htC.trans_le ht0_lt_one) (htC.trans_le ht0_lt_C)
  -- I is continuous and constant on [0, t0)
  -- so constant everywhere by density
  have hdense : Dense (Set.Ico (0 : ℝ) t0) := by
    apply dense_of_exists_between
    intro a b hab
    rcases lt_or_le a 0 with ha | ha
    · exact ⟨0, Set.left_mem_Ico.mpr ht0_pos, by linarith, by linarith⟩
    · rcases lt_or_le a t0 with hat0 | hat0
      · exact ⟨a, Set.mem_Ico.mpr ⟨ha, hat0⟩, lt_refl a, hab⟩
      · exact ⟨t0 / 2, Set.mem_Ico.mpr ⟨by linarith, half_lt_self ht0_pos⟩,
          by linarith, by linarith⟩
  sorry
```

---

## Better Approach for `hI_const_all`

Since `I` is continuous and equals a constant on `[0, t0)` which is dense in... wait, `[0, t0)` is not dense in all of `ℝ`. The correct argument is:

`I` is **analytic** (polynomial) in `t`, and a polynomial that is constant on an interval is constant everywhere. The polynomial structure comes from the fact that `det(id + t • A)` is a polynomial in `t`:

```lean
have hI_const_all : ∀ t : ℝ, I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  -- I(t) - vol is continuous and zero on [0, t0)
  -- I(t) - vol is analytic (det is polynomial in t)
  -- A function analytic on ℝ that vanishes on an interval vanishes everywhere
  have hzero_on : ∀ t ∈ Set.Ico (0 : ℝ) t0,
      I t - (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal = 0 :=
    fun t ht => sub_eq_zero.mpr (hI_const t ht.1 ht.2
      (ht.2.trans_le ht0_lt_one) (ht.2.trans_le ht0_lt_C))
  have hcont_diff : ∀ t : ℝ,
      HasDerivAt (fun t => I t - (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal) 0 t := by
    sorry
  -- By the identity theorem, zero on [0, t0) implies zero everywhere
  intro t
  have := hzero_on 0 ⟨le_refl 0, ht0_pos⟩
  linarith [sub_eq_zero.mp (hI_cont.sub continuous_const |>.const_smul 0 |>.eq_of_forall_eq_of_dense
    (by sorry) t)]
```

---

## Most Practical Approach

Given the complexity, the cleanest route is:

```lean
have hI_const_all : ∀ t : ℝ, I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  intro t
  -- Case split: if t < t0 use hI_const directly
  rcases lt_or_le t t0 with ht | ht
  · rcases lt_or_le t 0 with ht0 | ht0
    · -- t < 0: use continuity and value at 0
      have h0 := hI_const 0 le_rfl ht0_pos
        (ht0_pos.trans_le ht0_lt_one) (ht0_pos.trans_le ht0_lt_C)
      -- I is constant on [0, t0) so I(0) = vol
      -- need to extend to t < 0 via analyticity
      sorry
    · exact hI_const t ht0 ht (ht.trans_le ht0_lt_one) (ht.trans_le ht0_lt_C)
  · -- t ≥ t0: use analyticity to extend
    sorry
```

---

## Recommendation

The two `sorry`s in `hI_const_all` require either:
1. Showing `I` is analytic and using the identity theorem
2. Showing `I` is a polynomial explicitly

This is the hardest remaining step. The polynomial structure of `det(id + t • A)` needs to be made explicit. Would you like to pursue the analytic approach or the explicit polynomial approach?

[06/01/2026 08:38:29 +00:00] User:
do whichever is more convenient

Response:
The analytic approach is more convenient since Mathlib has `AnalyticOn.eq_of_frequently_eq` which says two analytic functions agreeing on a set with an accumulation point are equal everywhere.

---

## `hI_cont` First

```lean
have hI_cont : Continuous I := by
  simp only [I]
  apply continuous_parametric_integral_of_continuous
  · fun_prop
  · exact isCompact_closedBall 0 1
```

---

## `hI_const_all` via Analyticity

```lean
have hI_const_all : ∀ t : ℝ, I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  -- I is analytic in t
  have hI_analytic : AnalyticOn ℝ I Set.univ := by
    simp only [I]
    apply AnalyticOn.integral
    · fun_prop
    · exact isCompact_closedBall 0 1
  -- The constant function is analytic
  have hconst_analytic : AnalyticOn ℝ
      (fun _ => (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal) Set.univ :=
    analyticOn_const
  -- They agree on [0, t0) which has an accumulation point
  have hagree : ∀ t ∈ Set.Ico (0 : ℝ) t0,
      I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal :=
    fun t ⟨ht0, htC⟩ =>
      hI_const t ht0 htC (htC.trans_le ht0_lt_one) (htC.trans_le ht0_lt_C)
  -- 0 is an accumulation point of [0, t0)
  have hacc : AccPt 0 (Filter.principal (Set.Ico 0 t0)) := by
    rw [accPt_iff_nhds]
    intro U hU
    obtain ⟨ε, hε, hball⟩ := Metric.mem_nhds_iff.mp hU
    refine ⟨min (t0 / 2) (ε / 2), ?_, ?_⟩
    · simp only [Set.mem_Ico]
      exact ⟨by positivity, lt_min (half_lt_self ht0_pos) (by linarith)⟩
    · apply hball
      simp [dist_eq_norm, abs_of_pos, lt_min_iff]
      constructor
      · positivity
      · linarith
  -- By the identity theorem, they agree everywhere
  have heq : I = fun _ => (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
    apply AnalyticOn.eq_of_frequently_eq hI_analytic hconst_analytic
      (Set.mem_univ 0) (Set.mem_univ 0)
    rw [Filter.frequently_iff]
    intro U hU
    have hU' := Filter.inter_mem hU (Filter.principal_le_nhds hacc.1)
    sorry
  exact fun t => congr_fun heq t
```

---

## Simpler Alternative — Use Continuity Directly

Since `I` is continuous and constant on `[0, t0)`, and `[0, t0)` is dense in `(-∞, t0)`, we can extend. But for all of `ℝ` we need analyticity.

The most practical approach given Mathlib's API is:

```lean
have hI_const_all : ∀ t : ℝ, I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  have hagree : Set.EqOn I (fun _ => (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal)
      (Set.Ico 0 t0) :=
    fun t ⟨ht0, htC⟩ =>
      hI_const t ht0 htC (htC.trans_le ht0_lt_one) (htC.trans_le ht0_lt_C)
  have hfreq : ∃ᶠ t in nhds 0, I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
    rw [Filter.frequently_iff]
    intro U hU
    obtain ⟨ε, hε, hball⟩ := Metric.mem_nhds_iff.mp hU
    let s := min (t0 / 2) (ε / 2)
    have hs_pos : 0 < s := by positivity
    have hs_mem_U : s ∈ U := hball (by
      simp [s, dist_eq_norm, abs_of_pos hs_pos]
      exact lt_of_le_of_lt (min_le_right _ _) (by linarith))
    have hs_mem_Ico : s ∈ Set.Ico 0 t0 :=
      ⟨le_of_lt hs_pos, lt_of_le_of_lt (min_le_left _ _) (half_lt_self ht0_pos)⟩
    exact ⟨s, hs_mem_U, hagree hs_mem_Ico⟩
  -- I is analytic
  have hI_analytic : AnalyticAt ℝ I 0 := by sorry
  have hconst_analytic : AnalyticAt ℝ (fun _ => (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal) 0 :=
    analyticAt_const
  have heq_nhds : I =ᶠ[nhds 0] fun _ => (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal :=
    hI_analytic.eq_of_frequently_eq hconst_analytic hfreq
  intro t
  have hcont_sub : Continuous (fun t => I t - (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal) :=
    hI_cont.sub continuous_const
  have hzero_nhds : (fun t => I t - (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal) =ᶠ[nhds 0]
      fun _ => (0 : ℝ) := by
    filter_upwards [heq_nhds] with t ht
    simp [ht]
  have hzero_all : ∀ t, I t - (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal = 0 := by
    intro t
    have hconst : Continuous (fun t => I t - (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal) :=
      hcont_sub
    exact sub_eq_zero.mpr (hI_cont.eq_of_forall_eq_of_dense
      continuous_const (fun t => (hagree ⟨sorry, sorry⟩).symm) t)
  linarith [hzero_all t]
```

---

## Most Honest Assessment

Both approaches have `sorry`s that are hard to fill without either:
1. Explicitly constructing `I` as a polynomial
2. Using a Mathlib theorem about analytic functions on `ℝ`

The cleanest path forward is to use `Polynomial.funext` by showing `I` is literally a polynomial. Would you like to pursue that route instead?

[06/01/2026 08:43:35 +00:00] User:
let's show that I is literally a poly. as it is a determinant of polys in t, itself should be a poly in t, give a list of the important theorems to use and i will search to find if they exist in mathlib or have different names

Response:
Here are the key theorems needed, from bottom up:

---

## 1. The Integrand is Polynomial in `t`

The determinant of `id + t • A` is a polynomial in `t`:

```
Polynomial.det_one_add_smul
-- or
Matrix.det_one_add_smul
-- det(I + t • A) is a polynomial in t
```

---

## 2. Polynomial Functions are Analytic

```
Polynomial.analytic
Polynomial.analyticOn
-- a polynomial p gives an analytic function fun t => p.eval t
```

---

## 3. Integral of a Polynomial Parameter is a Polynomial

```
MeasureTheory.integral_polynomial_of_polynomial_integrand
-- if f(t, x) is polynomial in t for each x, then ∫ f(t, x) dx is polynomial in t
```

---

## 4. A Polynomial Constant on an Interval is Constant

```
Polynomial.funext
-- two polynomials equal on infinitely many points are equal
Polynomial.eq_of_infinite_isRoot
-- a nonzero polynomial has finitely many roots
```

---

## 5. Connecting Polynomial to Function

```
Polynomial.aeval_eq_sum_range
Polynomial.eval_eq_sum
-- evaluating a polynomial gives the function value
```

---

## 6. The Key Identity

```
Matrix.det_one_add_smul
-- det(1 + t • A) = ∑ k, t^k * (sum of k×k minors of A)
```

---

## Search Priority

Search for these in order:

1. `Matrix.det_one_add_smul` or `Polynomial.charmatrix`
2. `Polynomial.analyticOn` or `Polynomial.continuous`
3. `MeasureTheory.integral_comp_polynomial` or similar
4. `Polynomial.funext` — this almost certainly exists
5. `Polynomial.eq_zero_of_infinite_isRoot`

The most critical one is **4** (`Polynomial.funext`) since if we can show `I` is a polynomial and use `Polynomial.funext` to conclude two polynomials agreeing on `[0, t0)` (infinitely many points) are equal, the proof is complete.
