Response:
Here is the proof plan using the found theorems:

---

## Step 1 — Express the Integrand as a Polynomial in `t`

For each `x`, `det(id + t • fderiv g x)` is a polynomial in `t` via `Matrix.det_one_add_smul`.

---

## Step 2 — `I` is a Polynomial

```lean
-- The integrand for each x is a polynomial in t
have hintegrand_poly : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    ∃ p : Polynomial ℝ, ∀ t : ℝ,
    LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) = p.eval t := by
  intro x hx
  -- det(id + t • A) is polynomial in t
  sorry

-- I(t) = ∫ p_x(t) dx is itself a polynomial in t
have hI_poly : ∃ p : Polynomial ℝ, ∀ t : ℝ, I t = p.eval t := by
  sorry
```

---

## Step 3 — Use `Polynomial.funext`

```lean
have hI_const_all : ∀ t : ℝ, I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  obtain ⟨p, hp⟩ := hI_poly
  -- The constant polynomial C(vol)
  let q : Polynomial ℝ := Polynomial.C (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal
  -- p and q agree on [0, t0) which is infinite
  have hpq : p = q := by
    apply Polynomial.funext
    intro t
    -- For t ∈ [0, t0), p(t) = I(t) = vol = q(t)
    -- For other t, use that ℝ is infinite so we can find enough points
    -- Actually Polynomial.funext requires ALL t, so we need p = q as polynomials
    -- Use that they agree on infinitely many points
    sorry
  intro t
  rw [hp t, hpq]
  simp [q]
```

---

## Better Approach — Use `Polynomial.finite_setOf_isRoot`

```lean
have hI_const_all : ∀ t : ℝ, I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  obtain ⟨p, hp⟩ := hI_poly
  let q : Polynomial ℝ := Polynomial.C (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal
  -- p - q is zero on [0, t0) which is infinite
  -- so p - q = 0
  have hpq : p = q := by
    apply Polynomial.funext
    intro t
    simp only [q, Polynomial.eval_C]
    -- need p.eval t = vol for all t
    -- we know it for t ∈ [0, t0)
    -- use that p - q has infinitely many roots
    have hdiff_zero : ∀ t ∈ Set.Ico (0 : ℝ) t0, (p - q).eval t = 0 := by
      intro t ⟨ht0, htC⟩
      simp [hp t, hI_const t ht0 htC (htC.trans_le ht0_lt_one) (htC.trans_le ht0_lt_C), q]
    have hinf : Set.Infinite (Set.Ico (0 : ℝ) t0) :=
      Set.infinite_Ico 0 t0 ht0_pos
    have hroots_inf : Set.Infinite {t | (p - q).eval t = 0} :=
      hinf.mono (fun t ht => hdiff_zero t ht)
    by_contra hne
    have hne' : p - q ≠ 0 := by
      intro h
      apply hne
      have := congr_arg (· + q) h
      simp at this
      exact this
    exact hroots_inf (Polynomial.finite_setOf_isRoot hne')
  intro t
  rw [hp t, hpq]
  simp [q]
```

---

## The Remaining `sorry` — `hI_poly`

The key step is showing `I` is a polynomial. Using `Matrix.det_one_add_smul`:

```lean
have hI_poly : ∃ p : Polynomial ℝ, ∀ t : ℝ, I t = p.eval t := by
  simp only [I]
  -- For each x, det(id + t • Dg(x)) = p_x(t) for some polynomial p_x
  -- The integral of p_x(t) over x is itself a polynomial in t
  -- with coefficients being integrals of the matrix minor functions
  -- Use Matrix.det_one_add_smul to get the explicit polynomial
  -- det(1 + t • A) = 1 + tr(A)*t + ... + det(A)*t^n
  -- Integrating: I(t) = vol + (∫ tr(Dg(x)) dx) * t + ... 
  -- Each coefficient is a finite integral, giving a polynomial
  use ∑ k : Fin (n + 1), Polynomial.C (∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    -- k-th coefficient: integral of k-th elementary symmetric polynomial of eigenvalues of Dg(x)
    (Matrix.det_one_add_smul_coeff k (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)))) *
    Polynomial.X ^ (k : ℕ)
  sorry
```

---

## Honest Assessment

The `hI_poly` step requires connecting:
1. `Matrix.det_one_add_smul` — gives explicit polynomial formula for `det(1 + t • A)`
2. Linearity of integration — to integrate the polynomial coefficients
3. Measurability of the coefficients — to ensure the integrals exist

This is doable but requires significant work. The key theorem is:

```lean
Matrix.det_one_add_smul r M = 
  1 + trace M * r + (det (1 + X • M.map C)).divX.divX.eval r * r ^ 2
```

Which gives `I(t) = vol(B^n) + (∫ tr(Dg(x)) dx) * t + (∫ quadratic_term(x) dx) * t^2 + ...`

Each coefficient is a measurable integral, making `I` explicitly a polynomial in `t`.

Would you like to pursue the explicit polynomial construction, or use the analytic approach with `AnalyticOn.eval_polynomial` instead?

[06/01/2026 11:12:48 +00:00] User:
there doesn't seem to be a benefit to not explicitly giving I(t) as a polynomial, let's try that

Response:
The explicit polynomial for `I(t)` comes from `Matrix.det_one_add_smul`. For an `n × n` matrix `A`:

$$\det(I + tA) = 1 + \text{tr}(A)t + \left(\det(I + XA)\right).\text{divX}.\text{divX}.\text{eval}(t) \cdot t^2$$

So `I(t)` has the form:

$$I(t) = \int_{B^n} \det(I + t \cdot Dg(x)) \, dx = c_0 + c_1 t + c_2(t) t^2$$

where the coefficients are integrals over the ball.

---

## Define `I` Explicitly as a Polynomial

```lean
-- The three coefficient functions
let c0 : ℝ := (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal
let c1 : ℝ := ∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,
  (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).trace
let c2 : ℝ → ℝ := fun t => ∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,
  (Matrix.det (1 + (Polynomial.X : ℝ[X]) •
    (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map
    Polynomial.C)).divX.divX.eval t

-- The explicit polynomial
let P : Polynomial ℝ :=
  Polynomial.C c0 +
  Polynomial.C c1 * Polynomial.X +
  Polynomial.C (c2 0) * Polynomial.X ^ 2  -- this is wrong, c2 depends on t
```

---

## The Problem

`c2` depends on `t` through `.eval t`, so it is not a constant coefficient. The full polynomial is:

$$I(t) = c_0 + c_1 t + \left(\int_{B^n} p_x \, dx\right)(t) \cdot t^2$$

where `p_x = (det(I + X • A_x)).divX.divX` is itself a polynomial in `X`. So:

```lean
-- For each x, the polynomial in t
let p_x : E → Polynomial ℝ := fun x =>
  let A := LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)
  (Matrix.det (1 + (Polynomial.X : ℝ[X]) • A.map Polynomial.C)).divX.divX

-- The full polynomial
let P : Polynomial ℝ :=
  Polynomial.C c0 +
  Polynomial.C c1 * Polynomial.X +
  (∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1, (p_x x).toFun) -- this doesn't typecheck
```

---

## The Right Approach

The polynomial `P` has coefficients that are integrals:

$$P = \sum_{k=0}^{n} \left(\int_{B^n} [t^k]\det(I + t \cdot Dg(x)) \, dx\right) X^k$$

where `[t^k]` denotes the coefficient of `t^k`. Define it as:

```lean
let P : Polynomial ℝ :=
  ∑ k : Fin (n + 1), Polynomial.monomial k
    (∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      (let A := LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)
       (Matrix.det (1 + (Polynomial.X : ℝ[X]) • A.map Polynomial.C)).coeff k))
```

---

## Proving `I t = P.eval t`

```lean
have hI_poly : ∀ t : ℝ, I t = P.eval t := by
  intro t
  simp only [I, P, Polynomial.eval_finset_sum, Polynomial.eval_monomial]
  rw [← MeasureTheory.integral_finset_sum]
  · apply MeasureTheory.integral_congr_ae
    apply MeasureTheory.ae_restrict_of_forall_mem measurableSet_closedBall
    intro x hx
    -- For each x, det(id + t • Dg(x)) = P_x.eval t
    -- Use Matrix.det_one_add_smul
    have hA := LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)
    rw [show LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) =
        (1 + (Polynomial.X : ℝ[X]) • hA.map Polynomial.C).det.eval t from by
      simp [LinearMap.det_toMatrix, Matrix.det_one_add_smul]]
    rw [Polynomial.eval_finset_sum]
    congr 1
  · intro k _
    apply MeasureTheory.integrable_const
```

---

## Honest Assessment

This approach requires:

1. Connecting `LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x)` to `Matrix.det (1 + t • A_x)` ✓ (via `LinearMap.det_toMatrix`)
2. Connecting `Matrix.det (1 + t • A)` to `(det(1 + X • A)).eval t` ✓ (via `Matrix.det_one_add_smul`)
3. Swapping `∫` and `∑` ✓ (via `MeasureTheory.integral_finset_sum`)
4. Showing each coefficient integral is measurable (needs work)

The key missing piece is step 4. Would you like to proceed with this structure and fill in the measurability arguments?

[06/01/2026 11:56:54 +00:00] User:
noncomputable def matPolyEquiv {R : Type u_1} [CommSemiring R] {n : Type w} [DecidableEq n] [Fintype n] :
Matrix n n (Polynomial R) ≃ₐ[R] Polynomial (Matrix n n R)

The algebra isomorphism stating "matrices of polynomials are the same as polynomials of matrices".

(You probably shouldn't attempt to use this underlying definition --- it's an algebra equivalence, and characterised extensionally by the lemma matPolyEquiv_coeff_apply below.)

theorem matPolyEquiv_eval {R : Type u_1} [CommSemiring R] {n : Type w} [DecidableEq n] [Fintype n] (M : Matrix n n (Polynomial R)) (r : R) (i j : n) :
Polynomial.eval ((Matrix.scalar n) r) (matPolyEquiv M) i j = Polynomial.eval r (M i j)

@[simp]

```lean
  · simp [← hC]
  · calc t0 ≤ 1 / ((C : ℝ) + 1) := (min_le_left _ _).trans (min_le_right _ _)
```

```lean
  intro x
```

[06/02/2026 11:20:40 +00:00] User:
on the first goal, after

apply MeasureTheory.integral_congr_ae
        apply MeasureTheory.ae_restrict_of_forall_mem measurableSet_closedBall

the goal is

Response:
The `apply MeasureTheory.integral_congr_ae` and `apply MeasureTheory.ae_restrict_of_forall_mem` are being applied to the wrong goal. The goal is still an equality of integrals, not a pointwise equality. The `rw [← MeasureTheory.integral_finset_sum]` needs to happen first:

```lean
have hI_poly : ∀ t : ℝ, I t = P.eval t := by
  intro t
  simp only [I, P, Polynomial.eval_finset_sum, Polynomial.eval_monomial]
  conv_rhs =>
    arg 2
    ext k
    rw [← MeasureTheory.integral_mul_const]
  rw [← MeasureTheory.integral_finset_sum]
  · apply MeasureTheory.integral_congr_ae
    apply MeasureTheory.ae_restrict_of_forall_mem measurableSet_closedBall
    intro x hx
    -- Now goal should be pointwise equality
    rw [hdet_eval x hx t]
    rw [Polynomial.eval_eq_sum_range' (n := n.succ)]
    · simp [Polynomial.eval_finset_sum, Polynomial.eval_monomial]
    · sorry
  · intro k _
    apply MeasureTheory.Integrable.mul_const
    apply MeasureTheory.integrable_of_isCompact_support isCompact_closedBall
    apply Continuous.continuousOn
    fun_prop
```

---

## Why the Order Matters

The steps must be:
1. Rewrite RHS coefficients using `integral_mul_const` — moves `t^k` inside
2. Swap `∑` and `∫` using `integral_finset_sum` — now RHS is a single integral
3. Apply `integral_congr_ae` — reduces to pointwise equality
4. Prove pointwise equality using `hdet_eval`

[06/02/2026 11:27:50 +00:00] User:
the two goals after

      simp only [I, P, Polynomial.eval_finset_sum, Polynomial.eval_monomial]
      conv_rhs =>

## Recommendation

The cleanest approach is to note that `(P_x x).coeff k` is a polynomial function of the entries of `A x`, hence continuous. Extract it as a separate lemma:

```lean
lemma continuous_Px_coeff (k : ℕ) (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin n) ℝ E)
    (g : E → E) (hg : ContDiff ℝ 1 g) :
    Continuous (fun x => (Matrix.det (1 + Polynomial.X •
      (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map
      Polynomial.C)).coeff k) := by
  -- coeff k of det(1 + X • M) is a degree-k polynomial in entries of M
  -- entries of M = b.repr (fderiv g x (b j)) i are continuous in x
  have hentry_cont : ∀ i j : Fin n,
      Continuous (fun x => (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis
        (fderiv ℝ g x)) i j) := by
    intro i j
    fun_prop
  -- det.coeff k is a finite sum of products of entries
  -- hence continuous
  apply continuous_finset_sum
  intro σ _
  apply continuous_const.mul
  apply continuous_finset_prod
  intro i _
  fun_prop
```

[06/02/2026 12:18:44 +00:00] User:
as a lemma outside the environment, n is an unknown identifier

Response:
`n` is defined inside the theorem as `Module.finrank ℝ E`. The lemma needs to use `Module.finrank ℝ E` directly:

```lean
lemma continuous_Px_coeff {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] (k : ℕ)
    (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ E)
    {g : E → E} (hg : ContDiff ℝ 1 g) :
    Continuous (fun x => (Matrix.det (1 + (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) •
      (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map
      Polynomial.C)).coeff k) := by
  have hentry_cont : ∀ i j : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E),
      Continuous (fun x => (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis
        (fderiv ℝ g x)) i j) := by
    intro i j
    fun_prop
  simp only [Matrix.det_apply, Polynomial.coeff_sum, Polynomial.coeff_smul]
  apply continuous_finset_sum
  intro σ _
  apply Continuous.mul continuous_const
  apply continuous_finset_prod
  intro i _
  simp only [Matrix.add_apply, Matrix.smul_apply, Matrix.one_apply,
    Polynomial.coeff_add, Polynomial.coeff_smul, Polynomial.coeff_one,
    Polynomial.coeff_X]
  apply Continuous.add
  · apply continuous_const
  · apply Continuous.mul continuous_const
    exact hentry_cont _ _
```

## Key Change

Replace `Polynomial.coeff_sum` with `Polynomial.finset_sum_coeff` which says:

```lean
#check Polynomial.finset_sum_coeff
-- (∑ i in s, f i).coeff n = ∑ i in s, (f i).coeff n
```

This distributes `coeff k` over the `∑ σ` sum, allowing `continuous_finset_sum` to apply.

[06/02/2026 12:38:54 +00:00] User:

  map_sum

```lean

  -- Now need: Continuous fun x => (∏ i, M(σ i, i)).coeff k
  -- where M = 1 + X • A(x).map C

    sorry
```

## Better Approach — Use `Polynomial.coeff_prod` Differently

The product of polynomials' `coeff k` is not simply the product of coefficients. Instead, show the whole expression is continuous by showing it is a polynomial in the entries of `A x`:

```lean
  simp only [Matrix.det_apply, Polynomial.finset_sum_coeff]
  apply continuous_finset_sum
  intro σ _
  simp only [Polynomial.coeff_zsmul]
  apply Continuous.const_smul
  -- (∏ i, (1 + X • A(x).map C) (σ i) i).coeff k
  -- = (∏ i, (δ_{σi,i} + X * A(x)_{σi,i})).coeff k
  -- This is a sum of products of entries of A(x), hence continuous
  have : (fun x => (∏ i : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E),
      (1 + (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) •
      ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map
      Polynomial.C)) (σ i) i).coeff k) =
    (fun x => (∏ i : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E),
      ((if σ i = i then 1 else 0 : Polynomial ℝ) +
      Polynomial.X * Polynomial.C
        ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)) (σ i) i))).coeff k) := by
    congr 1; ext x
    congr 1; ext i
    simp [Matrix.add_apply, Matrix.smul_apply, Matrix.one_apply,
      Polynomial.smul_eq_C_mul, Polynomial.map_apply]
  rw [this]
  -- Now each factor is linear in A(x)_{σi,i}
  -- The product is a polynomial in these entries
  -- coeff k of this product is a polynomial in the entries, hence continuous
  apply Continuous.comp _ (continuous_finset_prod Finset.univ (fun i _ => by
    apply Continuous.add continuous_const
    apply Continuous.mul continuous_const
    exact (hentry_cont (σ i) i).comp continuous_id))
  exact Polynomial.continuous_coeff k
```

---

## If `Polynomial.continuous_coeff` Doesn't Exist

```lean
exact continuous_const.comp (Polynomial.coeff_continuous k)
```

Or prove it directly since `coeff k` is a linear map on polynomials:

```lean
exact (Polynomial.lcoeff ℝ k).continuous
```

[06/03/2026 10:14:48 +00:00] User:
after

simp only [Matrix.det_apply, Polynomial.finset_sum_coeff]
  apply continuous_finset_sum
  intro σ _
  simp only [Polynomial.coeff_smul]
  have : ∀ x, (∏ i : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E), (1 + (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) • 
    ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis) ↑(fderiv ℝ g x)).map 
    Polynomial.C) (σ i) i) = 
    ∏ i : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E), ((if σ i = i then (1 : Polynomial ℝ) else 0) + 
    Polynomial.X * Polynomial.C ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis) 
    ↑(fderiv ℝ g x) (σ i) i)) := by
    intro x
    congr 1
  simp_rw [this]

the goal is

⊢ Continuous fun a ↦
  Equiv.Perm.sign σ •
    (∏ i,
          ((if σ i = i then 1 else 0) +
            Polynomial.X * Polynomial.C ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis) (↑(fderiv ℝ g a)) (σ i) i))).coeff
      k

is this one we can expect to close?
  

Response:
Yes, this should be closeable. The key insight is that `coeff k` of a product of polynomials of the form `c + X * C(aᵢ)` is a polynomial in the `aᵢ`, hence continuous. 

The product `∏ i, (cᵢ + X * C(aᵢ))` has `coeff k` equal to a sum of products of the `aᵢ` values (the elementary symmetric polynomials), which is continuous in each `aᵢ`.

---

## Proof

```lean
apply Continuous.const_smul
-- coeff k of ∏ i, (c_i + X * C(a_i)) is continuous in the a_i
-- since it's a polynomial in the a_i
have hfactor_cont : ∀ i : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E),
    Continuous (fun x => (if σ i = i then (1 : Polynomial ℝ) else 0) +
    Polynomial.X * Polynomial.C
      ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)) (σ i) i)) := by
  intro i
  apply Continuous.add continuous_const
  apply Continuous.mul continuous_const
  exact (Polynomial.continuous_C).comp (hentry_cont (σ i) i)
-- The product is continuous as a Polynomial ℝ valued function
have hprod_cont : Continuous (fun x =>
    ∏ i : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E), ((if σ i = i then (1 : Polynomial ℝ) else 0) +
    Polynomial.X * Polynomial.C
      ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)) (σ i) i))) := by
  apply continuous_finset_prod
  intro i _
  exact hfactor_cont i
-- coeff k is continuous as a linear map
exact (Polynomial.lcoeff ℝ k).continuous.comp hprod_cont
```

[06/03/2026 10:22:21 +00:00] User:
ailed to synthesize instance of type class
  TopologicalSpace (Polynomial ℝ)

Response:
`Polynomial ℝ` does not have a canonical `TopologicalSpace` instance in Mathlib. We need to avoid working with `Polynomial ℝ` as a topological space and instead work directly with the `ℝ`-valued `coeff k` function.

---

## Fix — Work Directly with `coeff k`

Instead of showing the product is continuous as a `Polynomial ℝ`-valued function, show `coeff k` of the product is continuous directly using `Polynomial.coeff_prod` and induction:

```lean
apply Continuous.const_smul
-- Use Polynomial.coeff_prod to expand coeff k of the product
-- coeff k of ∏ (c_i + X * C(a_i)) = ∑ S ⊆ Fin n, |S|=k, ∏ i∈S a_i * ∏ i∉S c_i
-- which is a polynomial in the a_i, hence continuous
apply Continuous.comp _ (continuous_pi (fun i => 
  Continuous.add continuous_const 
    (Continuous.mul continuous_const 
      ((hentry_cont (σ i) i)))))
-- Now need: coeff k of product is continuous in the vector of factors
-- Use that it's a multilinear polynomial
exact continuous_finset_prod_coeff k
```

---

## Most Practical Fix — Use `Finset.prod_coeff` Directly

Expand `coeff k` of the product explicitly:

```lean
apply Continuous.const_smul
simp only [Polynomial.coeff_prod]  -- if this exists
apply continuous_finset_sum
intro S _
apply continuous_finset_prod
intro i _
simp only [Polynomial.coeff_add, Polynomial.coeff_one, Polynomial.coeff_X_mul,
  Polynomial.coeff_C]
apply Continuous.add
· exact continuous_const
· apply Continuous.mul continuous_const
  exact hentry_cont (σ i) i
```

---

## If `Polynomial.coeff_prod` Doesn't Exist

Use the fact that `coeff k` is a `ℝ`-linear map and hence continuous as a map `Polynomial ℝ → ℝ` **if** we give `Polynomial ℝ` the discrete or product topology. But since this doesn't work, the cleanest approach is:

```lean
apply Continuous.const_smul
-- Expand the product explicitly for small n
-- or use that coeff k ∘ prod = sum of products of coefficients
-- which is a polynomial in the entries
induction (Module.finrank ℝ E) with
| zero => simp
| succ n ih =>
  rw [Finset.prod_univ_succ]
  simp only [Polynomial.coeff_mul]
  apply continuous_finset_sum
  intro ⟨j, hj⟩ _
  apply Continuous.mul
  · -- coeff j of first factor
    simp [Polynomial.coeff_add, Polynomial.coeff_X_mul, Polynomial.coeff_C]
    apply Continuous.add continuous_const
    split_ifs <;> [exact hentry_cont _ _, exact continuous_const]
  · -- coeff (k-j) of remaining product
    exact ih _
```

---

## Recommendation

The cleanest solution is to avoid `Polynomial` entirely and directly compute `coeff k` of `∏ i, (cᵢ + X * aᵢ)` as a sum over subsets of size `k`:

$$[X^k] \prod_i (c_i + X \cdot a_i) = \sum_{S \subseteq [n], |S|=k} \prod_{i \in S} a_i \cdot \prod_{i \notin S} c_i$$

This is a polynomial in the `aᵢ`, hence continuous. The Lean proof would use `Polynomial.prod_coeff_eq` or similar. Would you like to pursue this explicit expansion?

Response:
The issue is that `Finset.induction` names the arguments differently. The `hi` is the new element and `ih` is the induction hypothesis. Let me fix the pattern:

```lean
  induction s using Finset.induction with
  | empty =>
    simp [Polynomial.coeff_one]
    exact continuous_const
  | insert ha ih =>
    -- ha : a ∉ s, where a is the new element
    -- ih : Continuous (fun x => (∏ i ∈ s, ...).coeff k)
    rename_i a s' ha
    rw [Finset.prod_insert ha]
    simp only [Polynomial.coeff_mul, Polynomial.finset_sum_coeff]
    apply continuous_finset_sum
    intro ⟨j, hj⟩ _
    apply Continuous.mul
    · simp only [Polynomial.coeff_add, Polynomial.coeff_X_mul, Polynomial.coeff_C,
        Polynomial.coeff_one]
      apply Continuous.add continuous_const
      split_ifs <;> [exact hentry_cont _ _, exact continuous_const]
    · exact ih
```

---

## Why This Fixes It

`Finset.induction` gives:
- `a : Fin n` — the new element being inserted
- `s' : Finset (Fin n)` — the existing set
- `ha : a ∉ s'` — membership proof
- `ih` — induction hypothesis

`Finset.prod_insert ha` then correctly takes `ha : a ∉ s'` as its argument.

## What `rename_i` Does Here

Before `rename_i`, the names are:
- `ha : Fin n` → rename to `elem`
- `ih : Finset (Fin n)` → rename to `s'`  
- `a✝¹ : ha ∉ ih` → rename to `hmem`
- `a✝ : Continuous ...` → rename to `hcont`

So `Finset.prod_insert hmem` now correctly takes the membership proof.

---

## Why `simp_rw` Instead of `rw`

`rw` cannot rewrite under binders (like `fun x => ...`), but `simp_rw` can. Since the product `∏ i ∈ insert ha ih, f i` is inside `fun x => (...)`, `simp_rw [Finset.prod_insert hmem]` correctly rewrites it to `f ha * ∏ i ∈ ih, f i` inside the lambda.

## Why This Works

After `simp only [Polynomial.coeff_mul]`, the goal splits into:

$$\sum_{j_1 + j_2 = k} [X^{j_1}](c + X \cdot a) \cdot [X^{j_2}](\prod_{i \in ih} \ldots)$$

- The first factor `[X^{j_1}](c + X \cdot a)` is either `0`, `1`, or `a_{σ(ha), ha}` depending on `j1` and whether `σ ha = ha`
- The second factor `[X^{j_2}](\prod_{i \in ih} \ldots)` is continuous by `hcont`

---

## Note on `Polynomial.finset_sum_coeff`

The correct name is `Polynomial.finset_sum_coeff` not `Polynomial.finset_sum_coef`. But since `simp_rw [Finset.prod_insert hmem]` followed by `simp only [Polynomial.coeff_mul]` already expanded things correctly via `Finset.antidiagonal`, we don't need it here.

## Fix 1 — `hentry_cont`

`fun_prop` cannot handle `LinearEquiv.trans`. Use the coordinate equivalence directly:

```lean
have hentry_cont : ∀ i j : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E),
    Continuous (fun x => (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)) i j) := by
  intro i j
  have : (fun x => (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)) i j) =
      (fun x => b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b j)) i) := by
    simp [LinearMap.toMatrix_apply, OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis]
  rw [this]
  have : (fun x => b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b j)) i) =
      (fun x => (EuclideanSpace.equiv (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ
        (b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b j)))) i) := by
    simp [EuclideanSpace.equiv]
  rw [this]
  apply Continuous.comp (continuous_apply i)
  apply Continuous.comp b.repr.continuous
  apply ContinuousLinearMap.continuous
  exact (hgcont_diff.continuous_fderiv (by norm_num)).comp continuous_id |>.comp continuous_const
```

## Fix 2 — `hcont j2`

The induction hypothesis `hcont` has type `∀ m, Continuous (fun x => (...).coeff m)` (after generalizing over `m`). So `hcont j2` gives `coeff j2`. But the goal has `(j1, j2).2` which reduces to `j2`. Fix with:

```lean
· have : (j1, j2).2 = j2 := rfl
  rw [this]
  exact hcont j2
```

Or more directly:


## Note on `hP_x_deg`

This requires:

```lean
have hP_x_deg : ∀ x : E, (P_x x).natDegree ≤ n := by
  intro x
  simp only [P_x]
  exact le_trans (Polynomial.natDegree_det_le _)
    (by simp [Matrix.natDegree_map, Polynomial.natDegree_X])
```

If `Polynomial.natDegree_det_le` doesn't exist, use:

Response:
The issue is that the `variable` command comes before the `class` declaration, and the docstring needs to go on the `class` itself. Move the `variable (E) in` modifier and put the docstring directly before `class`:

```lean
variable {E} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E] [FiniteDimensional ℝ E]

/-- Brouwer's fixed point theorem: every continuous map from the closed unit ball
to itself has a fixed point. This is assumed as an axiom and used to prove
the invariance of domain theorem. -/
variable (E) in
class BrouwerFixedPoint : Prop where
  brouwer_fixed_point (f : (closedBall (0 : E) 1) → (closedBall 0 1))
    (hf : Continuous f) : ∃ x, f x = x
```

---

## Why This Works

The `variable (E) in` modifier applies the `variable (E)` scope only to the next declaration. The docstring `/-- ... -/` must appear immediately before the declaration keyword (`class`, `def`, `theorem`, etc.), so it goes between `variable (E) in` and `class`.

lemma A_bound_of_contDiff {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E} (hgcont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g)
    (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ E) :
    let n := Module.finrank ℝ E
    let A : ℝ → E → Matrix (Fin n) (Fin n) ℝ :=
      fun _ x => LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)
    ∃ M : ℝ, 0 ≤ M ∧ ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      ∀ k j : Fin n, ‖A 0 x k j‖ ≤ M := by
  obtain ⟨M, hM0, hM⟩ := fderiv_bound_of_contDiff hgcont_diff
  refine ⟨M, hM0, fun x hx k j => ?_⟩
  simp only [LinearMap.toMatrix_apply, OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis,
    ContinuousLinearMap.coe_coe, OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis_repr_apply]
  have hstep1 : ‖b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)) k‖ ≤
      ‖b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))‖ := by
    change ‖(b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)) :
      PiLp 2 (fun _ : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E) => ℝ)).ofLp k‖ ≤
      ‖(b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)) :
      PiLp 2 (fun _ : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E) => ℝ))‖
    exact PiLp.norm_apply_le _ k
  calc ‖(b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))).ofLp k‖
      ≤ ‖b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))‖ := hstep1
    _ = ‖(fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)‖ := b.repr.norm_map _
    _ ≤ ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ * ‖b.toBasis j‖ := ContinuousLinearMap.le_opNorm _ _
    _ = ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ * 1 := by
        congr 1
        simp [OrthonormalBasis.norm_eq_one]
    _ ≤ M := by
        simp only [mul_one]
        exact hM x hx

## Cleaned Up Version

```lean
lemma A_bound_of_contDiff {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E} (hgcont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g)
    (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ E) :
    ∃ M : ℝ, 0 ≤ M ∧ ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      ∀ k j : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E),
      ‖(LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j‖ ≤ M := by
  obtain ⟨M, hM0, hM⟩ := fderiv_bound_of_contDiff hgcont_diff
  refine ⟨M, hM0, fun x hx k j => ?_⟩
  simp only [LinearMap.toMatrix_apply, OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis,
    ContinuousLinearMap.coe_coe, OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis_repr_apply]
  calc ‖(b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))).ofLp k‖
      ≤ ‖b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j))‖ := by
          change ‖(b.repr ((fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)) :
            PiLp 2 (fun _ : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E) => ℝ)).ofLp k‖ ≤ _
          exact PiLp.norm_apply_le _ k
    _ = ‖(fderiv ℝ g x) (b.toBasis j)‖ := b.repr.norm_map _
    _ ≤ ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ * ‖b.toBasis j‖ := ContinuousLinearMap.le_opNorm _ _
    _ = ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ := by simp [OrthonormalBasis.norm_eq_one]
    _ ≤ M := hM x hx
```

## What Changed

| Before | After |
|---|---|
| `let n` and `let A` in statement | Removed, use `Module.finrank ℝ E` directly |
| `hstep1` as separate `have` | Inlined into `calc` |
| `_ = ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ * 1 := ...` then `_ ≤ M := by simp; exact` | Collapsed to `_ = ‖fderiv ℝ g x‖ := by simp [...]` then `_ ≤ M := hM x hx` |
| `A 0 x k j` | `(LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)) k j` directly |

I want to separate this have statement out into one or more lemmas



Response:
The proof has two natural components:

1. The orthogonality argument — showing `fderiv ℝ f x` maps into `(f x)⊥`
2. The rank argument — concluding `det = 0` from rank deficiency

---

## Lemma 1 — Orthogonality

```lean
lemma fderiv_range_subset_orthogonal {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {f : E → E} (hf_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 f)
    (hf_maps : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1)
    {x : E} (hx : x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) :
    ∀ v : E, fderiv ℝ f x v ∈ (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ := by
  have hfx_norm : ‖f x‖ = 1 :=
    mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mp (hf_maps x (interior_subset hx))
  have hconst_on : ∀ y ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1),
      (fun y => inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f y) (f y)) y = 1 := by
    intro y hy
    have hfy := hf_maps y (interior_subset hy)
    rw [mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm] at hfy
    simp [hfy]
  have hfderiv_inner_zero : fderiv ℝ (fun y => inner (𝕜 := ℝ) (f y) (f y)) x = 0 :=
    HasFDerivAt.fderiv (hasFDerivAt_zero_of_eventually_const (1 : ℝ)
      (Filter.eventually_of_mem (isOpen_interior.mem_nhds hx) hconst_on))
  simp only [inner_self_eq_norm_sq_to_K, RCLike.ofReal_real_eq_id, id_eq] at hfderiv_inner_zero
  rw [fderiv_comp' x (DifferentiableAt.norm_sq ℝ differentiableAt_id)
    (hf_diff.differentiable_one).differentiableAt] at hfderiv_inner_zero
  simp only [fderiv_norm_sq_apply, ContinuousLinearMap.smul_comp] at hfderiv_inner_zero
  have hfderiv_inner_zero' : ((innerSL ℝ) (f x)).comp (fderiv ℝ f x) = 0 := by
    simp only [two_nsmul] at hfderiv_inner_zero
    ext v
    have hv := congr_fun (congr_arg DFunLike.coe hfderiv_inner_zero) v
    simp only [ContinuousLinearMap.add_apply, ContinuousLinearMap.zero_apply] at hv
    rw [add_self_eq_zero] at hv
    exact mem_eqLocus.mp hv
  intro v
  rw [Submodule.mem_orthogonal_singleton_iff_inner_right]
  exact congr_fun (congr_arg DFunLike.coe hfderiv_inner_zero') v
```

---

## Lemma 2 — Det is Zero

```lean
lemma det_fderiv_eq_zero_of_range_subset_orthogonal {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E]
    [InnerProductSpace ℝ E] [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {f : E → E}
    (hf_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 f)
    (hf_maps : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, f x ∈ sphere (0 : E) 1)
    {x : E} (hx : x ∈ interior (closedBall (0 : E) 1)) :
    LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) = 0 := by
  have hfx_norm : ‖f x‖ = 1 :=
    mem_sphere_zero_iff_norm.mp (hf_maps x (interior_subset hx))
  have hfx_ne : f x ≠ 0 := by
    intro h; rw [h, norm_zero] at hfx_norm; linarith
  have hrange := fderiv_range_subset_orthogonal hf_diff hf_maps hx
  have hrange_le : LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) ≤
      (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ := by
    intro w ⟨v, hv⟩
    rw [← hv]
    exact hrange v
  have hdim : Module.finrank ℝ (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ =
      Module.finrank ℝ E - 1 := by
    have hspan := finrank_span_singleton hfx_ne
    have hsum := Submodule.finrank_add_finrank_orthogonal (K := Submodule.span ℝ {f x})
    omega
  have hrank_lt : Module.finrank ℝ (LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E)) <
      Module.finrank ℝ E :=
    calc Module.finrank ℝ (LinearMap.range (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E))
        ≤ Module.finrank ℝ (Submodule.span ℝ {f x})ᗮ :=
            Submodule.finrank_mono hrange_le
      _ = Module.finrank ℝ E - 1 := hdim
      _ < Module.finrank ℝ E := Nat.sub_lt Module.finrank_pos one_pos
  have hnotinj : ¬ Function.Injective (fderiv ℝ f x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) := by
    intro hinj
    linarith [finrank_range_of_inj hinj]
  rw [det_eq_zero_iff_ker_ne_bot, Ne, ker_eq_bot]
  exact hnotinj
```

```lean
  intro x hx
  rw [show f_t 1 = f from by simp [f_t, g]]
  exact det_fderiv_eq_zero_of_range_subset_orthogonal hf_diff hf_maps hx
```

[06/04/2026 09:43:17 +00:00] User:
have hspan := finrank_span_singleton hfx_ne

typeclass instance problem is stuck
  Module ?m.228 E

Note: Lean will not try to resolve this typeclass instance problem because the first and third type arguments to `Module` contain metavariables. These arguments must be fully determined before Lean will try to resolve the typeclass.

needs some annotation like k = R

Response:
```lean
have hspan : Module.finrank ℝ (Submodule.span ℝ {f x}) = 1 :=
  finrank_span_singleton (R := ℝ) hfx_ne
```

---

## Why This Works

`finrank_span_singleton` has signature:

```lean
finrank_span_singleton : v ≠ 0 → finrank R (span R {v}) = 1
```

The `R` argument needs to be specified explicitly since Lean cannot infer it from `hfx_ne : f x ≠ 0` alone — it needs to know which ring to use for the module structure. Providing `(R := ℝ)` fixes the metavariable.

        LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (fun y => y + t • (f y - y)) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) =
        ∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1, |(ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det| := by
      apply MeasureTheory.integral_congr_ae
      apply MeasureTheory.ae_restrict_of_forall_mem measurableSet_closedBall
      intro x hx
      dsimp only
      rw [hderiv_eq_all x, abs_of_pos (hdet_pos x hx)]
    rw [hint_eq, ← hcov]
    rfl

Separate this out into one or more lemmas

Response:
The proof has three natural components:

1. The change of variables (`hcov`)
2. The determinant positivity (`hdet_pos`)
3. Connecting the integral to the volume

---

## Lemma 1 — Determinant Positivity

```lean
lemma det_pos_of_lt_t0 {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E} (hgcont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g)
    {J : ℝ → E → Matrix (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ}
    (hdiag_dom : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < 1 →
      ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      ∀ k : Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E),
      ∑ j ∈ Finset.univ.erase k, ‖J t x k j‖ < ‖J t x k k‖)
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) (htC : t < 1)
    {x : E} (hx : x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1) :
    0 < (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det := by
  have hdet_cont : ContinuousOn
      (fun s => (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det)
      (Set.Icc 0 t) := by
    apply Continuous.continuousOn
    apply ContinuousLinearMap.continuous_det.comp
    fun_prop
  have hdet_ne_zero : ∀ s ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) t,
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det ≠ 0 := by
    intro s ⟨hs0, hst⟩ h
    have hne := det_ne_zero_of_sum_row_lt_diag (hdiag_dom s hs0 (hst.trans_lt htC) x hx)
    apply hne
    rw [LinearMap.det_toMatrix]
    exact_mod_cast h
  have hpos_at_zero : 0 < (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + (0 : ℝ) • fderiv ℝ g x).det := by
    simp only [zero_smul, add_zero]
    have : (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E : E →L[ℝ] E).det =
        LinearMap.det (LinearMap.id : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) := by simp [ContinuousLinearMap.det]
    grind [LinearMap.det_id]
  rcases lt_or_gt_of_ne (hdet_ne_zero t ⟨ht0, le_refl t⟩) with hlt | hgt
  · obtain ⟨s, hs_mem, hs_zero⟩ := intermediate_value_Icc' ht0 hdet_cont
      (Set.mem_Icc.mpr ⟨le_of_lt hlt, le_of_lt hpos_at_zero⟩)
    exact False.elim (hdet_ne_zero s hs_mem hs_zero)
  · exact hgt
```

---

## Lemma 2 — `hI_const`

```lean
lemma I_eq_volume_of_bij {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {f g : E → E} {f_t : ℝ → E → E}
    (hgcont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g)
    (hft_strict_fderiv : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < 1 →
      ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      HasStrictFDerivAt (f_t t)
        (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) x)
    (hft_bij : Set.BijOn (f_t t) (closedBall (0 : E) 1) (closedBall (0 : E) 1))
    (hdet_pos : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      0 < (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det)
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) :
    ∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) =
    (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  have hcov := MeasureTheory.integral_image_eq_integral_abs_det_fderiv_smul volume
    measurableSet_closedBall
    (fun x hx => (hft_strict_fderiv t ht0 (by linarith) x hx).hasFDerivAt.hasFDerivWithinAt)
    hft_bij.injOn (fun _ => (1 : ℝ))
  simp only [hft_bij.image_eq, smul_eq_mul, mul_one, integral_const, MeasurableSet.univ,
    measureReal_restrict_apply, univ_inter] at hcov
  have hderiv_eq_all : ∀ x : E, fderiv ℝ (fun y => y + t • (f y - y)) x =
      ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x :=
    fun x => (hasFDerivAt_interpolation hgcont_diff t x).fderiv
  have hint_eq : ∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) =
      ∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      |(ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det| := by
    apply MeasureTheory.integral_congr_ae
    apply MeasureTheory.ae_restrict_of_forall_mem measurableSet_closedBall
    intro x hx
    dsimp only
    rw [show fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x = fderiv ℝ (fun y => y + t • (f y - y)) x from by congr 1]
    rw [hderiv_eq_all x, abs_of_pos (hdet_pos x hx)]
  rw [hint_eq, ← hcov]
  rfl
```

---

## Then `hI_const` Becomes

```lean
have hI_const : ∀ t : ℝ, 0 ≤ t → t < t0 → t < 1 → t < 1 / C →
    I t = (volume (closedBall (0 : E) 1)).toReal := by
  intro t ht0 htC ht1 ht1C
  simp only [I]
  exact I_eq_volume_of_bij hgcont_diff
    (fun t ht0 _ x hx => hft_strict_fderiv t ht0 htC x hx)
    (hft_bij t ht0 htC ht1 ht1C)
    (fun x hx => det_pos_of_lt_t0 hgcont_diff
      (fun t ht0 htC x hx k => hdiag_dom t ht0 htC x hx k)
      ht0 (htC.trans_le ht0_lt_one) hx)
    ht0
```

```lean
lemma det_pos_of_lt_t0 {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {g : E → E}
    (hdet_ne : ∀ s : ℝ, 0 ≤ s → s < 1 →
      ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det ≠ 0)
    {t : ℝ} (ht0 : 0 ≤ t) (htC : t < 1)
    {x : E} (hx : x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1) :
    0 < (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det := by
  have hdet_cont : ContinuousOn
      (fun s => (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det)
      (Set.Icc 0 t) := by
    apply Continuous.continuousOn
    apply ContinuousLinearMap.continuous_det.comp
    fun_prop
  have hdet_ne_zero : ∀ s ∈ Set.Icc (0 : ℝ) t,
      (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det ≠ 0 :=
    fun s ⟨hs0, hst⟩ => hdet_ne s hs0 (hst.trans_lt htC) x hx

        LinearMap.det (LinearMap.id : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) := by simp [ContinuousLinearMap.det]

```

## Fix the `sorry`

The `sorry` in `hdet_ne_all` is because `hdet` requires `s < t0` but we only have `s < 1`. Since `t0 ≤ 1`, we need `s < t0`. But `s < 1` does not imply `s < t0` in general.

The fix is to change `hdet_ne_all` to use `s < t0` instead of `s < 1`:

```lean

    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det ≠ 0 := by
  intro s hs0 hsC x hx h
  have hne := hdet s hs0 hsC x hx
  apply hne
  simp only [J]
  rw [LinearMap.det_toMatrix]
  exact_mod_cast h
```

```lean
    0 < (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x).det :=
```

```lean
have hdet_ne_all : ∀ s : ℝ, 0 ≤ s → s < t0 →
    ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1,
    (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det ≠ 0 := by
  intro s hs0 hsC x hx h
  -- hdet gives (J s x).det ≠ 0
  -- J s x = toMatrix (id + s • fderiv g x)
  -- ContinuousLinearMap.det = LinearMap.det = Matrix.det ∘ toMatrix
  have hJne := hdet s hs0 hsC x hx
  apply hJne
  simp only [J]
  rw [LinearMap.det_toMatrix]
  -- h : (id + s • fderiv g x).det = 0
  -- need : (toMatrix (id + s • fderiv g x)).det = 0
  have : (ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x).det =
      LinearMap.det (↑(ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + s • fderiv ℝ g x) : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) := rfl
  rw [this] at h
  rw [← LinearMap.det_toMatrix b.toBasis] at h
  exact_mod_cast h
```

## Lemma 1 — Polynomial Representation of Integrand

```lean
lemma det_fderiv_eq_poly_eval {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] {f g : E → E} {f_t : ℝ → E → E}
    (hgcont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g)
    (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ E)
    (hft_def : ∀ t x, fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x =
      ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) :
    let n := Module.finrank ℝ E
    let A : E → Matrix (Fin n) (Fin n) ℝ :=
      fun x => LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)
    let P_x : E → Polynomial ℝ := fun x =>
      Matrix.det (1 + (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) • (A x).map Polynomial.C)
    ∀ x : E, ∀ t : ℝ,
      LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) = (P_x x).eval t := by
  intro n A P_x x t
  rw [hft_def t x]
  rw [show LinearMap.det (↑(ContinuousLinearMap.id ℝ E + t • fderiv ℝ g x) : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) =
      Matrix.det (1 + t • A x) from by
    rw [← LinearMap.det_toMatrix b.toBasis]; congr 1; ext i j
    simp [A, LinearMap.toMatrix_apply, Matrix.one_apply, OrthonormalBasis.coe_toBasis]]
  simp only [P_x, eval_det]
  apply congr_arg Matrix.det; ext i j
  rw [matPolyEquiv_eval]
  simp [Matrix.one_apply]
  split_ifs with hij <;> simp [show Polynomial.eval t (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) = t from by
    simp]
```

## Lemma 2 — `I` is a Polynomial

```lean
lemma I_eq_poly_eval {E : Type*} [NormedAddCommGroup E] [InnerProductSpace ℝ E]
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] [MeasurableSpace E] [BorelSpace E]
    {g : E → E} {f_t : ℝ → E → E}
    (hgcont_diff : ContDiff ℝ 1 g)
    (b : OrthonormalBasis (Fin (Module.finrank ℝ E)) ℝ E)
    (I : ℝ → ℝ) (hI_def : ∀ t, I t = ∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1,
      LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E))
    (hdet_eval : ∀ x : E, ∀ t : ℝ,
      LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) =
      (Matrix.det (1 + (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) •
        (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C)).eval t) :
    let n := Module.finrank ℝ E
    let A : E → Matrix (Fin n) (Fin n) ℝ :=
      fun x => LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)
    let P_x : E → Polynomial ℝ := fun x =>
      Matrix.det (1 + (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) • (A x).map Polynomial.C)
    let P : Polynomial ℝ := ∑ k ∈ Finset.range n.succ,
      Polynomial.monomial k (∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1, (P_x x).coeff k)
    ∀ t : ℝ, I t = P.eval t := by
  intro n A P_x P t
  rw [hI_def]
  simp only [P, Polynomial.eval_finset_sum, Polynomial.eval_monomial]
  conv_rhs => arg 2; ext k; rw [← MeasureTheory.integral_mul_const]
  rw [← MeasureTheory.integral_finset_sum]
  · apply MeasureTheory.integral_congr_ae
    apply MeasureTheory.ae_restrict_of_forall_mem measurableSet_closedBall
    intro x hx
    simp only
    rw [hdet_eval x t]
    rw [Polynomial.eval_eq_sum_range' (n := n.succ)]
    · simp [Polynomial.eval_finset_sum, Polynomial.eval_monomial]
    · exact Nat.lt_succ_of_le (by
        have := Polynomial.natDegree_det_X_add_C_le (A x) 1
        simp only [Fintype.card_fin] at this
        convert this using 2
        simp [A, add_comm])
  · intro k _
    apply MeasureTheory.Integrable.mul_const
    exact (ContinuousOn.integrableOn_compact' (isCompact_closedBall 0 1)
      measurableSet_closedBall
      (continuous_Px_coeff k b hgcont_diff).continuousOn).integrable
```

## Lemma 3 — Polynomial Constant on Interval Implies Constant Everywhere

```lean
lemma poly_const_of_const_on_Ico {t0 : ℝ} (ht0_pos : 0 < t0)
    (I : ℝ → ℝ) (c : ℝ)
    (hI_poly : ∃ P : Polynomial ℝ, ∀ t, I t = P.eval t)
    (hI_const : ∀ t ∈ Set.Ico (0 : ℝ) t0, I t = c) :
    ∀ t : ℝ, I t = c := by
  obtain ⟨P, hP⟩ := hI_poly
  let q : Polynomial ℝ := Polynomial.C c
  have hpq : P = q := by
    apply Polynomial.funext
    intro t
    by_contra hne
    have hne' : P - q ≠ 0 := fun h => hne (by
      have := congr_arg (· + q) h
      simp only [sub_add_cancel, zero_add] at this
      exact congr_arg (Polynomial.eval t) this)
    have hdiff_zero : ∀ t ∈ Set.Ico (0 : ℝ) t0, (P - q).eval t = 0 := by
      intro t ht
      simp [hP t, hI_const t ht, q]
    exact (Set.Ico_infinite ht0_pos).mono
      (fun t ht => hdiff_zero t ht)
      (Polynomial.finite_setOf_isRoot hne')
  intro t
  simp [hP t, hpq, q]
```

## Why `linarith` Instead of `convert`

`Polynomial.natDegree_det_X_add_C_le` gives a `≤` bound on the degree, but the exact form may involve extra `map Polynomial.C` applications. Rather than trying to unify the expressions with `convert`, use `linarith` to close the numeric inequality directly from `this`.

[06/04/2026 11:41:49 +00:00] User:

        1).det.natDegree ≤
  Module.finrank ℝ E
⊢ (1 + Polynomial.X • ((toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis) ↑(fderiv ℝ g x)).map ⇑Polynomial.C).det.natDegree ≤ n

Response:
The issue is that `this` has a double `map Polynomial.C` and the order is different (`X • M + 1` vs `1 + X • M`). We need to show the two expressions are equal:

```lean
· apply Nat.lt_succ_of_le
  have hmap : ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C).map
      Polynomial.C = (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C := by
    ext i j
    simp [Polynomial.map_C]
  have hcomm : (1 : Matrix (Fin n) (Fin n) (Polynomial ℝ)) +
      (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) • (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis
        (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C =
      (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) • ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis
        (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C).map Polynomial.C + 1 := by
    rw [hmap]
    ring
  have := Polynomial.natDegree_det_X_add_C_le
    ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C) 1
  simp only [Fintype.card_fin, map_zero, Polynomial.C_1, Matrix.map_one] at this
  rwa [show (1 + (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) •
      (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C).det.natDegree =
      ((Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) • ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis
        (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C).map Polynomial.C + 1).det.natDegree from by
    congr 1; rw [hmap]; ring]
```

## Or More Simply

Just use `add_comm` and `hmap` to rewrite before applying the lemma:

```lean
· apply Nat.lt_succ_of_le
  have hmap : ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C).map
      Polynomial.C = (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C := by
    ext i j; simp [Polynomial.map_C]
  calc (1 + (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) •
        (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C).det.natDegree
      = ((Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) • ((LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis
          (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C).map Polynomial.C + 1).det.natDegree := by
          congr 1; rw [hmap]; ring
    _ ≤ Module.finrank ℝ E := by
          have := Polynomial.natDegree_det_X_add_C_le
```

```lean
    [FiniteDimensional ℝ E] [MeasurableSpace E] [BorelSpace E]
    {g : E → E} {f_t : ℝ → E → E}

      LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E))
    (hdet_eval : ∀ x ∈ closedBall (0 : E) 1, ∀ t : ℝ,
      LinearMap.det (fderiv ℝ (f_t t) x : E →ₗ[ℝ] E) =
      (Matrix.det (1 + (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) •
        (LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)).map Polynomial.C)).eval t) :

      fun x => LinearMap.toMatrix b.toBasis b.toBasis (fderiv ℝ g x)
    let P_x : E → Polynomial ℝ := fun x =>
      Matrix.det (1 + (Polynomial.X : Polynomial ℝ) • (A x).map Polynomial.C)
    let P : Polynomial ℝ := ∑ k ∈ Finset.range n.succ,
      Polynomial.monomial k (∫ x in closedBall (0 : E) 1, (P_x x).coeff k)
    ∀ t : ℝ, I t = P.eval t := by
  intro n A P_x P t
  -- Degree bound
  have hP_x_deg : ∀ x : E, (P_x x).natDegree ≤ n := by
    intro x
    have := Polynomial.natDegree_det_X_add_C_le (A x) 1
    simp only [Fintype.card_fin] at this
    convert this using 2
    simp [A, add_comm]
  rw [hI_def]
  simp only [P, Polynomial.eval_finset_sum, Polynomial.eval_monomial]
  conv_rhs => arg 2; ext k; rw [← MeasureTheory.integral_mul_const]
  rw [← MeasureTheory.integral_finset_sum]
  · apply MeasureTheory.integral_congr_ae
    apply MeasureTheory.ae_restrict_of_forall_mem measurableSet_closedBall
    intro x hx
    simp only
    rw [hdet_eval x hx t, Polynomial.eval_eq_sum_range' (n := n.succ)]
    exact Nat.lt_succ_of_le (hP_x_deg x)
  · intro k _
    apply MeasureTheory.Integrable.mul_const
    exact (ContinuousOn.integrableOn_compact' (isCompact_closedBall 0 1)
      measurableSet_closedBall
      (continuous_Px_coeff k b hgcont_diff).continuousOn).integrable
```

---

## Why This Is Cleaner

- `hP_x_deg` is proved inside using `Polynomial.natDegree_det_X_add_C_le` on `A x` directly
- `continuous_Px_coeff` is called directly since it is a standalone lemma
- The `convert this using 2` handles the `add_comm` difference between `1 + X • M` and `X • M + 1`
- The structure matches the original closely
